1001 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


City of Lubbock v. Corbin


NO. 07-94-0080-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


942 S.W.2d 14; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1786



April 30, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 137TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 90-531,690; HONORABLE CECIL G. PURYEAR, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART, AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Lubbock challenged a judgment from the 137th Judicial District Court of Lubbock County (Texas), denying an injunction to enforce a housing commission order against appellees property owners and awarding damages to appellees for their counterclaim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Appellant City of Lubbock sought review of a judgment in an action in which appellant was denied an injunction to enforce a housing commission's order against appellees property owners, and in which appellees had been awarded damages for their counterclaim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court affirmed the portion of the judgment denying an injunction, finding that appellant had not demonstrated an entitlement to the injunction. In reversing the portion of the judgment which awarded damages, the reviewing court found that a building inspector did not possess the requisite final policymaking authority necessary to find appellant liable for his actions under § 1983. The court rejected the claim of an alleged violation of substantive due process rights, finding no deprivation of a property right. The court rejected the equal protection claim, finding that the building code contemplated governance of specified situations and therefore the housing commission's action taken pursuant to the code against appellees was not unreasonable. Moreover, appellees had failed to exhaust their administrative appeals of the housing commission's order finding their house substandard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the judgment awarding appellee property owners damages, finding no violations of appellees' equal protection or substantive due process rights. The court affirmed the portion of the judgment denying appellant City of Lubbock an injunction to enforce the housing commission's order because appellant failed to prove an entitlement to an injunction.

 

1002 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


McElhaney v. City of Tyler


NO. 12-94-00183-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


926 S.W.2d 597; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2054



April 30, 1996, delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied November 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 2. SMITH COUNTY, TEXAS. ROGERS, RANDALL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee's wife challenged the decision of the County Court at Law No. 2, Smith County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee employer, in a workers' compensation case arising under the Texas Workers' Compensation Act of 1989 after the death of appellant's husband, who was an employee of appellee, under Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 401.011(12).


OVERVIEW: In appellant employee's wife's workers' compensation case arising under the Texas Workers' Compensation Act of 1989, the lower court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee employer. Appellant sought review, arguing that the lower court erred in granting summary judgment because genuine issues of fact existed regarding whether appellee waived its right to contest the compensability of appellant's husband's death by failing to timely deliver a form contesting the compensability to the Texas Workers' Compensation Commission. The court reversed and remanded, finding that the evidence did not establish that appellee was entitled to summary judgment as a matter of law on the issue of whether the contest form was timely delivered. Moreover, appellee was not entitled to judgment as a matter of law that appellant's husband did not receive an injury, under Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 401.011(12), in the course of his employment with appellee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee employer, finding that genuine issues of fact existed regarding whether appellee waived its right to contest the compensability of appellant's husband's death by failing to timely deliver a form contesting the compensability.

United Church of Christ Found. v. Harris County Appraisal Dist.


NO. 01-95-00807-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1507



April 18, 1996, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 234th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-50719.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant church foundation challenged an order of the 234th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee county on the issue of whether appellant was exempt from paying property taxes on a low-income housing complex.


OVERVIEW: Appellant church foundation was a charitable, nonprofit organization that was tax-exempt under 26 U.S.C.S. 501(c)(3) (1988). Appellant owned and operated a low-cost housing complex that was exempt from city and county taxes from 1973 to 1983. Appellant challenged appellee county's revocation of its tax-exempt status and challenged the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee on the issue. The court held that the language in appellant's trust agreement permitting it to make charitable contributions to other organizations did not satisfy the requirement of Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.18(f)(1), which required appellant's assets to be pledged to its charitable functions and did not permit the assets to be pledged to or used by another organization.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee county on the basis that appellant church foundation's charter was not in strict compliance with the tax code.

 

1004 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Lohmuller v. State


No. 10-95-308-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


921 S.W.2d 457; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1496



April 17, 1996, delivered  
April 17, 1996, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Court at Law. Ellis County, Texas. Trial Court # 93-11238-CR.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of his conviction by the County Court at Law, Ellis County, Texas, for driving with a suspended license in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h (1996), claiming that he was denied a speedy trial, that the information was insufficient to charge him with the crime, that he conclusively established a defense to the charge, and that he was denied due process.


OVERVIEW: When appellant driver was stopped by police for not wearing a seat belt, a check of his driver's license revealed that it was under a suspension order resulting from an unpaid judgment from a 1991 accident. Appellant challenged his conviction under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h, § 32(c)(1)(A) (1996) for driving a motor vehicle while his license to drive was suspended. The appeals court held that appellant failed to preserve for review his denial of a speedy trial claim. Appellant failed to attack the information at trial on the grounds asserted on appeal, thereby waiving any defects in the information. The existence of a liability insurance policy at the time of appellant's 1991 accident did not provide a defense under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701h, § 1D (1996) to the charge of driving with a suspended license. Finally, appellant's ex post facto claim was meritless where his license suspension order was based on a court judgment, which was entitled to a presumption of regularity. However, the court reversed and remanded sua sponte, based on the trial court's error in failing to give a required "reasonable doubt" definitional jury instruction.


OUTCOME: The court found no merit to appellant's points of error on appeal, but reversed his conviction for driving with a suspended license and remanded sua sponte, based on the trial court's error in failing to give a "reasonable doubt" definitional instruction to the jury.

 

1005 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Purnell v. State


NO. 01-95-01302-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


921 S.W.2d 432; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1385



April 11, 1996, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 14. Harris County, Texas. County Court Cause No. 5079. JIM BARKLEY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the County Criminal Court at Law Number 14 of Harris County (Texas), that affirmed his conviction of violating a sign ordinance under Houston Building Code § 4605(a). Defendant contended that the ordinance was vague, overbroad, and a prior restraint on freedom of speech.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction under Houston Building Code § 4605(a) for violating a sign ordinance was affirmed by the county court and defendant appealed. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that the sign ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The court found that the ordinance clearly established that the sign usage proscribed was for advertising, and thus, the ordinance was not vague. The court concluded that the ordinance was not overbroad because it focused on advertising signs that were installed on a firm support and did not reach a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct. The court determined that the reason for the ordinance was to promote highway safety and beautification. Because this governmental interest was substantial and the regulations were drawn narrowly to achieve this interest, the court ruled that the ordinance was not a prior restraint on freedom of speech. The court found that although the ordinance did not specify a culpable mental state, a mandatory presumption of guilt was not created because the complaint against defendant and the jury charge included a culpable mental state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of violating a sign ordinance because the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague, overbroad, or a prior restraint on freedom of speech.

 

1006 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re S.A.R.


Appeal No. 04-95-00040-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


931 S.W.2d 585; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1358



April 10, 1996, Delivered  
April 10, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appeal from the 289th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 94-JUV-0693. Honorable Carmen Kelsey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the 298th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which certified defendant, a child, to stand trial as an adult for capital murder and attempted capital murder. In her appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting at the certification hearing certain statements she made without having received the warnings required pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 51.09(b) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, certified to stand trial as an adult, sought review of the certification order on the grounds that statements she made while in custody were inadmissible at the waiver and certification hearing because she had not been given the warnings required by Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 51.09(b) (1996). The court reversed the order and remanded to the trial court. In reversing, the court found that § 51.09(b) was a mandatory evidentiary rule making inadmissible any statements obtained from a child not given the statutory warnings by a magistrate after the latter had examined the child independently and ascertained that the child had knowingly waived his or her rights. The court found that the only warnings given defendant were provided by a sheriff's deputy and therefore the statements she made were inadmissible in any future proceeding. The court rejected the state's argument that § 51.09(b) warnings were not required because the child was not in custody. The facts showed that the child was taken to the police station, finger printed, photographed, and interrogated and that those circumstances would lead the child to believe her liberty had been curtailed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the waiver and certification order that defendant be tried as an adult and remanded to the trial court, because the statements made by the child defendant while in custody were inadmissible because they were obtained without her having been provided the required statutory warnings by a magistrate.

Duran v. Furr's Supermarkets


No. 08-95-00169-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


921 S.W.2d 778; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1345



April 4, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied March 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 34th District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 92-12971). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Herbert E. Marsh, Jr., Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant customer sought review of a summary judgment from the 34th District Court of El Paso County (Texas) in favor of appellees, supermarket and security officer, arising from appellant's claim for damages for negligent hiring and supervision, assault and battery, false imprisonment and defamation of character.


OVERVIEW: Appellant customer brought claims for negligent hiring and supervision, assault and battery, false imprisonment, and defamation of character against appellees, supermarket and security officer, out of an incident that arose between herself and the security officer in the supermarket's parking lot over the improper parking of a vehicle in which she was a passenger. The court reversed and remanded the summary judgment for appellees, sustaining appellant's two points of error that the trial court had not only incorrectly granted summary judgment for the supermarket but also incorrectly granted summary judgment on qualified immunity for the security officer. On each of appellant's claims, the court found that appellees' proof at trial for their motion's numerous supporting arguments was inadequate to demonstrate no material issues of fact and thus to sustain summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment for appellees supermarket and security officer and remanded for trial on appellant's claims alleging negligent hiring and supervision, assault and battery, false imprisonment and defamation of character. The court found error in granting summary judgment because appellees' proof at trial on each alleged ground was inadequate to demonstrate that there were no genuine issues of material fact.

 

1008 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Central Power & Light Co. v. Sharp


NO. 03-95-00093-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


919 S.W.2d 485; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1323



April 3, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 1, 1996. Released for Publication May 1, 1996. Application for Writ of Error Denied March 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-2800, HONORABLE JERRY DELLANA, JUDGE PRESIDING.

This Opinion Substituted on Motion for Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of December 6, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3066.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility sought review of the summary judgment rendered in favor of appellee comptroller in the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District (Texas), on a motion for rehearing regarding appellee's interpretation of provisions within the Franchise Tax Act, Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 171.001(a), 171.109(b) (1992), that governed the computation of a company's surplus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant utility was required to capitalize the imputed cost of funds, known as Allowance for Funds Used During Construction (AFUDC)-equity, used to build a new power plant. Appellant was required to report and pay an annual franchise tax, based on taxable capital, pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 171.001 (1995). Appellant sought a refund of the difference between its tax as reported and paid, and its tax as it would have been computed without capitalizing its AFUDC-equity, a difference of approximately $ 3,000,000. Appellee comptroller denied the request for a refund, maintaining that generally accepted accounting principles reflected in Financial Accounting Standard 71 required appellant to capitalize its AFUDC-equity and then to depreciate it over the life of the structure. The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment because the tax classification assailed by appellant did not run afoul of Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1, which required equal and uniform taxation, and only recognized the fact that non-regulated enterprises do not enjoy a high probability that a return will be realized on their AFUDC-equity, unlike the return guaranteed to regulated companies through rates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the difference in value between regulated and non-regulated enterprises provided more than sufficient justification for the disparate treatment of Allowance for Funds Used During Construction-equity, that the disparate tax treatment did not violate the Texas Constitution, and that appellee's adoption of the franchise tax rule fell within its delegated authority.

General Dynamics Corp. v. Sharp


NO. 03-95-00341-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


919 S.W.2d 861; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1291



April 3, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 8, 1996. Released for Publication May 8, 1996. Application for Writ of Error Denied September 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO.92-11498, HONORABLE W. JEANNE MEURER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged the decision of the District Court of Travis County, 353rd Judicial District (Texas), which granted summary judgment for appellee comptroller in a tax-protest suit under Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 112.051-112.060 (1992 & Supp. 1996).


OVERVIEW: Appellee corporation objected to the amount of the franchise tax imposed by appellee comptroller. Appellant had contracted with the United States military to manufacture fighter jets, which were periodically delivered to a military base in Texas. For federal income tax purposes, the company used the completed contract method, under which it realized the income upon completion of the contract. Appellant protested imposition of a franchise tax in 1991 under Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 112.051-112.060 (1992 & Supp. 1996), based on the full amount reflected in the contract. The district court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment, and the court affirmed on appeal. The franchise tax formula did not violate the commerce and due process clauses of the United States Constitution, nor the due course of law provision of the Texas Constitution. The single-factor formula used by Texas did not create a grossly excessive disparity in comparison with a three-factor formula used by most other states. Further, when the state adopted the tax, the legislation was prospective, so it did not impair any vested rights of appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling that the imposition of a franchise tax on appellant corporation by appellee comptroller was valid, as the statutory formula for calculating the tax was not shown to be unconstitutional.

White v. Liberty Eylau Indep. Sch. Dist.


No. 06-95-00057-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


920 S.W.2d 809; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1282


March 26, 1996, Argued  
April 2, 1996, Decided  
April 2, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing of Application for Writ of Error Overruled November 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 202nd Judicial District Court. Bowie County, Texas. Trial Court No. D 202 CV 920168.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured sought review of the take-nothing judgment entered by the 202nd Judicial District Court of Bowie County (Texas) following a jury trial in appellants' personal injury suit against appellee school district.


OVERVIEW: Appellant injureds' car was struck by a school bus. The driver was employed by the county transportation department and was also a teacher with appellee school district. Appellants sued the driver, the county transportation department, and appellee. Appellants settled with the driver and the county transportation department. At trial on remand, the jury found that the driver was not acting as appellee's employee at the time of the accident, thereby absolving appellee of liability for appellants' injuries. Appellants sought review. Appellants challenged the lower court's definition of "employee" in the jury instructions. The court noted that the challenged sentence was take verbatim from Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.001 and was a correct statement of the law. The court found that the lower court erred in submitting the jury instruction concerning dual office holding under an interlocal contract. However, the court held that the error was not reversible error. Moreover, the jury's failure to find that the driver was appellee's employee at the time of the accident was not so against the weight and preponderance of the evidence as to be unjust.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the take-nothing judgment of the lower court after overruling all of appellants' points of error except one. The court concluded that the lower court erred in submitting the jury instruction concerning dual office holding under an interlocal contract; however, the court found that this was not reversible error.

 

1011 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re D.S.


NUMBER 13-94-498-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


921 S.W.2d 383; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1237



March 28, 1996, delivered  
March 28, 1996, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order from the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas transferring him from the custody of the Texas Youth Commission into the custody of the Institutional Division of the Texas Department of Criminal Justice to complete his sentence for murder. Appellant claimed that the transfer or release hearing under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.11 (Pamph. 1996) violated his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: When appellant was 14, he was adjudicated delinquent for having committed murder and was sentenced to 30 years commitment to the Texas Youth Commission (TYC). Later, at appellant's release or transfer hearing appellant was transferred to the custody of the Institutional Division of the Texas Department of Criminal Justice to serve the remainder of his sentence. On appeal, the court held that although, under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 51.13(a), appellant's adjudication of delinquency did not subject him to all the disabilities of a conviction, he had the same rights as an adult offender under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 51.10, 54.03(c), (f), 54.04(a) (1986 & Pamph. 1996) to counsel, a jury, etc. at the time of his adjudication. Thus, he was not being incarcerated without having been convicted. Because the hearing did not determine appellant's guilt but determined if appellant should be released from confinement, the trial court properly considered the post-adjudication TYC reports and other factors permitted by Tex. Fam. Code §§ 54.11(d), (k) (Pamph. 1996), and disclosed them to appellant's attorney as required by § 54.11(d) (Pamph. 1996). Therefore, the court affirmed the order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order transferring appellant from the Texas Youth Commission's custody into the custody of the Institutional Division of the Texas Department of Criminal Justice. The court held that because appellant had been adjudicated delinquent for murder at a hearing where his due process rights were protected, his constitutional rights were not violated at the release or transfer hearing where post adjudication evidence was admitted.

 

1012 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Tillman v. State


NO. 2-94-437-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


919 S.W.2d 836; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1258



March 28, 1996, Decided  
March 28, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 3, 1996. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 9, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 3 OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. DON LEONARD.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Criminal District Court No. Three of Tarrant County (Texas) that adjudicated him guilty of sexual assault of a child following his trial for violations of his deferred adjudication probation. Appellant claimed that his sentence was vindictive, and that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12 § 5(b) that precluded a right to appeal violated his due process rights under the Texas constitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to sexual assault of a child and was placed on deferred adjudication probation. Appellee state filed a motion for adjudication because of appellant's probation violation. Appellant pled true, but was granted a new trial where he pled not true to the violations. After the trial, the trial court found that the violations occurred, adjudicated him guilty of sexual assault of a child, and sentenced him to a longer term than upon his true plea. On appeal, the court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b) (Supp. 1996), which prohibited appeals from adjudications of guilt, did not violate appellant's due process rights under the Texas constitution because there was no right to appeal a criminal conviction in the Texas constitution. The court held that because appellant did not obtain the trial court's permission to appeal its failure to advise him of deportation penalties under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13(a)(4) (1989), the court was precluded by Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1) from reviewing that issue, and that because the longer sentence was assessed after a full trial, it was not vindictive. Thus, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment adjudicating appellant guilty of sexual assault of a child after his trial for violations of his deferred adjudication probation. The court held that no right to appeal a criminal conviction existed in Texas constitution, thus the statute prohibiting appeal was constitutional, and the sentence was not vindictive because the trial court had more facts after trial than on the hearing on appellant's vacated true plea.

State v. Whiteley


No. 05-94-01212-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1268



March 27, 1996, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 292nd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F92-19956-V.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the prosecution in a criminal case, challenged a judgment from the 292nd Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which granted appellee's motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with delivery of cocaine. Appellee filed a pretrial motion to suppress evidence, asserting that the evidence in the case was obtained as a result of illegal police conduct. The trial court granted appellee's motion to suppress, finding that police officers obtained evidence while performing an undercover investigation outside their jurisdiction. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it granted appellee's motion to suppress. Although the police officers had authority to investigate suspected criminal activity, the court determined that the officers were not authorized to conduct investigations outside of their county. The court stated that the fact that officers could have made a citizen's arrest was not relevant because the officers did not make such arrest. Instead, the officers purchased narcotics from appellee. Additionally, the officers could not have made a citizen's arrest in their capacity as police officers. The court concluded that because the officers' conduct was unlawful, suppression was warranted. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that granted appellee's motion to suppress was affirmed because police officers improperly obtained evidence against appellee by conducting an investigation of him outside of their jurisdiction.

 

1014 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Slaughter v. State


NO. 09-94-135 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2858


September 15, 1995, Submitted  
March 27, 1996, Delivered  
March 27, 1996, FILED


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 252nd District Court. Jefferson County, Texas. Cause No. 57957.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 252nd District Court (Texas), that convicted him of aggravated kidnapping on the grounds that it was error to allow an in-court identification, to admit evidence of an extrajudicial offense, and to fail to grant his motion for a mistrial due to the conduct of the state during jury argument.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated kidnapping. He sought review arguing that it was error to admit the in-court identification and evidence of an extrajudicial offense, and that his motion for a mistrial should have been granted. The court found that the identification procedures were not unnecessarily suggestive merely because appellant was the only individual wearing a particular jacket. The court agreed that it was error to admit evidence of an extrajudicial offense finding that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 3(a) prohibited evidence regarding an offense committed prior to September 1, 1993 in a noncapital case. Because the alleged extraneous offense was nearly identical to the subject offense and the state frequently mentioned the extraneous offense, the court was unable to say beyond a reasonable doubt that the evidence made no contribution to appellant's punishment. The court found that the state's jury arguments were reasonable deductions from the evidence, or that any error was cured by the instruction to disregard. The court affirmed the conviction, but reversed the punishment and remanded for a hearing on the punishment phrase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, but reversed the judgment with respect to the punishment phase of the trial and remand the case for a new punishment hearing only finding that it was error to admit evidence of appellant's extrajudicial offense, but that the in-court identification was permissible, and that the jury arguments were not improper so it was not error to deny appellant's motion for a mistrial.

 

1015 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Gibson v. State


No. 08-95-00148-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


921 S.W.2d 747; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1147



March 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied November 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 168th District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 78106). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Jack Ferguson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of an order from the 168th District Court of El Paso County (Texas), which denied him habeas corpus relief in his suit against appellee state to stop searches of his belongings and persons upon entry of the county courthouse under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 2.01, 11, 14, and 15 (1996), U.S. Const. amend IV, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 9.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney's requested habeas corpus relief in his suit against appellee state, seeking to stop the search of his person and his belongings by x-ray machines upon his entry of the county courthouse, was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the restraint was lawful. The court held appellee was the appropriate party, as appellant's proceeding under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 11 was a criminal proceeding subject to Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. art. 2.01 (1996). The court held appellant proved he was under restraint at the time he filed his application. Although appellant failed to establish he lacked an adequate remedy, good cause existed for the court to hear the appeal. The courthouse searches did not constitute arrests subject to Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 14 and 15 as appellant was free to walk away from the search. His consent was qualified, rather than non-existent. The searches were permissible under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 9, as they were reasonable, brief, not intrusive and appellee had a legitimate interest in providing security at the courthouse.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of habeas corpus relief to appellant attorney in his suit against appellee state to stop searches of his belongings and persons upon entry of the county courthouse. The searches did not constitute arrests and therefore only required qualified consent to be done without a warrant. The searches did not violate the Fourth Amendment of the U. S. Constitution or equivalent provisions of the Texas constitution.

 

1016 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Sims v. Adoption Alliance


Appeal No. 04-95-00745-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


922 S.W.2d 213; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1099



March 20, 1996, Delivered  
March 20, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appeal from the 131st District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 95-PA-01112. Honorable Martha Tanner, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a judgment from the 131st District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which terminated her parental rights and ordered that appellee adoption agency be appointed managing conservator of her child.


OVERVIEW: When appellant became pregnant, she decided that she did not want to keep the child. Appellant contacted potential adoptive parents and arrangements were lawfully made through appellee adoption agency. Appellant signed the affidavit of voluntary relinquishment twenty-six hours after the child's birth. Some time after appellant signed the affidavit, she changed her mind. Appellant then filed her answer opposing the termination of her rights. The trial court upheld the termination of appellant's parental rights and denied appellant's motion for habeas corpus. On appeal, the court held that a forty-eight hour waiting period was applicable to appellant's voluntary termination of her parental rights. The court rejected appellee's arguments that the legislature never intended for the forty-eight hour waiting period to apply retroactively. The court found that the language of the effective date of the applicable statute made the extended waiting period retroactive. The court also held that the waiting period was not unconstitutionally retroactive because appellee did not have a vested right to the possessory conservatorship of the child. Judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that terminated appellant's parental rights was reversed because an extended waiting period applied to appellant's voluntary termination of her rights and she changed her mind about terminating her rights within that period.

Behbahani v. State


Appeal Nos. 04-94-00621-CR, 04-94-00622-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1103



March 20, 1996, Delivered  
March 20, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 283rd District Court of Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Nos. F94-02203-LT and F94-02202-LT. Honorable Jack Hampton, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 283rd District Court of Dallas County (Texas), which convicted appellant of felony theft. Appellant asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the indictment under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a),(b)(3) (1994) for appropriation of property in the custody of any law enforcement agency. Appellant asserted that the statute violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex Const. art I, § 19.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.03(a), (b)(3) (1994), which provided that a person committed a felony theft offense if the person appropriated property in the custody of any law enforcement agency and the property was explicitly represented by any law enforcement agent to the person as being stolen. Appellant filed a pretrial motion to quash the indictments. The trial court denied appellant's pretrial motion to quash the indictments alleging that § 37.03(a), (b)(3) violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex Const. art. I § 19. Following the trial court's denial of appellant's motion, appellant entered a plea of nolo contendere and was found guilty as charged and placed on probation. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the statute was not vague because persons of common intelligence did not have to guess at its meaning and differ about its application, and the statute provided sufficient notice to law enforcement personnel to prevent arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement. The court further held that due process was not violated when a defendant was predisposed to commit an offense, and a rational basis existed for the legislature's actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment convicted appellant of felony theft convictions, holding that the Texas statute on appropriation of property was not unconstitutionally vague under the due process clause of the state or federal constitutions.

Williams v. State


No. 01-95-01278-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1042



March 14, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 184th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 702674.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the 184th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which denied appellant's pretrial petition for writ of habeas corpus after appellant was charged by two indictments under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.11 for impersonating a peace officer.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was charged by two indictments under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 37.11 (1994) for impersonating a peace officer, he petitioned the trial court for a writ of habeas corpus. Appellant contended that § 37.11 violated his free speech rights under U.S. Const. amend. I and Tex. Const. art. I, § 8, because only speech or acts protected as speech were contained as allegations in the indictments. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the petition for writ of habeas corpus, holding that impersonating a peace officer was not freedom of expression protected by U.S. Const. amend. I or Tex. Const. art. I, § 8 when a third party was threatened or coerced. The court also affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's request to make a bill of exceptions in connection with the denial of the motion to quash the indictment. The court held that the trial court was not entitled to preview the evidence in order to decide whether to quash an indictment, and that an indictment that tracked the language of the statute was legally sufficient to mandate a trial on the merits.


OUTCOME: Denial of writ of habeas corpus by the trial court was affirmed, because impersonating a peace officer was not speech protected by either the federal or state constitutions when a third party was threatened or coerced.

Burger v. State


No. 01-95-00214-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


920 S.W.2d 433; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1058



March 14, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 618032. Jim Barr, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 337th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of indecency with a child after a hearing on the state's motion to adjudicate guilt.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's indecency with a child conviction because appellant's no contest plea and his stipulation to the testimony of the state's witnesses was sufficient evidence to support a finding of guilt. The court found that appellant could not appeal the trial court's determination to adjudicate guilt because Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b) specifically prohibited an appeal from that determination. The court held that denial of the right to appeal did not create a suspect class or infringe on a fundamental right because there was no constitutional right to any appellate review. Having found that there was no fundamental right involved, the court then held that the denial of the right to appeal did not violate equal protection under the law because it was rationally related to the state's interest in preserving judicial and prosecutorial resources.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for indecency with a child because his no contest plea and his stipulation to the testimony of the state's witnesses constituted sufficient evidence of his guilt to support a verdict against him.

Lane v. State


No. 01-94-00891-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1060



March 14, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 339th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9405281.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 339th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which adjudicated appellant guilty of burglary of a building.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found appellant guilty of burglary of a building. Appellant sought review of the judgment, challenging the constitutionality of his trial to the court and the sufficiency of the evidence. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court held that appellant was not denied his right to compulsory process nor was it fundamental error for the trial court to have conducted a bench trial under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15. While appellant waived his right to a jury trial, appellant presented a defense, testified, and cross-examined the state's witnesses. The court held that the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to support his burglary conviction. Appellant admitted he entered the garage at night without the owner's permission. When the police found appellant inside the garage, the lock on the garage had been broken and the owner's property removed. The evidence was legally sufficient to support the conviction. Thus, the evidence showed that appellant entered the garage with the intent to commit theft.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which adjudicated appellant guilty of burglary of a building. The court held that appellant was not denied his right to compulsory process by the trial court's having conducted a bench trial because appellant presented a defense, testified, and cross-examined the state's witnesses. The court also held that the evidence was factually and legally sufficient to support appellant's conviction.

Convalescent Servs. v. Schultz


No. 14-94-01198-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


921 S.W.2d 731; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1071



March 14, 1996, Rendered  
March 14, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied January 10, 1997. Application for Writ of Error Overruled September 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 295th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-16766. Downey, Dan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nursing home challenged the judgment entered in the 295th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which found appellant was guilty of gross negligence in its care of a resident and awarded appellee family, as next of friend for the resident, punitive damages in the amount of $ 850,000.


OVERVIEW: Appellee family, acting as next of friend of a resident of appellant nursing home, filed suit against appellant alleging negligence and gross negligence in its care for the resident. A jury found in favor of appellee and awarded appellee $ 380,000 in damages and $ 850,000 in punitive damages. Appellant challenged the finding of gross negligence and the punitive damages award. The court held that the evidence was legally sufficient to support the jury's finding that appellant was guilty of gross negligence within the definition of the landmark opinion of the state. Specifically, appellant's knowing violation of its own policies, its failure to comply with the Nurse Practice Act, its apparent falsification of records, and disregard for doctor's orders constituted more than a scintilla of evidence of its conscious disregard for the risk of serious harm to the resident. The court further held that the trial court's failure to conduct a hearing on appellant's post-verdict motions or to articulate its findings did not deprive appellant of due process because adequate post-verdict review of punitive damages was available at the appellate level. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding appellant nursing home was guilty of gross negligence in its care for a resident and awarding appellee family, as next of friend for the resident, punitive damages because the evidence was legally sufficient to support the finding, and appellant was not denied due process.

Texas Medical Liab. Trust v. Garza


NUMBER 13-95-516-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


918 S.W.2d 632; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1135



March 14, 1996, delivered  
March 14, 1996, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 138th District Court - Cameron.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator insurer sought a writ of mandamus to set aside the order entered in the District Court of Cameron County, 138th Judicial District (Texas), which sustained the state's objection to indemnifying relator under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 110.002-.003 (1996) pursuant to a medical malpractice settlement between the insured and the claimant.


OVERVIEW: Relator insurer settled a medical malpractice suit filed against its insured by a claimant. Pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § §110.002-.003, relator requested indemnification from the state, and the state refused. Relator filed suit. The trial court sustained the state's objection, and relator sought a writ of mandamus to set aside the order. The state claimed that the statute did not apply because the claimant's action accrued prior to its effective date. The court held that the statute was governed by the Medical Liability Act, which contained an absolute two-year limitation period. Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1996). However, Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, precluded the application of the strict accrual date because it was impossible for claimant to discover his injury within that time. The court applied the discovery rule and held that the action accrued after the indemnification statute's effective date. Relator qualified for indemnification, and the settlement amount governed the indemnity amount. The court conditionally granted mandamus directing the trial court to vacate its order and to render an order directing the state to indemnify relator.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally granted relator insurer a writ of mandamus directing the trial court to vacate its order and to render an order approving the settlement and directing the state to make the required indemnity payment because the claimant's action accrued after the indemnification statute's effective date. Therefore, the statute applied.

Burkhalter v. Texas State Bd. of Medical Examiners


NO. 03-95-00328-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


918 S.W.2d 1; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1014



March 13, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126Th JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 485,096, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician challenged an order of the District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District (Texas), which dismissed his action for review of appellee Texas State Board of Medical Examiners' denial of his application for reinstatement of his medical license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant physician was convicted of attempted murder, and appellee Texas State Board of Medical Examiners revoked his license to practice medicine. After appellant was released from prison, appellee denied four applications to reinstate appellant's license. Following the denial of his last application, appellant brought an action to set aside the original revocation of his license, or in the alternative, to declare that the version of the Medical Practice Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4495b, § 4.10, in effect at the time his license was revoked was unconstitutional because it made no provision for judicial review of a denial of reinstatement by appellee. The trial court dismissed the action for lack of jurisdiction. On review, the court affirmed because there was no right to judicial review of an administrative decision in the absence of a statutory provision authorizing such review, and the right to practice medicine was a privilege rather than a fundamental right which required judicial intervention in the administrative process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that dismissed appellant physician's action for judicial review of appellee Texas State Board of Medical Examiners' denial of his application for reinstatement of his medical license because there was no statutory authorization for judicial review of appellee's decision.

Daussin v. Texas Commerce Bank Nat'l Ass'n


Appeal No. 04-95-00132-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1037



March 13, 1996, Delivered  
March 13, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied April 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 270th District Court of Harris County. Trial Court No. 93-36396. Honorable Susan Soussan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant niece sought review of a judgment from the 270th District Court, Harris County (Texas), determining that decedent's will excluded her as a descendant and finding in favor of appellee college as beneficiary under decedent's will.


OVERVIEW: Decedent's will created a testamentary trust naming two of his sisters-in-law as beneficiaries that would terminate upon the beneficiaries' death and pass to their descendants. If there were no descendants, the trust property would pass to appellee college. Both beneficiaries survived decedent; however, one beneficiary adopted appellant niece as an adult after decedent died. Appellant sought review after the lower court excluded her as a descendant under the testamentary trust provisions. The court found that the testator's intent was paramount, construed by the laws in effect at the time of the testator's death. Under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 46a, § 9 (repealed), in effect at decedent's death, an adopted child was not entitled to property conveyed to the natural child of the adoptive parent unless the intent to include was indicated by additional language or circumstances. As an attorney, decedent was presumed to understand the effect of the law at the time he wrote the will. Further, adoption of adults was not recognized in Texas until after his death. Because the will unambiguously did not include adopted children as descendants, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment that appellant niece, as an adopted child, was not descendant of decedent and was not entitled to a share of a testamentary trust created to benefit his descendants was affirmed. Decedent did not included adopted children as descendants as required by statute in effect at the time he wrote his will. The law also did not recognize adult adoptees. Defendant's intent was construed to exclude appellant as a descendant.

Saed Esfahai Moaiedi v. State


No. 01-94-01097-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 907



March 7, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 655283.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the 185th District Court, Harris County (Texas), that was obtained after appellant entered a plea of guilty to the offense of the possession of opium with intent to deliver, and the resultant sentence of 15 years' confinement and a fine. Appellant contended that his sentence was excessive, and that it was error for the judge to review a presentence report prior to finding him guilty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction in the trial court upon his plea of guilt to the offense of the possession of opium with intent to deliver, and the resultant sentence of 15 years' confinement and a fine, and asserted that his sentence violated the constitutional prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment and that appellant's conviction was void because the trial court reviewed a presentence report prior to an adjudication of guilt. The court affirmed and found that pursuant to Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 481.102(3)(A), 481.112(f) (Supp. 1996), appellant was subject to a punishment of life imprisonment or any term from 15 to 99 years, and a fine. The court found that appellant's sentence fell well within the statutory range and did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. The court held that although a trial judge should not examine a presentence report prior to the adjudication of guilt pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, 9(c)(1) (Supp. 1996), because appellant pled guilty to the charge prior to the trial court's examination of the report, the trial court could not be influenced by it.


OUTCOME: A conviction for possession of opium and sentence was affirmed because the sentence was well within statutory range so it was not excessive or cruel and unusual punishment, and because although the trial court read a presentence report prior to adjudication of appellant convict's guilt, appellant had pled guilty prior to the report, and the court found that the trial judge was not be influenced.

Roberts v. State


No. 01-95-00844-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 962



March 7, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 174th District Court Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause No. 556750.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order, entered in 174th District Court, Harris County (Texas), revoking his probation and adjudicating guilt for a burglary of a habitation, on the grounds that the trial court erred because of a fatal variance and insufficient evidence. Appellant also challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a trial court order, revoking probation and adjudicating guilt on the grounds that the trial court erred due to fatal variance and insufficient evidence. Appellant also challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b) (1996). Appellant pleaded guilty without an agreed recommendation to the offense of burglary of a habitation. Appellant also pleaded true to enhancement for a prior aggravated assault conviction. The trial court placed appellant on 10 years' deferred adjudication with community supervision. A judgment of guilt on the charged offense was rendered, which revoked appellant's community supervision, and gave him a 20-year sentence. On appeal, the court declined to address points of error regarding the adjudication of guilt, because a defendant could not appeal a court's decision to adjudicate guilt. Based on precedent, the court held that art. 42.12, § 5(b) did not violate appellant's equal protection rights. The court also found that art. 42.12, § 5(b) did not infringe on jurisdiction of the courts, as the legislature could impose restrictions on a right of appeal and regulations regarding appellate jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of appellant's probation and sentence, and declined to address points of error regarding the trial court's alleged error in adjudicating guilt, holding that a court's decision to adjudicate guilt was not appealable. Based on precedent, the court held that the procedural rule did not violate appellant's equal protection rights, and that it did not infringe on the court's jurisdiction.

Atkins v. State


No. 14-93-00300-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


919 S.W.2d 770; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 984



March 7, 1996, Rendered  
March 7, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 339th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 639953. Walker, George Hon., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of conviction from the 339th District Court, Harris County (Texas) of possession of a controlled substance. Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.115(b) (1992). Appellant alleged, inter alia, the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence of the cocaine and denying his Batson challenge. Appellant challenged constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 14.03(a)(4), the statute he was arrested under.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of conviction of possession of a controlled substance. Appellant alleged the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence because cocaine was obtained in a search incident to an illegal arrest. The appellate court concluded that in reviewing a warrantless arrest, whether probable cause existed was determined by applying the totality of the circumstances test. Searches incident to an arrest were not limited to those made at the instant a suspect was taken into police custody. When booked into a detention facility, a suspect may be searched without a warrant. The arrest and the search were lawful, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion to suppress the cocaine When reviewing the trial court's determination of a Batson challenge, the appellate court applied the clear error standard of review, which required deference to the trial court's finding on the prosecution's discriminatory intent. Nevertheless, the appellate court determined whether the decision of the trial court was clearly erroneous by looking at the record, including voir dire, racial makeup of the venire, and the prosecution's explanations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in appeal from conviction of possession of a controlled substance. The appellate court concluded that the trial court did not err in denying appellant's motion to suppress evidence because the cocaine was obtained in a search incident to a lawful arrest. Further, the trial court did not err in denying appellant's Batson challenge, and appellant's challenge to the constitutionality of Texas statute did not stand.

Turner v. Texas Dep't of Mental Health & Mental Retardation


NO. 03-95-00277-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


920 S.W.2d 415; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 941



March 6, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled May 1, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1705. Released for Publication May 1, 1996. Application for Writ of Error Denied October 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-9223, HONORABLE PAUL DAVIS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, who had been detained in a mental health facility against his will, sought review of summary judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District, Texas, of his complaint for deprivation of privacy, negligence and intentional infliction of emotional distress against appellees, mental health department and the state.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had been detained in a mental health facility against his will and brought suit against the mental health department and the state asserting a number of causes of actions. Prior to bringing suit, he had filed an action in federal court alleging the detention had violated his federal constitutional rights, which action was dismissed. The appellees sought summary judgment in the subsequent state court action, based on statute of limitations, which was granted. The court affirmed and held that Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.064 did not toll the statute of limitations while appellant's suit was pending in federal court. Appellees, on summary judgment had to show that either the federal court case had been dismissed for want of jurisdiction, or that the two causes of action were not the same. The court held that although the federal court case had been dismissed for want of jurisdiction, the two causes of action were not the same, since appellant could not have claimed federal constitutional rights' violations in state court and had not added his state court causes of action to his federal court case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because the statute of limitations for bringing complaint for deprivation of privacy, negligence, and intentional infliction of emotional distress had not been tolled during the time appellant's federal case was pending.

City of Garland v. Kaliney

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS

NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment and permanent injunction entered by the 134th Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which declared void and enjoined enforcement of certain zoning ordinances which appellee permit holder had held, relative to private beverage clubs which were inconsistent with Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 32.

The trial court granted the injunction and declared the specific use permits void. The court reversed and rendered judgment that neither appellant nor appellee take anything by their claims. The court held that appellant could not challenge the constitutionality of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 32 after it had availed itself of its benefits. The court further held that appellee could not challenge the specific use permit's regulatory provisions as he had availed himself of its benefits until his permit was suspended.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and held that neither party should take anything by their claims, as they had both benefitted from the regulations they were now challenging.

Clarke v. State


NO. 2-94-250-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 815

NOTICE:   [*1] PUBLISHED IN PART


PRIOR HISTORY: TRIAL COURT: 158TH DISTRICT COURT. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. PHILLIP VICK. COUNTY: DENTON COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the 158th District Court, Denton County (Texas), that convicted him of aggravated sexual assault, asserting that his speedy trial right was violated and that he should have been granted a change of venue.


OVERVIEW: After a retrial, defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault. Defendant appealed. The prosecution conceded that the delay in defendant's retrial was long enough to be presumed prejudicial, and failed to provide a valid reason for the delay. Defendant established that his defense was impaired by the delay because by the time his trial was held, other convictions had been entered against him that were considered by the jury; the prosecution thus failed to prove defendant suffered no prejudice by the delay. Despite this evidence, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that defendant's speedy trial right was not violated as there was proof that defendant did not immediately request a speedy trial, and requested dismissal rather than an accelerated trial. The court rejected defendant's claim that he was entitled to a change of venue based on the prosecution's failure to timely file counter-affidavits because the prosecution was not required to file the affidavits seven days before the hearing on the motion under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.01 (1989). Defendant's conviction was therefore affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of aggravated sexual assault was affirmed because the trial court properly applied a balancing test and did not abuse its discretion in finding defendant's speedy trial right was not violated. Further, defendant was not entitled to a change of venue as there were no time requirements with respect to the prosecution's counter-affidavits.

Childs v. State


Appeal No. 04-95-00016-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 772



February 28, 1996, Delivered  
February 28, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 144th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 94-CR-5160. Honorable Susan D. Reed, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 144th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, appellant was convicted of murder and sentenced to life imprisonment. Appellant challenged his conviction, claiming that the trial court erred by charging the jury with respect to parole law during the punishment phase of his trial. Because appellant's objection to the charge on appeal differed from that at trial, the court reviewed the claim as an unobjected-to error. Thus, although the trial court's misstatement that appellant, for good behavior, could earn time off his sentence was error as Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4a (1996) referred to time off the period of incarceration, the court held that appellant failed to demonstrate actual egregious harm as a result of the misstatement. In so ruling, the court noted that there was no indication that the jury was influenced by the charge. The court held that the grand jury indictment did not violate Tex. Const. art. I, § 10, because no additional investigation could have determined the exact manner or means of the victim's death. The court also held that the evidence was legally sufficient to support the conviction, which the court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for murder, because he did not demonstrate egregious harm as a result of the trial court's misstatement on parole law, the grand jury could not have determined through additional investigation the exact manner or means of the victim's death, and the evidence was legally sufficient to support the conviction.

Bowles v. Clipp


No. 05-94-01832-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


920 S.W.2d 752; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 689



February 22, 1996, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' and Appellees' Rehearing Denied April 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 193rd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-10531-L.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered in Part, Remanded in Part, Affirmed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, sheriff and county, challenged the judgment of the 193rd Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which found that the collection of bail bond approval fees violated the Texas Constitution, held appellants liable for actual damages and interest to appellee class of payors under a four-year statute of limitations, and assessed a penalty against appellant sheriff under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art 3909 (repealed 1993).


OVERVIEW: The trial court awarded appellee class of payors actual damages based on a four-year statute of limitations with prejudgment interest and a statutory penalty as damages against appellants, sheriff and county, for the unauthorized collection of pre-conviction bail bond approval fees. On review sought by appellants, the court affirmed the portion of the order awarding actual damages because appellants were liable jointly and severally for a refund of the collected amount of unauthorized fees. Appellants were not entitled to legislative or governmental immunity, because the taking for the purpose of providing services affecting the public interest was incident to a public use under Tex. Const. art I, § 17. The court reversed the portion of the order that applied a four-year statute of limitations because the two-year period for a taking of personal property should have been used. The court remanded for a recalculation of the prejudgment interest based on the two-year statute of limitations. The court also reversed the portion of the order that assessed a penalty against appellant sheriff under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 3909 (repealed 1993).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's order that awarded actual damages to appellee class of payors for the unauthorized collection of pre-conviction bail bond approval fees by appellants, sheriff and county. The court reversed the portion of the order that assessed a penalty against appellant sheriff. The court also reversed and remanded the portion of the order that calculated damages under a four-year statute of limitations.

GENERAL TIRE, INC. v. KEPPLE


No. 14-94-01166-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


914 S.W.2d 444; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 706



February 22, 1996, Rendered  
February 22, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled and Dissenting Opinion on Motion for Rehearing March 28, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 1202.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 151st Judicial District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-040828. Garcia, Carolyn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tire manufacturer challenged an order of the 151st Judicial District Court, Harris County, Texas, which denied appellant's request, pursuant to Tex. R. Civ. P. 76a, to seal documents presented during discovery in a manufacturing defect action filed by appellee tire owners.


OVERVIEW: Appellee tire owners alleged injuries caused by a defect in appellant tire manufacturer's tires which contributed to vehicle rollover. After the trial court dismissed the suit, it granted appellees' motion for relief from a protective order and denied appellant's motion to seal. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed, because the trial court did not abuse its discretion in applying Tex. R. Civ. P. 76a to appellant's request for limited protection of court records rather than Tex. R. Civ. Appellant failed to rebut the presumption of openness with evidence of its interest in protecting its trade secrets. The court found that the notice of a rule 76a hearing was sufficient to confer jurisdiction over court records produced during an earlier suit with a different plaintiff who was represented by appellees' counsel. The court held that the terms of rule 76a were fairly limited and not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying appellant tire manufacturer's motion to seal documents because the trial court did not abuse its discretion where appellee tire owners, presented sufficient evidence that the documents were court records and appellant failed to rebut the presumption of openness.

Johnson v. Blackhurst


No. 14-92-00387-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 713



February 22, 1996, Rendered  
February 22, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 278th District Court. Walker County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 17,773-C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the dismissal of his pro se in forma pauperis action by the 278th District Court, Walker County (Texas). Appellant brought suit against appellee correctional officer, alleging that appellee negligently or recklessly damaged appellant's watch. The trial court ruled that appellant's cause was frivolous and dismissed with prejudice pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code § 13.001(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate brought suit against appellee correctional officer, alleging that appellee negligently or recklessly damaged appellant's watch during a search of his cell while he was at work. The court held that the trial court used the appropriate standard in determining whether to dismiss appellant's in forma pauperis complaint under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code § 13.001(b)(2) which was whether the claim had no arguable basis in law or fact. In affirming the trial judge, the court ruled that from the face of appellant's petition, the trial court could have found the presence of the elements of the official immunity duty defense: performance of a discretionary duty, action within the scope of authority, and good faith. The court also ruled that appellant waived his constitutional challenge to Tex. Civ. Prac. Rem. Code § 13.001 because he did not properly raise the challenge in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial judge. The court held that the lower court used the appropriate standard and ruled that appellant's claim should have been dismissed because it had no arguable basis in law or fact. Because the trial court could have found from the face of appellant inmate's petition that appellee correctional officer was entitled to official immunity, there was no abuse of discretion in dismissing the complaint.

Allen v. Tolon


No. 11-95-269-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


918 S.W.2d 605; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 722



February 22, 1996, Decided  
February 22, 1996, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 129th District Court of Harris County.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient and wife sought review of decision by the 129th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted appellee doctor's motion for summary judgment dismissing the malpractice claim against him because it was barred by the statute of limitations in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (1996).


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient and wife claimed that appellee doctor negligently failed to diagnose cancer when appellant patient was examined by the doctor for rectal bleeding. Appellants claimed that the negligence was the proximate cause of damages that would have been prevented if the doctor had made a proper diagnosis or referral. The trial court granted summary judgment dismissing the case because appellee examined the patient on only one occasion in May 1991. Appellants' first lawyer sent a notice of claim to appellee in August 1992, but the lawsuit was not filed until July 1994, more than three years after the examination. On appeal, the court affirmed. Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (1996), provides a two year statute of limitations for medical malpractice actions and excludes such cases from the Deceptive Trade Practices-Consumer Protection Act, Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 17.41 et seq. (1996). In addition, there was no evidence of fraudulent concealment in the record that might have tolled the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because the summary judgment proof established that the action was filed more than three years after the examination which was the basis of the claim and the statute of limitations for medical malpractice is two years. Since there was no evidence of fraud and the law precluded a deceptive trade action the action was time barred.
