Solis v. State


Appeal No. 04-94-00660-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 670



February 21, 1996, Delivered  
February 21, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Motion for Discretionary Review Refused as Untimely Filed July 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 144th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 94-CR-3068. Honorable Phil Chavarria, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 144th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which found him guilty of murder and sentenced him to 18 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for murder, found guilty, and sentenced to 18 years imprisonment. Appellant claimed the trial court erred at the punishment phase in not allowing him to describe his girlfriend's personality traits and the events precipitating the assault on his girlfriend a few days prior to the murder. The court overruled appellant holding that there was not sufficient evidence in the record to indicate that appellant's assault on his girlfriend had any bearing on the murder. Appellant complained that the trial court wrongfully instructed the jury that good behavior could reduce the time of his sentence rather than his period of incarceration. The court held that appellant did not properly object to the charge nor did he suffer any egregious harm. The court further held that since appellant was tried for this offense after the effective reenactment of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, which allowed such an instruction to be given to the jury, the parole instruction was constitutional. The court found that the jury was not unduly swayed by the parole charge because appellant's sentence was only three years more than the minimum punishment of imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the 18-year sentence concluding that there was not sufficient evidence in the record to show that appellant's assault on his girlfriend had any bearing on the murder. The court held that appellant did not properly object to the jury instruction that good behavior could reduce the time of his sentence, nor did he suffer egregious harm since such an instruction was constitutional.

R. Civ. P. 13. The appeal arose out of appellee's successful suit for breach and anticipatory repudiation of an alimony contract and subsequent motion for an ex parte temporary turnover order.

Houston v. State


No. 14-93-00406-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


916 S.W.2d 705; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 597



February 15, 1996, Rendered  
February 15, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 185th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 640247. Walker, Jr. Carl Hon., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 185th District Court, Harris County (Texas), that denied his motion to quash enhancement paragraphs in his indictment, convicted him of burglary of a habitation under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02 (1989), and assessed punishment, enhanced by two prior convictions, at 25 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to burglary of a habitation, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.02 (1989). The trial court assessed punishment, enhanced by two prior convictions, at 25 years in prison. Challenging the decision, appellant contended the trial court erred by denying his motion to quash the enhancement paragraphs in his indictment. Prior to the burglary offense he was convicted of criminal mischief and of burglary of a building. Appellant argued that his prior conviction for criminal mischief was void because the indictment failed to include a necessary mens rea and the indictment was void because the underlying statute was unconstitutionally vague. Reviewing the record, the court found that the criminal mischief statute did not include a separate mens rea. Appellant had signed a written waiver of his constitutional rights in open court, while represented by counsel, in accordance with Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 1.15 . The waiver specifically referred to the underlying statute so that any ambiguity was cleared. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the trial court did not err by overruling appellant's motion to quash the enhancement paragraphs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied appellant's motion to quash enhancement paragraphs in his indictment, convicted him of burglary of a habitation, and assessed punishment at 25 years in prison because the prior convictions were neither void nor tainted by a constitutional defect.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 268th District Court, Fort Bend County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault of a child.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child because there was no clear and convincing evidence that the victim's in-court identification of appellant was tainted by her pre-trial identification when the victim was able to see appellant during the commission of the crime, her description of appellant was accurate, she was positive of her identification, and she identified appellant's photograph and a tattoo on him within days of the crime. Texas State Bd. of Medical Examiners v. Burzynski


NO. 03-95-00222-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


917 S.W.2d 365; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 495



February 7, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 3, 1996. Released for Publication April 3, 1996. As Corrected May 8, 1996. Application for Writ of Error Denied September 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 94-12915, HONORABLE PAUL DAVIS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from Travis County, 353rd Judicial District (Texas), which reversed, under the Texas Medical Practice Act (TMPA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4495b, § 509(a), appellant's suspension of appellee's license to practice medicine.


OVERVIEW: Appellee prescribed federally unapproved drugs to patients. Appellant suspended appellee's license to practice medicine, and appellee sought the trial court's review. The trial court reversed, and appellant sought the court's review asserting the trial court erred in finding that the Texas Medical Practice Act (TMPA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4495b, § 5.09(a), authorized appellee's use of the drugs, and erred in holding the false advertising statute, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 431.183(a)(2) (1992), unconstitutional. The court held that § 509 authorized doctors to dispense drugs only when urgent necessity precluded resort to a pharmacy, and did not authorize distribution of drugs not approved by the Federal Drug Administration. Further, where appellee's assertion that § 431.183(a)(2) was unconstitutional was based upon appellant's finding that appellee's brochures constituted false advertising, because appellee was involved in an illegal activity, his brochures were not entitled to protection under U.S. Const. amend. I. Therefore, appellee failed to show an injury, and the trial court erred in ruling on appellee's constitutional challenge. Judgment reversed.


OUTCOME: Judgment in appellee's favor reversed where the trial court erred in finding statutory support for appellee's act of dispensing drugs which were not federally approved to patients, and where it improperly ruled on appellee's constitutional challenge to a false advertising statute as appellee had failed to show an injury under that statute.

Tidrow v. State


NO. 2-94-236-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


916 S.W.2d 623; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 363



February 1, 1996, Decided  
February 1, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 16TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. JOHN NARSUTIS.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from an order of the 16th District Court of Denton County (Texas) which convicted him of capital murder.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of capital murder. During the trial, the trial court admitted, over appellant's objection, the written statements to the police by two co-defendants which were consistent with appellant's statement, which had been previously admitted. Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in admitting those statements, arguing that they were inadmissible hearsay. Appellant also argued that the evidence against him was insufficient to corroborate the promise of remuneration and that a photo entered into evidence and shown to the jury was overly prejudicial. On review, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the statements were admissible as an exception to hearsay, as they were self-inculpatory and against the declarants' penal interest that a reasonable person in the declarants' position would not have made the statement unless believing it to be true and that appellee State provided evidence of corroborating circumstances sufficiently convincing to clearly indicate the trustworthiness of said statements. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to establish remuneration and that the photo was relevant and not overly prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, holding that statements to police made by co-defendants were admissible as statements against interest and that appellee State had presented evidence which supported the truthfulness of those statements. The court also held that there was sufficient evidence to establish remuneration was behind the murder and that a photo entered into evidence was relevant and not overly prejudicial.

Fiore v. HCA Health Servs.


NO. 2-95-063-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


915 S.W.2d 233; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 413



February 1, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 29, 1996. Application for Writ of Error Denied November 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 348th DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. MARYELLEN HICKS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, patient and husband, sought review of the summary judgment granted by the 348th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) in favor of appellee health care providers because appellants' claims were barred by the statute of limitations. Appellants argued that the trial court erred in summarily dismissing their lawsuit because the open courts provision, Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, saved their claims.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient was treated by appellee health care providers seven years before she sued them for a misdiagnosis. Appellant husband sued on derivative claims. Appellants had learned of the misdiagnosis six years after the treatment by appellees. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellees because appellants' claims were barred by the two-year statute of limitations imposed by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. Art. 4590i, § 10.01. On appeal, the court held that, under the statute of limitations, the lawsuit was barred. Under the open courts provision, Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, they had a reasonable time after they learned of the misdiagnosis to bring their lawsuit even though it was past the limitations period because it was inherently impossible for them to file suit before they learned of the misdiagnosis. The reasonable time was not equivalent to another limitations period. Without explanation for the delay, they failed to sue for more than a year after learning of the misdiagnosis. As a matter of law they did not bring their lawsuit within a reasonable time and, therefore, were not entitled to relief from the open courts provision. Summary judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment entered by the trial court in favor of appellee health care providers for a misdiagnosis which occurred more than seven years before the lawsuit was filed. The lawsuit was barred by the statute of limitations, and appellants, patient and husband, were not entitled to relief under the open courts provision because they failed to file suit within a reasonable time after learning of the misdiagnosis.

Gerry Tanner & Co. v. Kroger Co.


No. 01-95-00594-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 404



January 29, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 190th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-14016.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company and financial corporation sought review of a decision by the 190th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which dismissed appellants' lawsuit against appellee company. Appellee filed a special appearance, and the trial court sustained appellee's challenge to its jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a company and a financial corporation, sought review of the trial court's dismissal of their suit against appellee company. Appellee had filed a special appearance, and the trial court had sustained appellee's challenge to its jurisdiction. On appeal, appellants argued that the trial court committed error in granting appellee's special appearance and dismissing their claims. Appellants contended that appellee invoked the court's jurisdiction by calling a witness to testify and by seeking findings of fact concerning the merits of the case. Appellees also argued that certain of the trial court's findings of fact were improper as relating to the merits of the case. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that exercise of jurisdiction over appellee did not offend traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice and that the trial court could properly assert general jurisdiction over appellee. The court also held that appellee did not waive its special appearance by offering testimony at the special appearance hearing and that no determination of any issue of fact in connection with the objection to jurisdiction was a determination of the merits of the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which dismissed appellant company and financial corporation's lawsuit. The court held that the trial court erred in sustaining appellee's challenge to its jurisdiction. The court remanded the case for trial on the merits.

Keith v. State


NO. 07-95-0137-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


916 S.W.2d 602; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 322



January 26, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 69TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF MOORE COUNTY; NO. 2624; HONORABLE RON ENNS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REFORMED AND AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for the offenses of indecency with a child by contact and aggravated sexual assault from the 69th Judicial District Court of Moore County (Texas), and the imposition of certain conditions of community supervision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of indecency with a child by contact and aggravated sexual assault. The court affirmed the judgments but reformed them by deleting certain conditions of community supervision. Defendant contended that state failed to disclose exculpatory evidence which would have demonstrated inconsistencies in victims' statements. The court reviewed sealed records and found that they did not include exculpatory evidence. The failure of the trial court to release other records to defendant in order to impeach a witness or find exculpatory evidence was harmless error because the records were consistent with the witness' trial testimony and cumulative. The trial court erred in requiring defendant to not contest extradition to Texas and requiring defendant to pay the victim's therapy and medical costs, but because state conceded these points, the court did not address the merits. The trial court erred in requiring defendant to contribute to a counseling fund because it was not authorized by law, and in requiring that defendant pay a fine within 10 days because the trial court never made an inquiry into defendant's ability to pay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed conviction of defendant for the offenses of indecency with a child by contact and aggravated sexual assault but reformed to eliminate certain conditions of community supervision. The trial court's refusal to release records to defendant was harmless error because the records did not contain exculpatory evidence, and they were consistent with trial testimony and cumulative.

Duron v. State


No. 01-94-01238-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


915 S.W.2d 920; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 232

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defendant sought review of his conviction in the 232nd District Court, Harris County, Texas, of indecency with a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant defendant was convicted of the offense of indecency with a child upon pleading guilty without an agreed recommendation and sought review. Appellant claimed that the indictment was fundamentally defective for failing to allege the statutory elements of the offense of indecency with a child. Appellant also contended that the indictment was defective for failing to allege a culpable mental state as to all elements of the charged offense and that this defect rendered his plea invalid and deprived him of due process of law and due course of law under U.S. Const. amend 14 and Tex. OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant defendant's conviction of indecency with a child. Appellant waived any alleged errors objections alleged defects in the substance of the indictment by failing to object to these defects prior to trial. Also, the indictment was not defective for failing to allege that appellant knew his victim's age when he committed the charged offense.

Smith v. Smith


No. 01-95-00252-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 243



January 25, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law. Waller County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-11-12,471.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mother and biological father, sought review of the judgment of the County Court at Law, Waller County (Texas), which granted appellee presumed father sole managing conservatorship of the minor child. Appellants claimed it was error to strike appellant mother's amended petition, to award conservatorship of the child to appellee, and to strike appellant biological father's intervention.


OVERVIEW: After appellant mother filed for divorce she became aware that her husband, appellee presumed father, was not the biological father of her minor child. She amended her divorce complaint and appellant biological father filed an intervention in the action seeking to show his paternity of the child. The trial court struck the amended pleading and the intervention and granted a continuance. After the trial court awarded appellee sole managing conservatorship of the child, appellants sought review. As soon as appellant biological father suspected that he might be the father, he acknowledged responsibility for the child's care and maintenance and made serious and continuous efforts to establish a relationship with the child. The court found that this was sufficient to give appellant biological father standing to file a paternity suit, and that the trial court abused its discretion in striking his intervention. The court found that although appellee would have been surprised by the amended pleadings, there was no showing that the continuance did not cure the surprise. The court reversed the order granting appellee conservatorship of the minor child and remanded for a new hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded a paternity and divorce case for a new hearing, finding that although an amended pleading would have been a surprise to appellee presumed father, it should not have been stricken without a showing that the continuance would not have cured the surprise. Additionally, it was an abuse of discretion to strike appellant biological father's intervention because he had established that he had standing to intervene.

Harris County Appraisal Dist. v. Herrin


No. 14-94-00408-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


917 S.W.2d 345; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 313



January 25, 1996, Rendered  
January 25, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 125th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-41645. O'Neill, Eileen, Judge.

Original Opinion of August 17, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1899.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, tax appraiser and appraisal review board, challenged the decision of the 125th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which held that the prepayment or forfeiture provision of Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08(b) (1992) was unconstitutional as applied to appellee taxpayers.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, tax appraiser and appraisal review board, appraised nine parcels of property owned by appellee taxpayers. Appellants received a protest from appellees in return, arguing that the property valuations were too high under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 41.44(a) (1992). Appellants lowered the appraised value on the properties, but the values were still not as low as appellees claimed they should have been, and appellees brought a suit for de novo review, without paying the taxes. Although Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08 required forfeiture of the claim in this circumstance, the trial court rendered judgment for appellees. Appellants challenged this decision. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that § 42.08 clearly created a financial barrier to access to the courts by requiring that a taxpayer pay the appropriate amount of taxes before the delinquency date or forfeit the right to obtain a final determination from the reviewing court. Because of this the court held that § 42.08 violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, the open courts provision. The court found that there were less drastic alternatives available to appellants that would ensure taxpayer compliance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's review and revaluation of appellee taxpayers' property appraisal because a statute clearly created a financial barrier to access to the courts by requiring that a taxpayer pay the appropriate amount of taxes before the delinquency date or forfeit the right to obtain a final determination from the reviewing court, so that the statute violated the open courts provision of the Texas Constitution.

Draheim v. State


Appeal No. 04-94-00039-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


916 S.W.2d 593; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 220



January 24, 1996, Delivered  
January 24, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused August 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 226th Judicial District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 93-CR-5189. Honorable Sid L. Harle, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction of aggravated sexual assault and indecency with a child in the 226th Judicial Court of Bexar County (Texas) He claimed that the trial court erred in admitting and excluding certain evidence at his sentencing. He claimed fundamental error arising out of the state's references to hardships endured by the jury, the state, and the state's witnesses as a result of his exercising his right to trial by jury.


OVERVIEW: After appellant pleaded guilty to aggravated sexual assault and indecency with a child, he was sentenced to prison. The court affirmed the trial court, holding that it did not err in refusing to permit appellant to cross-examine the victim's mother about other sexual offenses against the victim by other perpetrators in order to show that the victim's emotional problems were not caused exclusively by appellant's conduct. The court reasoned that some of the testimony was inadmissible hearsay and that some of it was excluded by the trial judge, acting within his discretion, as irrelevant. The court also held that the trial court did not err in admitting the videotape appellant made of his offense, holding that the tape was prejudicial but not unfairly prejudicial and that the trial judge acted within his discretion in admitting it. The court found neither error nor egregious harm in the state's references to hardships on the jury, the state and the state's witnesses. The court held that they were not directed at appellant's exercise of his right to a jury trial but that they recognized the painful nature of the case for all and sought to meet appellant's closing argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that judgment of the trial court, holding that the trial court did not err in excluding certain evidence at appellant's sentencing, because some of it was hearsay and some of it was irrelevant. It did not err in admitting a videotape, because the tape was not unfairly prejudicial. The state's references to hardships were not directed at appellant's exercise of his right to trial by jury and did not cause fundamental error.

University of Texas v. Ables


NO. 03-95-00077-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


914 S.W.2d 712; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 244



January 24, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 92-11497, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Rendered in Part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed a judgment of the District Court of Travis County (Texas), which awarded plaintiff employees compensatory damages for sex and age discrimination, declaratory relief, and attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employees' positions were abolished when defendant employer reorganized. Claiming a right to continued employment and that the reorganization was only a pretext for discharging them because of their age or sex, plaintiffs brought an action against defendant to recover compensatory damages for discrimination, declaratory relief, and attorney's fees. The trial court awarded compensatory damages to one plaintiff, declaratory relief to one plaintiff for deprivation of property without due process of law, and attorney's fees to all plaintiffs. On appeal, the court affirmed the award of compensatory damages to one plaintiff and reversed as to another plaintiff, holding that the trial court erred as a matter of law in awarding one plaintiff declaratory relief for deprivation of property without due process of law because the evidence did not show that she was deprived of a property interest. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of compensatory damages for discrimination to one plaintiff. It reversed the award of declaratory relief to one plaintiff for deprivation of property without due process of law, because she was not deprived of a property interest, and rendered that she take nothing. It held that the trial judge abused his discretion in awarding plaintiffs' attorney's fees and rendered a judgment that plaintiffs take nothing.

Soderman v. State


No. 14-95-00233-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


915 S.W.2d 605; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 173

January 18, 1996, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Court at Law No. 3. Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 79,736. James Blackstock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the County Court at Law No. 3, Brazoria County (Texas), which convicted him for unlawful carrying of a weapon.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for unlawful carrying of a weapon. The court found that the prosecution against appellant did not have to be dismissed with prejudice under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01 because that provision did not apply to county courts. The court also determined that appellant waived his complaint that the trial judge was biased because appellant failed to file a timely motion for recusal. The court concluded that appellant was not entitled to a jury charge instruction on the defense of traveling because appellant was not in the course of travel when he was apprehended and that the exception in the statute for traveling was not so unclear as to be void. The court found no basis to conclude that the mere failure of a police officer and a justice of the peace to submit written statements, when the oaths of office themselves have been taken, rendered the oaths invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against appellant for unlawful carrying of a weapon. The prosecution against appellant did not have to be dismissed with prejudice under a statute because that statute did not apply to county courts. Appellant was not entitled to a jury charge instruction on the defense of traveling and the statutory exception to the offense for traveling was not so unclear as to be void.

Arnold v. State


No. 01-95-00633-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


920 S.W.2d 704; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 201



January 18, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 22, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law Number Seven. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9521473. SHELLY P. HANCOCK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the denial of his application for writ of habeas corpus from the County Criminal Court at Law Number Seven, Harris County (Texas), raising the issue of whether an administrative suspension of a driver's license for failing a breath test constituted a bar to prosecution for driving while intoxicated on the basis of double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: Following appellant's administrative driver's license suspension for failing a breath test, the state filed an information against appellant for driving while intoxicated (DWI). Appellant filed an application for writ of habeas corpus, requesting a double jeopardy bar of his DWI prosecution on the ground that he was punished by the driver's license suspension. The trial court denied relief and appellant sought review therefrom. The court affirmed the denial of the application, holding that the administrative suspension of appellant's driver's license for failing a breath test did not constitute a bar to prosecution for DWI. The court explained that generally a civil sanction that was partly remedial and partly deterrent was a jeopardy bar. Despite the court's finding that the suspension statute was punitive based on the legislative history and the statute's focus on criminal culpability, the driver's license suspension was not a double jeopardy bar because it was designed to constitute rough remedial justice and its effect was not exponentially greater than the amount of the damages caused. Rather, the court viewed the license suspension as a measured and appropriate response.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's application for writ of habeas corpus, holding that an administrative suspension of a driver's license for failing a breath test did not constitute a bar to appellant's prosecution for driving while intoxicated on the basis of double jeopardy.

Norton v. State


No. 14-95-00114-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


918 S.W.2d 25; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 215



January 18, 1996, Rendered  
January 18, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted June 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd District Court. Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 28,198.

This Corrected Majority Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of January 11, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 111.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County (Texas), denying his application for writ of habeas corpus on the ground that the state failed to indict him within two court terms from the date of his arrest.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied appellant's application for writ of habeas corpus complaining of violation of his right to a speedy trial and the state's failure to present an indictment against him in the next term of court after his commitment or admission to bail in violation of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01 (1989). The hearing on appellant's petition for writ of habeas corpus was held before the judge of the 239th District Court, rather than the 23rd District Court where the indictment was filed. The trial court reasoned that, although two terms of the 23rd District Court had passed, the term of the 239th District Court was controlling, and a second term of that court had not passed from the time of arrest to the time of indictment. On appeal, the court held that because the relevant time period under art. 32.01 was from arrest to indictment, the term of the court in which the case was pending during that period, the 23rd District Court, should control. Accordingly, because the second term of the 23rd court passed before appellant was indicted, the indictment was not timely for purposes of art. 32.01. The court sustained appellant's point of error, reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial below of appellant's application for writ of habeas corpus, finding that two terms of the court had expired before appellant was indicted. The court remanded the case with instructions to dismiss the prosecution.

Westphal v. Diaz


NUMBER 13-94-237-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


918 S.W.2d 543; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 339



January 18, 1996, delivered  
January 18, 1996, filed

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 319th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, in her capacities as executrix, individually, and as next friend of deceased son, sought review of the summary judgment rendered in the 319th District Court of Nueces County (Texas) in favor of appellee doctor who asserted the defense of limitations to appellant's survival and wrongful death actions based on appellee's malpractice.


OVERVIEW: Appellee doctor treated decedent for Hodgkin's Disease with Cytoxan. Decedent began to excrete blood in his urine while he was on vacation, and was advised by a different doctor that extended use of Cytoxan had caused his bladder to bleed. Over the course of treatment for the bleeding from his bladder and urinary tract, decedent was intermittently hospitalized from 1984 until his death in 1992, and was led to believe that his condition was a curable effect of the Cytoxan and consequently declined to bring suit. Decedent's bladder cancer was first detected when a new doctor recommended reconstructive bladder surgery in 1991. Appellant as executrix, individually, and as next friend decided to sue appellee for negligence in the course of treatment when the terminal cancer was discovered, but no action was filed until a year after decedent's death. The court held that appellee did not demonstrate that he was entitled to summary judgment because there was an issue of material fact as to whether the urinary tract bleeding was part of the cancer, or whether it was merely a minor, curable side-effect of treatment with Cytoxan, and the bladder cancer was a separate and distinct injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against appellant individually and as executrix, but reversed the summary judgment and remanded the action asserted by appellant as next friend, holding that appellee doctor's proof was inadequate to establish that the statute of limitations barred appellant's claim that the open courts provision and application of the discovery rule could have been invoked in the malpractice suit against appellee.

Howard v. State


No. 01-95-00326-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 92



January 11, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 680983.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 337th District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of aggravated robbery and sentencing him as a second offender to 50 years in prison, on grounds that his sentence was cruel and unusual under U.S. Const. amends. VIII, XIV, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, that his presentence report was reviewed prior to a determination of his guilt in error, and that he was denied compulsory process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to aggravated robbery and was sentenced as a second offender to 50 years in prison. He appealed on grounds that the sentence was cruel and unusual. Under Tex. Penal Code § 12.42(c), defendant was subject to a prison term of no more than 99 years or less than 15 years. The punishment was not cruel or unusual under state or federal constitutions because it was within statutory limits. Defendant's conviction was not void because the lower court did not review his presentence report before determining guilt. Defendant had already pled guilty and did not object to review of the report before his guilt was pronounced. Defendant argued that his right to compulsory process was denied. The court noted that under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (Supp. 1996) (art. 1.15), the state had to produce evidence of defendant's guilt if defendant pled guilty and waived the right to a jury trial. Defendant did not offer evidence, and art. 1.15 did not prevent him from doing so. Defendant did not have to expressly waive his right to compulsory process, but his express waiver of other rights effectively waived his compulsory process right. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated robbery and his sentence to 50 years in prison as a second offender was affirmed. Defendant's sentence was within statutory limits; thus, the punishment was not cruel and unusual under either state or federal constitutions. The lower court's review of his presentence report occurred after defendant had pled guilty. Defendant effectively waived his right to compulsory process, but was not denied this right.

Glasscock Underground Water Conservation Dist. v. Pruit


No. 08-94-00358-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


915 S.W.2d 577; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 118; 137 Oil & Gas Rep. 447



January 11, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 14, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 238th District Court of Midland County, Texas. (TC# 39,419). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. John Hyde.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county water conservation district sought review of a judgment of the 238th District Court of Midland County (Texas), which determined that appellant did not have the right to tax severed mineral estates underlying land in another county that surface owners had annexed into appellant's district from appellees, appraisers and appraisal district, pursuant to 1989 Tex. Sess. Law Serv. 2159 or Tex. Water Code Ann. § 52.521 (Supp. 1996).


OVERVIEW: The Texas legislature enacted 1989 Tex. Sess. Law Serv. 2159, which allowed county landowners to petition to annex their land into appellant county water conservation district. Owners of land in adjoining water district could also annex their land into appellant's district by petitioning for exclusion from the adjoining district, and then petitioning for annexation into appellant's district under Tex. Water Code Ann. § 52.521 (Supp. 1996). Owners of surface estates filed petitions under each of the statutes, but the owners of severed mineral estates under those surface estates did not. Appellees, appraisers and appraisal district, prepared tax rolls for appellant's county that included the value of the surface estates, but not of the severed mineral estates. Appellant sued for a declaration that the severed mineral estates should have been included on the tax rolls for its county. After holding that there was no administrative remedy for appellant to exhaust, the court affirmed a trial court declaration that the severed mineral estates were not annexed into appellant's county. The statutes limited the effect of an owner's petition to the estate that the petitioner actually owned.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed for appellees, appraisers and appraisal district. The statutes gave each owner of an estate in a county the right to petition for annexation of that estate into appellant county water conservation district, and appellant could only tax those estates that chose annexation into its district.

State v. Cannady


NUMBER 13-95-141-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


913 S.W.2d 741; 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 20



January 4, 1996, delivered  
January 4, 1996, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied January 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 138.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 156th District Court of Bee County, Texas. TR.CT.NO. B-94-M004-PR-B.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision of the 156th District Court of Bee County (Texas) that quashed the aggravating portions of appellant's indictment of appellee, thereby barring prosecution of appellee for capital murder.


OVERVIEW: While appellee was incarcerated for two murder convictions, he killed a fellow inmate. Appellant state indicted appellee for capital murder based on the aggravating factor of his two previous convictions. The trial court granted appellee's motion to quash the aggravating portions of the indictment and appellant sought review, contending that the trial court erred in its ruling. The court noted that the indictment alleged all the requirements to properly elevate appellee's offense from murder to capital murder pursuant to the Capital Murder Statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(6). Appellee argued that applying § 19.03 to his case violated the ex post facto prohibition. The court disagreed because at the time appellee murdered his fellow inmate, the act was punishable under § 19.03 and the statute did not retroactively impose a greater punishment that that already prescribed on the date of the crime. The court also rejected appellee's argument that the statute was unconstitutional. The court reversed the order of the trial court quashing the indictment and remanded the cause to the trial court for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court quashing the indictment because it found that the indictment alleged all of the elements necessary to elevate appellee's murder of a fellow inmate to capital murder. In addition, the court held that the capital murder statute was constitutional.

Kaazim Abul 'Umar v. Price


NO. 09-95-068 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 2900


June 26, 1995, Submitted

January 4, 1996, FILED


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 9th District Court. Polk County, Texas. Cause No. 14,983.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner and other prisoners challenged a decision from the 9th District Court, Polk County, (Texas) dismissing their litigation pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001(Supp. 1995). Appellants had contended that the appellee prison officials had committed violations of U.S. Const. amend. VIII and IV, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 (1994), and had committed intentional infliction of emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner and other prisoners filed suit against appellee prison officials in the trial court claiming that appellees had committed negligence and gross negligence in providing meals to inmates, committed violations of U.S. Const. amend. VIII and IV, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 (1994), and had committed intentional infliction of emotional distress. Appellees filed a motion to dismiss in the trial court which was granted pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001(Supp. 1995). Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001 allowed for the dismissal of frivolous suits. Appellants challenged the dismissal on appeal. The court held that some of the appellants' allegations were sufficient to negate official immunity and that sufficient facts were alleged to place good faith in controversy as to the some of the appellees' conduct. Concluding that dismissal of the appellants' suit was premature, the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings on claims dealing with appellee prison officials' claims of immunity, and whether appellants' alleged damages were de minimis. The intentional infliction of emotional distress claim was overruled as to most appellants.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded as to the validity of appellant's claim other than as to intentional infliction of emotional distress as to some prisoners, determination of appellee prison officials' claims of immunity, and determination as to whether appellant's alleged damages are de minimis. The court found some appellant's allegations sufficient to negate official immunity making dismissal premature as to all claims.

Holmans v. Transource Polymers


NO. 2-95-035-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


914 S.W.2d 189; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3222; 131 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P58,041



December 21, 1995, Decided  
December 21, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 1, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 158TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. PHILLIP VICK.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged an order of the 158th District Court of Denton County (Texas) that dismissed his common law claim for unpaid wages against appellee employer. Appellant alleged that the trial court erred in deciding that it lacked subject-matter jurisdiction, and erred in interpreting the Payday Law, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 61.001 et seq. (1996), as providing a mandatory and exclusive remedy.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee brought a common law claim against appellee employer to recover a debt for unpaid wages after having brought a statutory claim therefor against appellee under the Payday Law, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 61.001 et seq. (1996), before the Texas Employment Commission. The court reversed the dismissal order entered by the trial court against appellant's common law claim and remanded the matter for a trial. The trial court erred by granting the dismissal because appellant's Payday Law claim did not pre-empt subject matter jurisdiction over appellant's common law claim. The court held that appellant's common law claim was not purely statutory because the Payday Law did not provide a reasonable substitute for the remedy of a jury trial, which was a constitutional right. The court found that the Payday Law did not repeal the common law remedy, but rather provided an alternative means to recover the debt. Therefore, the court determined that an interpretation of the Payday Law as the mandatory and exclusive remedy would be unconstitutional. Appellant could proceed to trial because he had withdrawn his administrative Payday Law claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that dismissed appellant employee's common law claim for unpaid wages against appellee employer because the trial court properly had subject matter jurisdiction, for the Payday Law that did not repeal the common law remedy, and remanded the matter for trial because appellant had a constitutional right to a jury trial.

Brent v. State


NO. 01-94-00635-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


916 S.W.2d 34; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3267



December 21, 1995, rendered and delivered  
December 21, 1995, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 180th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 669,329. PATRICIA R. LYKOS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for capital murder from the 180th District Court, Harris County (Texas), on the grounds that evidence should have been suppressed because it was seized based on an invalid arrest warrant, that a photograph should have been excluded under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 403, and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: The state charged appellant with capital murder. The court affirmed his conviction of this charge. The trial court correctly decided not to suppress evidence seized pursuant to the execution of the warrant for appellant's arrest. The court held that, although the warrant's supporting affidavit was not signed as required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 18.01(b) (Supp. 1995), the evidence was admissible under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.23(b) (Supp. 1995) for three reasons. First, the evidence was seized in good faith. Second, the warrant was issued by a neutral magistrate under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 2.09 (Supp. 1995). Third, the warrant was based on probable cause. Therefore, the evidence seized pursuant to the invalid warrant's execution was admissible despite any violation of the federal and state constitutions. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting a photograph under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 403 because it was not exceedingly gruesome. Appellant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel due to not being prevented from testifying at a co-defendant's trial because there was no right to be free from the threat of impeachment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for capital murder because the trial court correctly decided not to suppress evidence seized pursuant to an invalid warrant when it was admissible under an exception to the signed affidavit rule; the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting a photograph that was not exceedingly gruesome; and appellant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel.

Hood v. Ryland Group


NO. 09-94-198 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


911 S.W.2d 931; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3205


June 8, 1995, Submitted  
December 14, 1995, Delivered  
December 14, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 2nd 9th District Court. Montgomery County, Texas. Cause No. 94-04-01081-CV. Honorable John C. Martin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, tenant and guests injured when a second-story deck collapsed, sought reversal of an order from the 29th District Court, Montgomery County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee builder in appellants' negligent construction lawsuit.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, tenant and guests, challenged a trial judge's order granting appellee builder summary judgment in appellants' negligent construction lawsuit. The court reversed and remanded. Appellants had sued appellee after the deck on which they wee standing collapsed, asserting that appellee had negligently constructed the deck out of untreated lumber. Appellee responded that because it had constructed the deck over 10 years before suit was filed, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.009 deemed it not liable. Appellants retorted that the fraudulent concealment and willful misconduct exceptions to the 10-year statutory repose period applied. The court, in reversing the trial judge's summary judgment ruling favoring appellee, held that although appellee had conclusively established that it had built the deck over 10 years before it was sued, it had not conclusively defeated appellants' willful misconduct averment. Because a factual dispute related to appellants' willful misconduct argument existed, summary judgment was inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The trial judge's order granting appellee builder summary judgment was reversed, and the case remanded for further proceedings. Although appellee established that the 10-year period under a statute of repose applied, appellants, tenant and guests, made a sufficient proffer that the willful misconduct exception to the repose period also applied, and the existence of a factual dispute as to this issue rendered summary judgment inappropriate.

Bowles v. Reed

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO

December 13, 1995, filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and rendered in part; and reversed and remanded in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a county and its sheriff, sought review of a decision from the District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which entered judgment in favor of appellee trustee, and which awarded actual and punitive damages and attorney's fees. Appellee filed suit against appellants challenging two different bail bond processing fees levied by a county commissioner's court. Appellants filed an equitable setoff claim.


OVERVIEW: Appellee trustee was appointed to administer the bankruptcy estate of a bail bondsman. Appellee filed suit against appellant sheriff and appellant county challenging two different bail bond processing fees levied by the county commissioner's court, and sought four times that sum as a penalty, prejudgment interest, costs of court, and attorneys fees. Appellants filed an equitable setoff claim in response. The lower court rendered judgment against appellants and found them to be jointly and severally liable for damages, costs, attorney's fees, and prejudgment interest. Appellant sheriff was found separately liable for additional damages and prejudgment interest. The court reversed and rendered a take-nothing judgment in appellant sheriff's favor on one bond fee issue because it held that appellant sheriff had legislative immunity from liability for authorized acts. However, the court determined appellant sheriff was liable in his representative capacity for on the second bond fee issue because he was not authorized to collect such fees.


OUTCOME: The lower court's decision awarding appellee trustee actual and punitive damages, attorney's fees, and prejudgment interest was affirmed in part. The court held that appellant sheriff was improperly held to be personally liable for the bond fees. The court determined that appellant sheriff was liable for the other fees and that remand was necessary for a new determination of the amount of his liability.

911 S.W.2d 893; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3203



December 11, 1995, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 237TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 93,588-A; HONORABLE JOHN R. MCFALL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife sought review of a judgment from the 237th Judicial District Court of Lubbock County (Texas), which found in favor of appellee, her ex-husband's new wife, in appellant's suit to recover a portion of her ex-husband's retirement benefits and a portion of an annuity paid to appellee on the ex-husband's death. The original property division had been made under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.91(a) (1993).


OVERVIEW: Appellant ex-wife brought an action against appellee, her ex-husband's new wife, to recover a portion of her ex-husband's retirement benefits and a portion of an annuity paid to appellee on the ex-husband's death that had been purchased with proceeds from the retirement benefits. Appellant had divorced her ex-husband 12 years earlier and agreed to a property division, at which time the existence of the retirement benefits was known. The court also opined that § 3.91 was constitutional and that, in any event, appellant could not challenge its constitutionality for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against appellant ex-wife and in favor of appellee, her ex-husband's new wife, on appellant's suit for a portion of her ex-husband's retirement benefits. The court found that appellant had not carried her burden of showing that the property division occurring at the time of the divorce had been manifestly unjust.

Anderson v. State


No. 01-94-00568-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3077



December 7, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused May 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 679766.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 337th District Court, Harris County, Texas convicting him of capital murder under a conspiracy theory under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) (1994) and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 7.02(a)(2),(b) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) (1994), under a conspiracy theory, after he and an accomplice stabbed a young boy during an attempted robbery. Appellant challenged the conviction arguing that the trial court erred by submitting an instruction to the jury that authorized the jury to convict appellant of capital murder without any requirement of intent. The court affirmed, finding that the law of parties under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 7.02(b) (1994) eliminated any necessity on the part of the state to prove that the appellant had any intent to kill the boy. To convict under § 7.02(b), the state only had to show that appellant conspired with others to commit an aggravated robbery, that one of his coconspirators intentionally caused the death in the course of committing or attempting to commit the aggravated robbery, and that appellant should have anticipated the result. The court also found that the § 7.02(b) instruction did not implicate U.S. Const. amends. VIII and XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19, because this was not a death penalty case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's capital murder conviction. The court found that the instruction authorizing the jury to convict appellant of capital murder without the requirement of intent was valid, because the intent of his coconspirator was imputed to him under the law of parties, since the murder was a foreseeable result of the aggravated robbery.

Bennett v. State


No. 01-94-00841-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3078



December 7, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9418775.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 176th District Court, Harris County, Texas, for felony theft by check under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of felony theft by check and sentenced to 25 years in prison. Appellant challenged his conviction, but the court affirmed, finding that the evidence was legally sufficient to support the charge. The court found that the state proved that appellant unlawfully appropriated merchandise, with the intent to deprive the store of the property, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a) (1994), when he wrote bad checks for the merchandise. The court found that the trial court properly admitted evidence of an extraneous hot check transaction that occurred after the charged offense, because the offense was similar and showed both identity and intent, which appellant had placed at issue with a "not guilty" plea. The court found that the evidence was not so compelling under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 403 as to affect the trial court's ability to disregard the evidence for any but its proper purpose. The court found that appellant's sentence did not violate his U.S. Const. amends. VIII, XIV rights because, given his two prior felonies and the possibility of parole, the sentence was not disproportionate to the crime committed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's felony theft by check conviction, finding that the evidence was legally sufficient to support the conviction, that evidence of a similar, post-offense conviction was properly admitted to show identity and intent, and that the 25-year sentence was not unconstitutional, given appellant's two prior felonies, and his possibility of parole.

Harris v. State


No. 06-95-00051-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


913 S.W.2d 706; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3082


December 7, 1995, Submitted  
December 7, 1995, Decided  
December 7, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 291st Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court No. F94-58143-SU.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his sentence and conviction from the 291st Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas) for possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress narcotics found on his person and by assessing punishment in excess of the statutory maximum for a state jail felony under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112(b) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his sentence and conviction for possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court first rejected defendant's claim that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress narcotics found on his person after a search incident to arrest. Specifically, defendant claimed that the arresting officers did not have adequate facts in their possession to justify a temporary investigative detention and that, therefore, the narcotics were improperly admitted into evidence. The court ruled that defendant's odd conduct, that of dancing in the street, coupled with the officers' observation of him holding what appeared to be a crack pipe, provided the officers with reasonable suspicion to conduct an investigatory stop. The court then rejected defendant's claim that he should have been sentenced to state jail under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112(b) (1996), as amended, because he was sentenced after the statute was amended. The court ruled that he was properly sentenced under the statute as it read when the offense occurred and that such a sentence did not violate his equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence and conviction for possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance. Defendant's conduct coupled with the arresting officer's observations provided reasonable suspicion for the investigative detention of defendant. The narcotics found in the subsequent search incident to arrest were properly not suppressed. Defendant was properly sentenced under the statute that was effective at the time of arrest.

Owens v. State


No. 14-94-00722-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3144



December 7, 1995, Rendered  
December 7, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 683253.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 177th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, weighing less than 28 grams.


OVERVIEW: Two deputies stopped appellant for driving a vehicle with license plates not registered to that vehicle. During the stop, the deputies found crack cocaine in appellant's car. Thereafter, appellant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, weighing less than 28 grams. Appellant challenged his conviction, contending that the officers' initial detention was unconstitutional. Affirming the trial court's judgment, the court ruled that law enforcement officers may stop and briefly detain persons suspected of criminal activity on less information than is constitutionally required for a probable cause to arrest. The court held that the officers had reasonable suspicion that some activity out of the ordinary had occurred or was occurring, and that there was some suggestion to connect appellant with the unusual activity and some indication that the activity was related to a crime. As such, the trial court did not err in refusing to suppress the evidence discovered in the subsequent arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, weighing less than 28 grams because the temporary detention of appellant was justified because the officers personally observed him committing a traffic offense.

Agbor v. St. Luke's Episcopal Hosp.


No. 14-94-00410-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


912 S.W.2d 354; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3007



November 30, 1995, Rendered  
November 30, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 129th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-19,823. Abbot, Greg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant family sought review of the summary judgment entered by the 129th District Court of Harris County, Texas, for appellee hospital in appellant's suit for negligent credentialing of a doctor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant family sued appellee hospital and delivering doctor for negligent credentialing and medical malpractice for injuries sustained by their son during his birth. The trial court granted appellees summary judgment and severed the two actions. Appellant sought review of the negligent credentialing action, and argued that trial court incorrectly interpreted the Texas Medical Practice Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. ann. Art. 4495b 1.01-6.13 (1995), as requiring patients to prove malice in actions against hospitals. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court reviewed the Act in its entirety. The court reasoned that, if interpreted as the trial court did, the Act would require injured patients to prove malice without benefit of discovery. The court held that such an interpretation would make the Act internally contradictory. The court found that the legislative history of the Act stated that immunity was never meant to cover injured patients, and held that sustaining the judgment would deny appellants a meaningful or effective remedy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order granting summary judgment because the court determined that appellant hospital could not be permitted to require proof of malice in a negligent credentialing claim by an injured patient.

Fitchett v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3054



November 30, 1995, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 10. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. MA94-30603-L, MA94-31571-L, and MA94-30477-L.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the Dallas County Criminal Court No. 10 (Texas) for promotion of obscenity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1), claiming that the statute was unconstitutional because it violated appellant's free speech rights. Appellant also claimed that the evidence to sustain his conviction was insufficient.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, who worked at an adult video store, was convicted of promotion of obscenity, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1), after recommending pornographic tapes to undercover police officers. Appellant sought review of his conviction, claiming that the obscenity statute was unconstitutional because it violated his free speech rights under Tex. Const. art I, § 8. Appellant further argued that the evidence to sustain his conviction was insufficient to show that he knew the nature and content of the videotapes alleged to be obscene. The court sustained appellant's conviction, holding that obscenity was not protected speech under Tex. Const. art I, § 8, and that in any event appellant did not argue the constitutionality of the obscenity statute during trial, and therefore the argument could not be raised for the first time on appeal unless the obscenity statute was facially unconstitutional. The court also ruled that there was sufficient evidence to sustain appellant's conviction. The boxes to the videotapes that appellant recommended to the police officers suggested sexual content, and appellant could be convicted on such circumstantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant criminal defendant's conviction for promotion of obscenity, holding that obscenity was not protected speech under the Texas Constitution. The court further stated that appellant did not argue at trial that the obscenity statute was unconstitutional, therefore, the argument was waived on appeal. The court also held that the evidence was sufficient to sustain appellant's conviction.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator sought a writ of habeas corpus alleging he was illegally restrained of his liberty by virtue of a judgment of contempt and a commitment order issued by the 309th District Court, Harris County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Relator was ordered to pay child support. Years later, he was charged with the offense of criminal non-support. Relator pleaded nolo contendere in the criminal court and was placed on probation for two years subject to paying restitution. Six months later, the district court found relator in contempt for failure to pay child support and confined him in the county jail. He then filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus with the court. The court granted the petition, ordered relator released on bond, and heard oral arguments. In his petition, relator contended that the district court's order was void because it violated the double jeopardy provisions of the United States and Texas Constitutions, the criminal court erred by imposing criminal penalties for acts not proven beyond a reasonable doubt, and Tex. After overruling all of relator's contentions, the court declined to grant the writ of habeas corpus. The writ was denied, relator's bond revoked, and he was remanded to the sheriff's custody.


OUTCOME: The court denied relator's petition for a writ of habeas corpus, revoked his bond and remanded relator to the custody of the county sheriff because the contempt and commitment order were not void under the double jeopardy provisions of the United States and Texas Constitutions. Relator provided nothing to show that the trial court applied the incorrect standard, and the Texas statute did not violate due process.
