Harris County Mun. Util. Dist. No. 48 v. Mitchell


No. 01-94-00712-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


915 S.W.2d 859; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2857



November 16, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 269th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-13656. DAVID WEST, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified, as modified, affirmed,


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility challenged a judgment from the Harris County District Court (Texas), which awarded appellee, the executrix of the developer's successor in interest, contract damages arising out of a loan to provide utilities for a subdivision.


OVERVIEW: A developer loaned appellant utility a certain amount of money so that appellant could provide services to a subdivision. Appellee, the executrix of the developer's successor in interest, filed an action against appellant to collect on the loan. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellee. Appellant argued that the trial court erred because appellee was not a proper party to the lawsuit. On appeal, the court held that as the succeessor's executrix, appellee was a proper party to the lawsuit. The court also held that the parties' contract was not rendered ambiguous because of a variable interest rate. The court further found that the financial agreement did not contain a condition precedent. The court held that a commission had primary jurisdiction to determine the interest rate because it was authorized by state statute. The court also held that the trial court erred by concluding that the commission's determination of a lump sum was not a lower interest rate. Additionally, the trial court erred when it awarded attorney's fees to appellee. Judgment was modified but affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that awarded appellee contract damages was modified because the trial court erred when it awarded prejudgment interest and attorney's fee to appellee. However, judgment was affirmed because the evidence was sufficient to support it.

 

1077 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Winkle v. Tullos


No. 14-93-00995-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


917 S.W.2d 304; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2866



November 16, 1995, Rendered  
November 16, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion on Motion for Rehearing February 8, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 548.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 11th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 87-31847. Davidson Mark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two medical malpractice suits against appellee doctor, appellant patient challenged judgments for appellee by the 11th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which held that the limitations period of the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01, barred the first suit, and that appellee was not liable in the second suit.


OVERVIEW: Following knee replacement and revision surgeries by appellee doctor, appellant's right leg was amputated below the knee. Appellant sued appellee for medical malpractice. Regarding the knee replacement surgery, the jury found that appellant brought suit beyond the limitations period of the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01. As to the revision surgery, the jury found that appellee was not liable for lack of informed consent, misrepresentation, negligence, gross negligence, and damages. The trial court entered judgment accordingly. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the Act's statute of limitations barred appellant's first suit because it was not filed within two years of the date of the knee replacement surgery. With respect to the revision surgery, the judgment was affirmed because appellee fully disclosed the risks of the surgery and appellant gave her informed consent. Moreover, there was sufficient evidence that appellee's use of a tourniquet during the surgery was within reasonable medical standards. Thus, there was no basis to find appellee liable for negligence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's entry of judgments in favor of appellee doctor in two medical malpractice cases brought by appellant, holding that the limitations period of the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act did bar the first suit regarding knee replacement surgery and the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to find that appellee was not negligent with respect to the second revision surgery.

 

1078 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Roth v. State


NO. 03-94-00201-CR, NO. 03-94-00202-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


917 S.W.2d 292; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3296



November 15, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion to Publish Opinion Granted January 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NOS. 0935934 & 0935935, HONORABLE MICHAEL LYNCH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded on Both Causes


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his convictions by the 167th Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas), for possession of a controlled substance, psilocybin, in an amount less than 28 grams and for possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, in an amount less than 28 grams.


OVERVIEW: When police officers entered appellant's apartment searching for a runaway, they observed psilocybin and cocaine. Appellant was convicted of two counts of possession of a controlled substance. On appeal, the court held that consent was not voluntary if it was nothing more than acquiescence to a claim of lawful authority. The court held that an officer's subjective testimony that appellant looked like he did not mind the intrusion and the fact that appellant had not invited the officers into his apartment showed that the consent was not voluntary. The court found no exigent circumstances excusing the warrantless intrusion into appellant's apartment because state failed to show that there was not time to obtain a search warrant or that the runaway was in danger of losing his life or suffering serious bodily injury. The court held that the plain view doctrine was inapplicable because the officers did not have a right to be in appellant's apartment when they saw the psilocybin. The court held that the cocaine obtained after officers obtained written consent was an exploitation of an illegal arrest and detention, and it was not purged of the primary taint of the illegal intrusion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded appellant's convictions for possession of a controlled substance because the trial court improperly denied appellant's motion to suppress evidence found in his apartment. State failed to show that appellant freely and voluntarily gave the police officers consent to enter and search his apartment, and there were no exigent circumstances that would otherwise justify the warrantless entry.

 

1079 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Telles Bail Bonds v. State


No. 08-95-00032-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


911 S.W.2d 820; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3206



November 9, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] November 9, 1995, Motion Granted for Publication. Rehearing denied December 13, 1995. Motion for Rehearing of Application for Writ of Error Overruled September 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Court at Law # 2 of El Paso County, Texas. (TC # 93-B04346). Trial Court Judge: Hon. Sam Callan - presiding.



DISPOSITION: Having overruled Appellant's sole point of error, we affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bail bonds company sought review of a judgment of County Court at Law #2 of El Paso County (Texas), which granted forfeiture of an appearance bond under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.13(1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellant bail bond company executed a surety bond to secure the release of a principle from custody. The principle failed to appear at a court hearing as required by the terms of the bail bond and was re-arrested. The principle entered a plea of guilty to the offense charged, was sentenced, and released from custody. The trial court rendered judgment against appellant in favor of the state for forfeiture of the bail bond. The court affirmed the judgment that granted a final forfeiture on the bail bond because under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.13(1989) disposition of the underlying criminal case did not exonerate appellant from liability on a bail bond where the principle failed to appear at a scheduled criminal hearing prior to the disposition of the criminal case. The court held that the only grounds for exonerating appellant from forfeiture of the bond were provided under art. 22.13. The bond was valid, the principle had not died, the principle was not sick or subjected to any other uncontrollable circumstances which prevented his appearance at court, and the state did not fail to present an indictment or information at the first term of the court after bail was posted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that granted a final forfeiture on the bail bond in favor of the state against appellant bail bond company because disposition of the underlying criminal case failed to exonerate appellant from liability on the surety when the principle failed to appear in court at a criminal hearing before the disposition of the criminal case.

 

1080 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Naugle v. Theard


No. 08-94-00356-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


917 S.W.2d 287; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2719



November 2, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 28, 1995. Rehearing Overruled December 15, 1995. Released for Publication March 25, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 120th Judicial District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC # 93-9577). Trial Court Judge: Hon. Robert Dinsmoor.



DISPOSITION: Having overruled each of Appellant's points of error, we affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order from the 120th Judicial District Court of El Paso County (Texas) granting appellee doctor's summary judgment motion on the ground that appellant's medical malpractice suit, brought pursuant to the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sued appellee doctor for medical malpractice. Appellant asserted that appellee's failure to advise her that he had not ligated her right fallopian tube led to the subsequent pregnancy and health problems. Appellee moved for summary judgment, contending that the two-year statute of limitations provision of the Medical Malpractice Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, barred the claim. The lower court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. Appellant challenged, attacking the judgment and claiming that the lower court erred in granting summary judgment because the cause of action was not barred by the statute of limitations. Appellant asserted that Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01, as applied to her cause of action, violated the open courts provision of the state constitution. The court disagreed. Appellant learned of her injury while there was a reasonable time to sue within the period prescribed by the statute, and thus the statute of limitations was not unconstitutional as applied to her. Further, the court ruled that there was not a disputed fact issue as to when appellant discovered the nature and full extent of her injuries.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order granting appellee doctor's summary judgment motion because the two-year statute of limitations provision of the state Medical Malpractice Act barred appellee's medical malpractice claim, and the statute of limitations was not unconstitutional as applied to appellant.

 

1081 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Ericson v. Roberts


NO. 12-94-00134-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


910 S.W.2d 608; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2765



October 31, 1995, delivered  
October 31, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 241ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF SMITH COUNTY, TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, patient and wife, challenged a take-nothing summary judgment entered by the 241st Judicial District Court of Smith County (Texas) in a medical malpractice case in which appellants alleged that appellee doctor negligently performed a circumcision operation. Appellants contended that the court erred when it held that their malpractice claim was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, patient and wife, contended that appellee doctor negligently performed a circumcision operation. A year after the surgery, appellant returned to appellee for treatment of redness and pain. Appellee's insurance carrier paid for corrective surgery arranged by appellee. Action was initiated by appellants within two years after the corrective surgery, but almost three years after the initial surgery. The trial court granted a take-nothing summary judgment on behalf of appellee, holding that appellants' claim was barred by the statute of limitations, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 4.01. On appeal, the court held that the limitations period began to run on the date of the initial surgery. Appellants did not allege that appellee negligently administered a course of treatment over a continuing period of time or that appellee misdiagnosed a condition. The corrective surgery did not extend the limitations period, but was merely an amicable attempt to settle a potential claim. The open courts provision, Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, did not apply because it was not impossible for appellants to know of the injury within two years. The order was therefore affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor because the claim of appellant patient and wife was barred by the statute of limitations. The corrective surgery arranged by appellee was an amicable attempt to resolve a potential claim and did not extend the limitations period on the claim against appellee.

 

1082 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. State


No. 01-94-00833-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2624



October 26, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 56th District Court. Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93CR1410.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 56th District Court, Galveston County (Texas), which convicted him of murder, contending that the trial court erred by not reading him the indictment at arraignment or trial, by excusing a potentially qualified juror sua sponte, and by including language on parole eligibility in the jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for murder, contending the trial court reversibly erred by failing to read him the indictment at arraignment or trial, by excusing a potential juror sua sponte, and by including language on parole eligibility in the jury instructions. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, finding the trial court complied with the provisions of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 27.13 (1989), which pertained to procedures in guilty pleas. The court determined that defendant waived, in open court, the reading of the indictment, and that he was entitled to waive that right under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.14(a) (Supp. 1995). The court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's sua sponte dismissal of a potential juror based upon the determination that she could not deliberate in the case with clarity. The court concluded that following an amendment, Tex. Const. art. IV, § 11(a) permitted the legislature to reenact Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07(4) to permit the trial court to inform the jury about the effect of good conduct time and eligibility for parole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for murder, finding the trial court followed the appropriate guilty plea procedure, and in accordance therewith defendant waived the reading of the indictment. The court determined there was no abuse of discretion in the trial court's dismissal of a juror sua sponte, and an amendment to the state constitution permitted legislation that allowed the court to inform the jury about parole eligibility.

 

1083 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Kimsey


No. 08-95-00070-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


915 S.W.2d 523; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2664



October 26, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Motion for Rehearing November 8, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2785.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator husband petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus to challenge a Texas trial court order, which held him in contempt of court for failing to obey a temporary order that required him to pay his wife's interim attorney fees and expenses in their divorce action and which committed him to the county jail. Relator argued that the order was void because he was incarcerated for failure to pay a debt in violation of Texas Const. art. I, § 18.


OVERVIEW: Relator's wife filed suit for divorce and requested additional temporary orders seeking interim attorney fees and expenses. The trial court entered a temporary order requiring relator husband to make 10 payments of $ 5,000 for temporary spousal support. After relator failed to pay the $ 50,000 to the registry of the court, his wife filed a motion for contempt. The trial court found relator in contempt of court for failing to make the required payments and committed him to the county jail until he complied with the order. Thereafter, relator filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Relator argued that the contempt order was void because he was incarcerated for failure to pay a debt in violation of Texas Const. art. I, § 18. The appeals court denied relator's petition. The court held that relator's confinement was valid pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 3.58(f) because he violated the temporary order. The court reasoned that obligations incurred for the support of children and spouses did not constitute a debt. Thus, an order of contempt arising from the failure to pay those obligations could be enforced by incarceration without running afoul of the constitutional prohibition.


OUTCOME: The appeals court denied relator husband's petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The court held that relator's confinement was valid because he violated the temporary order requiring him to make payments for the support of his children and his former spouse and that those obligations did not constitute a debt.

City of Dallas v. Aye


No. 05-95-00361-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2642



October 24, 1995, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 101st District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 95-02133-E.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city filed an interlocutory appeal that challenged the decision of the 101st District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which granted appellee taxicab driver a temporary injunction to prevent appellant from enforcing a city ordinance that made it a criminal offense to operate a taxicab more than five years old unless it was equipped to use alternative fuel.


OVERVIEW: Appellee taxicab driver successful obtained an order form the civil trial court that temporarily enjoined appellant city from enforcing its ordinance that made it a criminal offense to operate a taxicab more than five years old unless it was equipped to use alternative fuel. Appellant filed an interlocutory appeal challenging the order. The court reversed and held that the civil trial court did not have jurisdiction to enjoin a penal ordinance. The court held that the use of public highway by common carriers was a privilege, and the mere fact that use of a vehicle could subject appellee to arrest and prosecution was not irreparable injury because appellee could challenge the constitutionality of the ordinance in a criminal prosecution of the penal ordinance, which was an adequate remedy at law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court that enjoined appellant city from enforcing its ordinance because the trial court was a civil court and had no authority to enjoin a penal ordinance.

Devore v. Central Bank & Trust


NO. 2-94-128-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


908 S.W.2d 605; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2550



October 19, 1995, Decided  
October 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM COUNTY COURT AT LAW NUMBER TWO OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. STEVE WALLACE.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the trial court's judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment debtor sought review of an order from the County Court at Law Number Two of Tarrant County (Texas), which entered a turnover order requiring him to turn over to appellee judgment creditor monthly income received as an independent contractor in appellee's suit to collect on a judgment under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 31.002 (1995).


OVERVIEW: In appellee judgment creditor's suit against appellant judgment debtor to collect on a default judgment, the trial court entered a turnover order requiring appellant to turn over monthly sums he received as an independent contractor. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding the trial court did not abuse its discretion. The court held that the trial court's findings of the monthly amount to be paid, and that appellant was working as an independent contractor, were supported by ample evidence, and thus were not arbitrary or unreasonable. Wages he received from his client were not exempt from turnover as "current wages" under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 31.002(f) (1995) or Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 42.001(b)(1) (1995) as appellant was an independent contractor. Appellant's argument that wages paid to him by his professional corporation were "current wages," and were therefore a violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 3, was meritless as appellant testified he no longer received wages from his law firm. The term "current wages" implies a master and servant relationship, not an attorney engaged in private practice as an independent contractor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order requiring appellant attorney judgment debtor to turn over to appellee judgment creditor monthly income received as an independent contractor in appellee's suit to collect on a judgment. Appellant's income were not "current wages" exempt from turnover as he was an independent contractor and he testified that he no longer received wages from his law firm.

Penick v. Christensen


No. 14-94-00209-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


912 S.W.2d 276; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2412



October 5, 1995, Rendered  
October 5, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 55th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 85-39836, Stone Kathleen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and Reversed and Remanded in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient, sought review of the take nothing judgment entered by the 55th District Court, Harris County, Texas, after a partial summary judgment in favor of appellee manufacturer, and jury trial against appellee doctor, in a medical malpractice and product liability action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient, in a medical malpractice and product liability action sought review of the partial summary judgment entered in favor of appellee doctor, and a take nothing judgment entered in favor of appellee manufacturer. Appellant claimed appellee doctor negligently recommended and negligently performed unnecessary hip replacement surgery, without his informed consent; and appellee manufacturer's cement product was defective causing the artificial hip to become loose. The court affirmed the take nothing judgment finding that the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act's, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, 6.02 (1995), procedure for obtaining a patient's informed consent through disclosure of risks promulgated by the Texas Medical Disclosure Panel was constitutional. The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of appellee manufacturer finding its summary judgment motion had not addressed causation, and had only argued that there was no defect in the cement. The court held the law did not provide for summary judgment for a defendant unless it conclusively negated an element of a plaintiff's cause of action.


OUTCOME: In a medical malpractice/product liability action, the court reversed the summary judgment in favor of appellee manufacturer and remanded appellant patient's cause of action against it for a trial on the merits. The court concluded that appellee manufacturer failed to establish that it was entitled to judgment as a matter of law. The take nothing judgment in favor of appellee doctor was affirmed.

 

1087 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Delgado v. State


No. 08-95-00007-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


908 S.W.2d 317; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2430



October 5, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled October 25, 1995. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 24, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 65th District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 71390-65). Trial Court Judge: Hon. Edward Marquez.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction and sentence for burglary of a vehicle entered by the District Court of El Paso County (Texas). On appeal, he maintained that he should have been sentenced under the amended version of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.04(c).


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to, was convicted of, and sentenced for burglary of a vehicle. On appeal, he asserted that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to compel sentencing under the amended version of the Texas Penal Code. Appellant committed his offense nearly one year before the effective date of the amendments. Consequently, the court found that the trial court properly applied the pre-revision version of the Penal Code at appellant's plea hearing and sentencing. Appellant also contended that Tex. Gov't Code Ann § 311.031 provided for sentencing under an amended statute where the amendment reduced the punishment for an offense if punishment had not yet been imposed. However, the court determined that a general savings clause conflicted with the specific savings provision of the later enacted legislation that amended the Penal Code, and therefore, it was inapplicable. Appellant's equal protection claim was also without merit as appellant was tried and sentenced in the same manner as all criminal defendants who committed similar offenses prior to the effective date of the revised Penal Code. The judgment and sentence of the trial court was therefore affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed; appellant had committed his offense nearly one year before the effective date of the amendments to the Texas Penal Code, so the trial court properly applied the pre-revision version of the Penal Code at appellant's plea hearing and sentencing.

Meisner v. State


No. 10-94-276-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


907 S.W.2d 664; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2376



September 29, 1995, delivered  
September 29, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Court at Law. Ellis County, Texas. Trial Court # 93-12626-CR.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the County Court at Law, Ellis County (Texas), which convicted him for the traffic violation of "digging out," or squealing a car's tires, under Waxahachie, Tex., Code § 32-132. The trial court denied appellant's motion to quash, finding that the ordinance was constitutional and that it gave sufficient notice of the proscribed conduct.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled no contest to the municipal traffic violation of "digging out" under Waxahachie, Tex., Code § 32-132, for squealing his car's tires on a rainy day. Appellant sought review in the county court, where his motion to quash the complaint was denied and he was fined $ 10. Appellant further challenged his conviction, asserting that the municipal ordinance was void for vagueness, and the court on appeal agreed. The court found that the ordinance was unconstitutional as applied to appellant because "willful" was not defined, and because the police would not have sufficient information to prevent arbitrary enforcement of the ordinance. The court also found the second provision of the ordinance, prohibiting unnecessary noise, to be vague and to give insufficient notice to both appellant and the police. Because both halves of the ordinance were unconstitutional, the court reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for "digging out," or squealing a car's tires, and remanded with instructions to dismiss the complaint because the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the term "willful" was not defined and that the second half of the ordinance, prohibiting unnecessary noise, was similarly unconstitutional as applied to appellant because it gave insufficient notice of the proscribed conduct.

Harris County Appraisal Dist. v. Transamerica Container Leasing


No. 01-90-00678-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


920 S.W.2d 678; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2305



September 21, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied January 10, 1997. Motion for Rehearing of Application for Writ of Error Overruled February 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 80th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89-12817. R.L. McKIM, Judge.

Original Opinion of September 26, 1991, Reported at: 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2389.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an appraisal district and its appraisal review board, sought review of the judgment of the 80th District Court, Harris County (Texas), that an ad valorem property tax was unconstitutional as applied to shipping containers owned by appellee corporation and used exclusively in foreign commerce.


OVERVIEW: On request by appellee corporation for judicial review of the application by appellants, an appraisal district and its appraisal review board, of an ad valorem property tax to appellee's shipping containers that were used only in foreign commerce, the trial court determined that the tax was unconstitutional as applied. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment on the initial appeal, but was reversed and directed by the United States Supreme Court to further consider the issue. On remand, the court noted that the parties had stipulated that the shipping containers had a sufficient nexus with the state, that the tax was fairly apportioned, and that it did not prevent the federal government from speaking with one voice when regulating commercial relations with foreign governments. The court further held that the tax did not discriminate against interstate commerce and that it was fairly related to the services provided by the state. Holding that there was a substantial risk that the containers would be subject to multiple taxation and that the tax thus violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I. § 8, cl. 3, however, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the ad valorem property tax was unconstitutionally applied by appellants, an appraisal district and its appraisal review board, to appellee corporation's shipping containers, because the substantial risk that the tax could expose the containers to multiple taxation as a result of their use in foreign commerce constituted a violation of the Commerce Clause.

American Home Assur. v. Texas Dep't of Ins.


NO. 03-94-00498-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


907 S.W.2d 90; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2286



September 20, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled October 25, 1995. Released for Publication October 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 92-09938, HONORABLE JERRY A. DELLANA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurers challenged a decision of the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District (Texas), which granted judgment in favor of appellees State Board of Insurance and state officers in appellants' tax protest action that challenged Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 5.76-5 (1995).


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurers which were underwriters for workers' compensation insurance challenged the imposition and collection of a tax created under Tex. Ins. Code Ann art. 5.76-5 (1995), designed to retire bonds issued to create a workers' compensation insurance fund. A device was created for a tax recoupment system in Tex. Admin. Code Ann. § 1.411 (1993). Appellants protested the tax collection and were denied recovery. Appellants challenged the decision and asserted the recoupment system was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment that the insurers take nothing and held that the statute was constitutional. It did not act as a retroactive law because the tax was basis on business activity before the date of collection. The court further held that the fund was not a collection of public funds for private purposes and concluded that the tax was equal and uniform, and did not constitute double taxation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that appellant insurers take nothing in their tax protest action against appellees State Board of Insurance and state officers since the court determined that the tax enabling statute did not violate the Texas Constitution.

State v. Southoaks Dev. Co.


Appeal No. 04-93-00640-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


920 S.W.2d 330; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3627



September 20, 1995, Delivered  
September 20, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied October 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 45th Judicial District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 89-TA1-2853 and 89-TA1-4468. Honorable Martha Tanner, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state and local taxing units, sought review of a decision by the 45th Judicial District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which granted partial summary judgment in favor of appellee landowner in appellants' action for agricultural roll-back taxes and rendered judgment in a consolidated bench trial for appellee's counterclaim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because appellants' lack of adequate notice denied him procedural due process.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, state and local taxing units, brought actions against appellee landowner for agricultural roll-back taxes and penalties. At the time the agricultural roll-back tax was assessed, the only communication the statutes required to be given appellee was a statement for additional taxes, which did not reach appellee because they were sent to the prior owners of appellee's land. The statutes contained no provision for protesting the agricultural roll-back tax. Appellants challenged the judgment granting partial summary judgment in favor of appellee in appellants' actions for back taxes, penalties, and costs, and awarding appellee attorney's fees and costs under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The court affirmed and found the summary judgment was supported by sufficient evidence. The then-existing procedures violated appellee's due process rights because they were not adequate to provide appellee with either notice of the tax assessment or a meaningful opportunity to protest and have his protest heard. Appellee was entitled to attorney's fees and costs under § 1988 because he obtained significant relief under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and thus was a prevailing party for purposes of § 1988.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the partial summary judgment in favor of appellee landowner in the action by appellants, state and local taxing units, against appellee for agricultural roll-back taxes, penalties and interest, and the award of attorney's fees and costs. The roll-back provision deprived appellee of due process by not giving him sufficient notice or an opportunity to protest the tax, and sufficient evidence supported the summary judgment.

Deprez v. Brewer


No. 05-94-01540-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3408



September 8, 1995, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 44th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-8126-B.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff concert patron appealed a judgment of 44th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which was entered on a directed verdict as to all causes of action against defendants, city, police department and police officer, and as to all causes of action against defendants, theater operator and its affiliates, except assault, false imprisonment, and negligence, as to which judgment was entered against plaintiff on a take-nothing verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant theater operator's employee detained plaintiff concert patron after a scuffle and chase that was prompted by plaintiff's attempt to sell T-shirts at the concert. Plaintiff was ultimately arrested by defendant police officer, who was working as a security guard. Plaintiff sued defendants, city, police department, officer, theater operator, and affiliates. Defendants prevailed. On appeal, the court held that the evidence established that defendant officer was entitled to immunity because he acted in good faith under both state and federal law, and the trial court did not err in granting a directed verdict for defendants city, police department, and officer, on all causes of action. The court also affirmed the directed verdict for defendant theater operator and affiliates because there was no evidence of breach of contract, and affirmed the jury take-nothing verdict on other causes of action. The jury findings were legally and factually sufficient, the reconsideration of discovery sanctions was not an abuse of discretion, and any errors involved in the exclusion of deposition evidence and of testimony on attorney's fees, or in the trial judge's conduct, were harmless.


OUTCOME: Judgment for defendants in tort action was affirmed. There was no evidence that defendants, theater operator and affiliates, breached a contract, and defendants, city, police department, and police officer, had immunity. The verdict on plaintiff concert patron's false imprisonment claims against defendant theater operator and affiliates was not against the weight of the evidence, and reconsideration of sanctions was not an abuse of discretion.

Martin v. State


No. 05-91-01485-CR, No. 05-91-01486-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3388



September 7, 1995, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 2. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. F91-63357-K and F91-63356-MK.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of orders from the Criminal District Court No. 2, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him of robbery, arguing that the indictments against him should have been quashed and asserting that his appellate attorney was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to two counts of robbery, and appealed his convictions. Appellant argued that the indictments against him should have been quashed, and asserted that his appellate counsel was ineffective. The court held that appellant's notice of appeal met the requirements of Tex. R. App. P. 40(b)(1), and preserved his right to appeal the denial of his motion to quash. Appellant failed to show the rule was unconstitutional as applied to him. However, the court found that appellant waived his right to appeal the alleged defects in the indictments because he did not object to the indictments before the date of trial, but filed his motion to quash on the day of trial. Further, appellant signed a form that expressly waived his right to challenge defects in the indictment. The court rejected appellant's argument that he was denied effective assistance of appellate counsel because, although the notice of appeal was proper, appellant presented nothing for review. The court therefore affirmed appellant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The trial court's orders convicting appellant of robbery were affirmed because appellant expressly waived his right to challenge any defects in the indictments, and waived his right to challenge the defects by failing to object to the indictments before the date of trial. Appellant's ineffective assistance of appellate counsel arguments were moot, as there were no valid issues raised for review on appeal.

 

1094 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hanley v. State


No. 14-93-00559-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


909 S.W.2d 117; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2120



August 31, 1995, Rendered  
August 31, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 10. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9254214. Ross Sherman Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of misdemeanor assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.01(a) (1989), entered by the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10, Harris County, Texas. Appellant argued that the trial court improperly excused a juror sua sponte after the jury had been selected, sworn, and impaneled, and that his conviction was invalid because he did not execute a written waiver of his right to trial by jury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was tried for misdemeanor assault. During voir dire, a prospective juror indicated that he would be unable to concentrate on the trial. Nevertheless, he was seated as a juror and he failed to report to the trial court on the second day of trial. Over defense counsel's objection, he was excused from further jury service. The trial court then gave the defense the choice between proceeding to trial with five jurors or empanelling a new jury. Without waiving his objection, defense counsel chose to proceed with five jurors. The trial court convicted appellant of assault. On appeal the court reversed the conviction and held that a jury of five in county court was not a jury pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 33.01 and Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 62.301. The court further found that in the absence of a written waiver, appellant's mere participation in a trial without a full jury did not constitute a valid waiver of his right to trial by jury. The court remanded for a new trial and held that a new trial would not be an infringement of appellant's right against double jeopardy because appellant was still in the initial jeopardy proceeding in which an error had been found.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction and sentence for misdemeanor assault because a jury of fewer than six jurors in county court was not a jury trial, and appellant had never signed a waiver of his right to a jury trial. The court also remanded for a new trial and held that the double jeopardy clause did not preclude the state from retrying appellant's case because the conviction was set aside for an error in the proceedings.

Nowling v. State


No. 14-93-01069-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


909 S.W.2d 121; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2121



August 31, 1995, Rendered  
August 31, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discetionary Review Refused February 14, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 674021. Poe Ted Hon Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle by the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas), claiming that his sentence of 50 years in prison subjected him to cruel and unusual punishment in violation of U.S. Const. amend VIII, Tex. Const. art. 1, § 13, and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.09 (1977).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle, and after ascertaining that he had previously been convicted of two prior felonies, was sentenced to 50 years in prison. He appealed his conviction and sentence, claiming that the sentence subjected him to cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amend. VIII, Tex. Const. art. 1, § 13, and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.09 (1977). He claimed that the revision was unconstitutional. The prosecution argued that defendant waived his right to appeal because he never preserved the issues for appeal. The court in affirming the conviction and sentence decided to consider the issues anyway. It held that defendant was neither subjected to cruel and unusual punishment under the constitutions nor under the court rules. It reasoned that under the habitual offender statute, Tex. Penal Code § 12.42(d), a defendant who had two prior enumerated felonies and who was then convicted of a state jail felony should have been punished in accordance with the habitual offender statute, and would then be subjected to the same punishment as defendant received.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence of 50 years in prison for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle because defendant's sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment and defendant, who met the requirements for sentencing under the habitual offender statute, would have been subjected to the same punishment range had the trial court sentenced him under the habitual offender statute.

Morgan v. State


NO. 2-93-013-CR, NO. 2-93-014-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


906 S.W.2d 620; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2162



August 31, 1995, Decided  
August 31, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled October 19, 1995. Appellant's Petiton for Discretionary Review Refused January 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW OF PARKER COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. FRED M. BARKER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged his conviction from the County Court at Law of Parker County (Texas) for the offense of possession of marijuana weighing less than two ounces.


OVERVIEW: Appellants jointly challenged their convictions for the offenses of possession of marijuana which arose out of a routine traffic stop for a speeding violation Police opened the door of the pickup truck in which appellants were traveling, without consent, in an attempt to obtain the VIN, after an unsuccessful attempt to read the only partially visible VIN located on the dashboard of the pickup. The court affirmed the conviction and held that Tex. Const. art. I, § 9 did not provide greater protection than U.S. Const. Amend. IV, under which it had been held that occupants of a car did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy in either the VIN located on the dashboard or interior doorjamb when stopped for a traffic violation. The court held that the jury instruction given on the VIN search was thus also proper and that appellants' challenge to the jury panel was not supported by written affidavit as required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Art. 35.07, thus not preserved for review, nor was it not shown that the noncompliance compromised the fairness of his trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment and held that that occupants of a car did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy in either the VIN located on the dashboard or interior doorjamb when stopped for a traffic violation and that appellants' challenge to the jury panel was not supported by written affidavit, thus not preserved for review, nor was it not shown that the noncompliance compromised the fairness of his trial.

Texas Dep't of Pub. Safety v. Raffaelli


No. 06-95-00054-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


905 S.W.2d 773; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2092


August 18, 1995, Submitted  
August 30, 1995, Decided  
August 30, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 102nd Judicial District Court. Bowie County, Texas. Trial Court No. 95CO318-102.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, and judgment here RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state department of public safety challenged the judgment of the 102nd Judicial District Court of Bowie County (Texas), which reversed an administrative decision upholding the suspension of appellee's driver's license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state department of public safety automatically suspended appellee's driver's license because of his refusal to submit to a breath test and the lower court reversed the administrative decision upholding the suspension of appellee's driver's license. The court reversed the lower court and held that there was substantial evidence in the agency record to support the administrative order suspending appellee's driver's license. Further, it held that a reviewing court could not substitute its judgment as to the weight of the evidence for that of the state agency. The court further held that appellant's findings and conclusions, made on a preprinted form, satisfied their overall purpose, to inform the parties and the courts of the basis for the agency's decision so that the parties could intelligently prepare an appeal, and so that the courts could properly exercise their reviewing function.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment because there was substantial evidence in the agency record to support the administrative order suspending appellee's driver's license and the findings and conclusions on the preprinted form satisfied their overall purpose, to present the basis for the agency's decision so parties could intelligently prepare an appeal and courts could properly exercise their reviewing function.

Gibson v. Barbe


Appeal No. 04-95-00092-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


907 S.W.2d 646; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2601



August 30, 1995, Delivered  
August 30, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion For Rehearing Denied October 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 224th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 94-CI-09817. Honorable Michael Peden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chief of police challenged summary judgment granted by the 224th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), in favor of appellee police officer in appellee's action seeking to force appellant to promote him to fill a vacancy pursuant to Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 143.036(e) (1988) and § 143.036(f) (Supp. 1995), following the felony conviction of a police sergeant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant chief of police challenged summary judgment granted for appellee police officer in appellee's action seeking to force appellant to appoint him to fill a vacancy on the force pursuant to Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 143.036(e) (1988) and § 143.036(f) (Supp. 1995), following the felony conviction of a police sergeant. Appellee contended that a vacancy occurred when the police sergeant's conviction for a felony was entered. Appellant claimed that the vacancy did not occur until an agreed order was entered dismissing the sergeant's appeal of his removal from the police force. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling that pursuant to Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 415.058(a) (1988), the sergeant's felony conviction created an automatic vacancy because a convicted felon was disqualified from being an officer. Since an eligibility list existed on the date, and since appellee's name was on it, and given that appellant admitted that he would have promoted appellee had a vacancy existed at that time, the court held that appellant should have done so. Summary judgment for appellee was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for appellee police officer affirmed because the law provided that if an eligibility list existed on the date a vacancy occurred the vacancy was to be filled from the list within 60 days after the date the vacancy. A felony conviction of a sergeant created an automatic vacancy, appellee's name was on the list at the time, and appellant chief of police admitted that he would have promoted appellee had a vacancy existed.

Chandler v. Jorge A. Gutierrez, P.C.


NO. 03-94-00683-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


906 S.W.2d 195; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2093



August 30, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled October 11, 1995. Released for Publication October 11, 1995. Application for Writ of Error Denied March 21, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 94-04627, HONORABLE JOHN K. DEITZ, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insured sought review of the summary judgment entered in the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District (Texas), in favor of appellee receiver of an insolvent insurance company, which found that appellant failed to timely file a proof of claim with the receiver although the claims were unknown and could not have been known until after the filing deadline had passed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insured was issued a series of occurrence liability policies that covered claims asserted after the policy periods expired, as long as appellant's acts or omissions gave rise to an occurrence during the covered policy periods. The insurer was designated an "impaired insurer" subject to the Texas Property and Casualty Guaranty Act (Guaranty Act), Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.28-C (1995), and appellee receiver was appointed by court order. Appellee notified appellant that all claims against the insurer had to be filed by September 30, 1989. A number of former patients sued appellant in 1991 and 1992 alleging injuries whose occurrence dates fell within coverage. Appellee rejected this proof of claim as being filed after the filing deadline. The trial court affirmed appellee's determination. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, concluding that article 21.28 did not authorize extension of the filing deadline for equitable reasons, it only provided for the filing of know claims, and that appellee was required to apply the same filing deadline to all claims presented to it to assure some degree of finality in the liquidation proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, concluding that appellant insured's claim was barred, as a matter of law, under the claims filing deadline provisions and under the Guaranty Act, and that appellant's procedural and substantive due process guarantees were not violated since the obligations due to appellant under his contract with the insurer were not impaired by the constitutionally valid receivership court order.

City of Sherman v. Henry


No. 05-94-00055-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


910 S.W.2d 542; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2890



August 28, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted August 28, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 366th District Court. Grayson County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-0720.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part, REVERSED in part and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On rehearing, appellant sought review of the summary judgment rendered in the 366th District Court, Grayson County (Texas), in favor of appellee public employee that reversed the decision of the civil service commission upholding the police chief's refusal to promote appellant based solely on off-duty, private, legal sexual conduct, a decision that did not constitute a valid reason pursuant to Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 143.036(f) (1995).


OVERVIEW: Appellee was ranked first on the list of candidates who were eligible for promotion to sergeant. The police chief refused appellee's promotion due to his relationship with a fellow police officer's wife, who was also employed by the police department, on the grounds that appellee would not command respect and trust from other members of the department, and that appellee's promotion would adversely affect the efficiency and morale of the department. The trial court held that as a matter of law appellant had violated appellee's constitutional rights. Reviewing the constitutional question de novo, the court noted that appellee's conduct was legal, that there were no allegations that appellee ever engaged in sexual activity while on duty, that all the witnesses with personal knowledge of the police department testified that the department's morale and discipline had not suffered in the three months after the relationship became common knowledge, and that there were no written regulations or guidelines prohibiting the complained-of conduct that were carefully tailored to meet appellee's specified needs.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment as it related to the constitutional issues was affirmed, as appellee public employee's conduct was protected by the Texas Constitution, and appellant city did not prove it had a compelling governmental interest that could be achieved by no less intrusive, more reasonable means. The trial court's judgment as related to attorney's fees was reversed and remanded as appellant's affidavits raised issues of material fact.

Valentine v. Bessire


No. 01-94-01016


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1974



August 24, 1995, filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 113th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-63547A.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged the judgment of the 113th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor in appellant's suit for medical malpractice. The trial court dismissed the claim on the basis that the two-year statute of limitations provided by the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (1995), had expired.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient brought suit against appellee doctor for medical malpractice. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. The court affirmed the judgment and held that appellant's claim was barred by the statute of limitations. The court also held that because appellant's claims were health care liability claims, they were governed by the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (1995). The court stated that the subject of appellant's claim was appellee's failure to diagnose and treat her, and no course of treatment was established by appellee. The court held that the continuing course of treatment theory did not apply to appellant's claim. The court also held that appellant served a notice of claim on appellee more than two years after her last visit with appellee. The court further held that appellant failed to establish that a fact issue existed as to whether they knew or should have known of appellee's negligence within two years of its occurrence; therefore, the open courts defense did not apply to negate the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing appellant patient's claim against appellee doctor for medical malpractice. Appellant's claim was not filed within the applicable statute of limitations; the continuing course of treatment theory did not apply because no course of treatment was established; and open courts defense did not apply because appellant did not show a question of fact as to whether she knew or should have known of negligence.

Love v. State


No. 08-92-00365-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


909 S.W.2d 930; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2000



August 24, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 7, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 210th District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 33224). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Virgil Mulanax, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by jury verdict in the 210th District Court of El Paso County (Texas) for the offense of murder and the assessment of life imprisonment. Appellant contended that jury instructions were erroneous, and that the trial court erred in not having found appellant insane.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction, by jury, for the offense of murder and the punishment of life imprisonment. The court affirmed. The inclusion of a parole law instruction to the jury at the punishment stage was not error because the trial judge admonished the jury not to consider the parole laws as applied to appellant. The trial judge's instruction regarding a deadlock was supported by extensive authority and was not coercive. The court upheld the jury's rejection of appellant's insanity defense because the issue of insanity was within the province of the jury. While appellant presented extensive medical evidence concerning his schizophrenia, the state presented medical evidence contradicting that testimony. Appellant's objections to testimony by the state regarding his post-arrest silence, which he previously allowed into evidence, was without merit on appeal. Appellant was not denied a speedy trial because the delay was due to appellant's own agreement that he was incompetent to stand trial until a date when he agreed to an order of competency. The trial court did not err in admitting a medical opinion that was based on information provided by appellant's sisters.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for murder and punishment of life imprisonment. The trial judge did not err in instructing the jury on a parole law because a curative instruction was issued. The issue of insanity was within the province of the jury, and testimony pertaining to appellant's post-arrest silence was already introduced by appellant. The delay in trial was due to appellant's lack of competency.

Houston Indep. Sch. Dist. v. Plexchem Int'l


No. 14-94-00417-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2016



August 24, 1995, Rendered  
August 24, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 113th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89-53392.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, school district, city, and county appraisal district, challenged a decision from the 113th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted appellee domestic exporter's motion for summary judgment and held that ad valorem property tax appraisals made by appellant county appraisal district on goods appellee stored in a Customs Bonded warehouse were unconstitutional, in violation of the Commerce Clause and the Import-Export Clause.


OVERVIEW: Appellee domestic exporter claimed that a tax assessment on property it stored in a United States Customs Bonded warehouse violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, the Import-Export Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 2, and the doctrine of federal preemption. Appellee brought an action against appellants, a school district, a city, and a county appraisal district. The lower court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment on the issue of the constitutionality of the assessment, and declared the tax assessment to be unconstitutional. On appeal, the decision was reversed and remanded. The appellate court applied a six-prong test and determined that no violation of the Commerce Clause existed. The appellate court applied a three-prong test and determined that the import-export tax was constitutional. The appellate court held that appellant county appraisal district was authorized to domestically tax manufactured goods held in a Customs Bonded warehouse awaiting export to a foreign country, without violating the federal preemption doctrine.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment in appellee domestic exporter's favor, on the unconstitutionality of appellant county appraisal district's imposition of ad valorem taxes upon property appellee stored in a Customs Bonded warehouse, was reversed and remanded. The appellate court held that the tax did not violate the Commerce Clause, the Import-Export Clause, or the federal preemption doctrine.

Owen v. State


No. 10-94-322-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


905 S.W.2d 434; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1960



August 23, 1995, delivered  
August 23, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 220th District Court. Bosque County, Texas. Trial Court # 94-06-11766-BCCR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order the 220th District Court, Bosque County (Texas), which convicted appellant of involuntary manslaughter after allowing the state to introduce appellant's videotape conversation with an officer, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22, § 5 (1995), and charging the jury on the two types of driving while intoxicated offenses under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 49.01 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was driving an automobile and was involved in a collision in which a young boy riding a bicycle was killed. During the investigation the officer had a videotaped conversation with appellant at the scene. Appellant was later given Miranda warnings and an intoxilyzer test at the jail. Part of the recorded conversation and the results of the test were offered into evidence by the state. Appellant was convicted by a jury of involuntary manslaughter and because she was intoxicated while driving, using a deadly weapon. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that there was no abuse of discretion by the trial court in finding that the recorded statement by appellant was voluntary and not the result of custodial interrogation and it was therefore admissible pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22, § 5 (1995). The court further held that the trial court did not err in charging the jury on the two types of driving while intoxicated offenses under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 49.01 (1994), and that an automobile could be considered a deadly weapon in an involuntary manslaughter conviction arising out of the operation of a motor vehicle while intoxicated.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for involuntary manslaughter with a deadly weapon was affirmed because the court held that her recorded statement was voluntary and not the result of custodial interrogation, that it was not error to charge on the two types of driving while intoxicated, and that an automobile could constitute a deadly weapon where a death resulted from the operation of a motor vehicle while intoxicated.

City of San Antonio v. Rankin


Appeal No. 04-95-00385-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


905 S.W.2d 427; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2263



August 23, 1995, Delivered  
August 23, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 45th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 95-CI-01752. Honorable Charles Gonzalez, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: ORDER GRANTING TEMPORARY INJUNCTION AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a temporary injunction order by the 45th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which enjoined appellants from enforcing appellant's Ordinance 80329, its' ethics ordinance, which required appellees, district fire chiefs, to file annual financial disclosure statements with the city clerk.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city passed an ethics ordinance (ordinance), San Antonio Ordinance 80329, which required appellee district fire chiefs to file annual financial disclosure statements and annual financial involvement records with the city clerk. Violation of the ordinance was a Class C misdemeanor. Appellees filed a suit for declaratory and injunctive relief. The trial court granted a temporary injunction that ordered the appellant to desist and refrain from requiring appellees to file the financial disclosure forms pending trial on the merits. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the court had jurisdiction because the application of the ordinance interfered with appellees constitutional right to privacy. The court further held that there was no abuse of discretion on the part of the trial court in that appellees showed a probable right to recovery and the temporary injection was necessary to preserve the status quo pending trial on the merits.


OUTCOME: The temporary injunction was affirmed enjoining appellant city from disciplining or prosecuting appellees, district fire chiefs, for failing to file financial disclosure forms pending the trial on the merits. The court held that the ordinance would interfere with appellees right of privacy, the appellees proved a probable right of recovery, and that the order was necessary to preserve the status quo.

 

1106 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


City of Garland v. Allen


No. 05-94-01374-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3404



August 18, 1995, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 116th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-5057-F.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, Remanded in part, Affirmed in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the 116th District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which granted summary judgment seeking mandamus relief in favor of appellee police officer and granted summary judgment to the state, and denied appellants' amended motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city asserted that appellee police officer's appeal of his suspension was untimely and improper. The trial court granted appellee's summary judgment motion seeking mandamus relief, and appellant sought review. The court reversed a portion of the trial court's judgment granting mandamus relief to appellee and summary judgment to the state, but affirmed the judgment in all other respects. The court found that appellee's notice of appeal was not untimely, as his interlocutory partial summary judgment merged into the final judgment; thus, appellee's partial summary judgment was proper. However, in the absence of an affidavit or a properly authenticated exhibit, appellee was not entitled to summary judgment. The court held that the trial court improperly granted the state's summary judgment declaring Tex. Local Gov't Code Ann. § 143.057(d) (1988) unconstitutional, as there was no constitutional challenge at the time that the state's summary judgment was heard. Appellant waived error in the trial court's denial of its amended summary judgment motion, and in the denial of its motion to strike the state's intervention, as it did not cite authorities to support its point.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in part and granted mandamus relief to appellee police officer because his administrative appeal was timely, entitling him to partial summary judgment. The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the state, as there was no constitutional challenge at the time that the state's summary judgment was heard. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in all other respects.

Povolish v. Bethania Regional Health Care Ctr.


NO. 2-94-260-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


905 S.W.2d 66; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1876



August 17, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 30TH DISTRICT COURT OF WICHITA COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Robert Brotherton.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, children of decedent, sought review of a decision of the 30th District Court of Wichita County (Texas), that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee health care providers, claiming that the statute of limitation provision of the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4950i, § 10.01, violated the due process clause and the equal protection clause of the state constitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, children of decedent, filed suit against appellee health care providers. They alleged medical malpractice resulting in the wrongful death of decedent. Appellees moved for summary judgment, alleging that the statute of limitations under the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4950i, § 10.01, barred the action. Summary judgment was granted. Appellants challenged on the grounds that the Act violated the due process clause, Tex. Const. art. 1, § 19, and the equal protection clause, Tex. Const. art. 1, § 3. The court affirmed the judgment. The two-year limitations period did not violate due process because it was reasonable in relation to the stated purposes of the Act. Further, the court held the limitations period, as applied to minors, did not violate equal protection, but only in order to be consistent with controlling precedent. The court noted that section 10.01 had been ruled unconstitutional as to minors bringing suit for their own personal injuries and stated its agreement with another appellate court that minors who had lost a parent due to the same type of negligence should be equally deserving of protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of appellee health care providers in a medical malpractice suit, holding that the statute of limitations period for bringing medical malpractice claims did not violate the due process clause of the state constitution because it was reasonable. Furthermore, the statute of limitation did not violate the equal protection clause of the state constitution because controlling precedent required such holding.

Morris v. Collins


No. 01-94-00950-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


916 S.W.2d 527; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1917



August 17, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 278th District Court. Walker County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 18,515-C. JERRY SANDEL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Finding no reversible error, we affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the order from the 278th District Court, Walker County, Texas, which dismissed his lawsuit regarding the Texas Department of Criminal Justice's (TDCJ) grooming standards against appellee executive director of the TDCJ.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate brought suit and contended that the Texas Department of Criminal Justice's (TDCJ) grooming standards were unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed with prejudice appellant's suit against appellee executive director of the TDCJ because it was frivolous under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001. Appellant contended that the policy violated his equal protection rights and that the grooming policy caused him to lose his individuality and self-esteem because he was not able to grow his hair in a way that flattered him to compensate for hereditary hair loss. The court concluded that the grooming regulation which forbid long hair and challenged by appellant was reasonably related to the legitimate penological interests of security, allocation of resources, and health and safety, and was therefore valid. The court held that the cause of action was frivolous because the claim had no arguable basis in law and the dismissal was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Trial court's dismissal of appellant inmate's action was affirmed because there was no arguable basis in law for his claim that the grooming policy violated his equal protection rights.

McGee v. State


No. 01-91-00862-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


923 S.W.2d 605; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1932



August 17, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 240th District Court. Fort Bend County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 22,125. THOMAS R. CULVER, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 240th District Court, Fort Bend County (Texas), that convicted him of burglary of a building and assessed punishment of 25-years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for burglary of a building, and his sentence of 25-years confinement. He contended that the trial court erred in refusing to dismiss the venire after a prospective juror stated that she knew appellant had prior convictions, that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction for burglary because the state did not prove intent, and that the instruction to the jury on parole and the effect of good conduct under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (1995) was unconstitutional under Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 13 and 19. The court found that appellant was not forced to accept a juror who was prejudicially influenced by any comments, and he failed to show harm arising from the juror's remark. A rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant entered the house with the intent to commit theft. Because Tex. Const. art. IV was amended to permit the legislature to enact laws that required or permitted courts to inform juries about the effect of good conduct time and eligibility for parole, the reenactment of article 37.07 was constitutional. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant of burglary of a building and assessed punishment of 25-years confinement because appellant failed to show harm, the state proved the element of intent in the crime, and the amendment to the statute that allowed instruction to the jury on parole and good conduct was constitutional.
