McGee v. State


Nos. 01-93-01091-CR, 01-93-01092-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


923 S.W.2d 627; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1939



August 17, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-17717 & 93-39468. JOSEPH TERRACINA, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed.

For Appellant: JOHN B. HOLMES, JR., ROGER A. HASEMAN, HOUSTON, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claiming error in the denial of his motions to dismiss the informations, appellant, employee of septic tank cleaner company, sought review of the decision of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12, Harris County (Texas), that found him guilty of violating Tex. Water Code Ann. §§ 26.2121(a), 26.2121(d) (1995) and sentenced him to four days in jail and a fine in each case.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, employee of septic tank cleaner company, pleaded no contest to violating Tex. Water Code Ann. §§ 26.2121(a), 26.2121(d) (1995). He was sentenced to four days in jail and a fine in each case. Appellant claimed the trial court erred by denying his motions to dismiss the informations because both alleged that he discharged industrial waste into and adjacent to water in the state, and a sanitary sewer line was not within the statutory definition of "water in the state." He also claimed that §§ 26.2121(a), 26.2121(d), and 26.121(a)(1) were unconstitutionally vague because he was not able to know in advance from the written statute that his act was criminal. On appeal, the court applied precedent in interpreting the definition of "water in the state." The court held that appellant's discharge into a sanitary sewer line was a discharge into "water in the state" under Tex. Water Code Ann. § 26.211. By pleading no contest, appellant admitted the information allegations that he discharged industrial waste without a required permit. There was no evidence that appellant was confused about the meaning of any statute or unable to comply with it. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that sentenced appellant to four days in jail and a fine for violating the Texas Water Code because appellant's discharge into a sanitary sewer line was a discharge into "water in the state"; by pleading no contest, appellant admitted the information allegations that he discharged industrial waste without a required permit.

Harris County Appraisal Dist. v. Herrin

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON

August 17, 1995, Filed

DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged a decision of the 125th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which ruled for appellee property owners in a de novo hearing on an ad valorem property tax valuation despite the fact that appellees had not paid the taxes due before they became delinquent as required under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08(b) (1992).

The court further held that appellees' argument that § 42.08(b) was unconstitutional under Tex. Const. art. OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of appellee property owners in their de novo review of an ad valorem property tax valuation made by appellant county, and rendered judgment in favor of appellant. Appellees had not paid any part of the taxes prior to the delinquency date and the trial court, therefore, no longer had subject matter jurisdiction over the case.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a Florida corporation that dispensed contact lenses by mail at discount prices, challenged the summary judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District (Texas), in favor of appellee state of Texas, in appellant's suit for declaratory and injunctive relief with respect to Texas Optometry Act, Tex. Campbell v. State


Nos. 01-94-00261-CR, 01-94-00262-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1727



August 3, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 11, 1995. Certiorari Denied May 20, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 3295.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 344th District Court. Chambers County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 7891 & 7892.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the 344th District Court, Chambers County (Texas) that denied appellant's motion to suppress evidence and convicted appellant of aggravated possession of cocaine and failure to pay a controlled substance tax.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for aggravated possession of cocaine and failure to pay a controlled substance tax. Appellant's motion to suppress evidence was denied by the trial court. Appellant then entered a plea of nolo contendere to both charges. The trial court convicted appellant as charged. The controlled substance tax was not facially defective and various arguments of appellant were not jurisdictional in nature, and thus were waived on appeal. A plea of guilty without a plea bargain agreement waived review of a pretrial motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's drug convictions, holding that a plea of guilty without a plea bargain agreement waived review of a pretrial motion to suppress. The controlled substance tax was not facially defective and various arguments of appellant were not jurisdictional in nature, thus waived.

Bridgewater v. State


NO. 2-94-077-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


905 S.W.2d 349; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1749



August 3, 1995, decided  
August 3, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NUMBER TWO OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. LEE ANN DAUPHINOT.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the trial court's judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction and sentence of life confinement for capital murder entered upon a jury verdict in the Criminal District Court Number Two of Tarrant County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of capital murder and the trial court sentenced him to life confinement. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed. After viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the verdict, the court found sufficient evidence existed to connect appellant to the murder and to support the jury's verdict. Additionally, the court found that evidence regarding appellant's membership in a street gang constituted very probative evidence because it showed the witness's potential bias or motive in refusing to testify against appellant and in claiming that neither he nor appellant participated in the robbery and murder in spite of his previous testimony and guilty plea at his own trial. Furthermore, the prejudicial effect of the evidence was limited by the two instructions from the trial court to the jury to consider the evidence only for impeachment purposes. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion. Finally, after examining all the evidence from trial, the court found the state did present enough evidence to raise the issue of the law of parties. Accordingly, the trial court did not err in charging the jury on the law of the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence of life confinement for capital murder. The court found sufficient evidence existed to connect appellant to the murder and to support the jury's verdict. The court also found the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the state's questions concerning a street gang. Further, sufficient evidence existed to support submitting a charge to the jury on the law of the parties.

Appling v. State


NUMBER 13-93-334-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


904 S.W.2d 912; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1786



August 3, 1995, delivered  
August 3, 1995, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused December 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 347th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the 347th District Court of Nueces County (Texas) for third degree felony theft under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a) for intentionally and knowingly appropriating liquor, valued between $ 750 and $ 20,000, from the liquor store without the owner's consent and with the intent to deprive the owner of the liquor.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant of third degree felony theft under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a) for intentionally and knowingly appropriating liquor, valued between $ 750 and $ 20,000, from a liquor store without the owner's consent and with the intent to deprive the owner of the liquor. As appellant was "unavailable," the court held that his unwarned, unrecorded, voluntary oral statements made to a Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission agent with regard to cases of liquor found in the bed of his truck were admissible as an exception to the hearsay rule, Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 806, and were properly admitted for impeachment of his credibility as a witness, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22(5). The court held the liquor was properly confiscated without a warrant, Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. art. 103.03(1), as appellant did not have the requisite transportation statement and failed to invoke the personal consumption exception, Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 107.08. Finally, appellant failed to meet his burden that the identity of a confidential informant should have been disclosed, Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 508(c).


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was affirmed because unwarned, voluntary statements of appellant were properly admitted, as an exception to the hearsay rule, for purposes of impeaching appellant's credibility as a witness; appellant failed to invoke and prove the personal consumption exception; and appellant failed to meet his burden to compel the identification of the confidential informant.

 

1116 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Contico Int'l v. Alvarez


No. 08-95-00060-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


910 S.W.2d 29; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1795



August 3, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted for Withdrawn Opinion of July 13, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1606.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator corporations sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent judge to vacate an order denying relators' motion to disqualify lawyer and law firm from representing plaintiffs in current pending litigation. Relators further sought to compel the trial court to substitute an order disqualifying law firm.


OVERVIEW: Lawyer represented plaintiffs in the civil suit underlying the mandamus action. He was accused of stealing relator corporations' investigation file. Relators sought sanctions, and a hearing was held where lawyer appeared with counsel. When he was asked what he possessed and how he obtained it, he refused to answer, claiming that to do so would expose him to criminal liability. The court held that opposing counsel and the trial court sought and were entitled to an accounting of lawyer's use of the public trust bestowed on him. This trust obligated him to respond to the accusations leveled against him, and the trial court should have imposed some meaningful penalty on him for his refusal to do so. On these facts, mandamus will lie to correct the trial court's misapplication of the law to the facts. The court conditionally granted the writ of mandamus and ordered respondent to rescind his order to the extent that it did not disqualify law firm from representing plaintiffs in the underlying suit and did not sanction lawyer. The court further ordered that respondent issue an order disqualifying law firm from representing plaintiffs in the underlying suit and sanctioning lawyer.


OUTCOME: The court granted relator corporations a conditional writ of mandamus. The court ordered respondent to rescind his order to the extent that it did not disqualify law firm from representing plaintiffs in the underlying suit and did not sanction lawyer.

City of Garland v. Hunter & Assocs.


No. 05-94-01620-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3576



July 31, 1995, Opinion filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 14th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-09521-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed from the 14th District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant architects. Defendants argued that summary judgment was proper because the suit was untimely filed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff appealed a summary judgment granted in favor of defendant architects. Plaintiff contended that the statute of repose was unconstitutional. Plaintiff additionally asserted that the Deceptive Trade Practices Act claims were not barred by the statute of repose. Plaintiff claimed that fact issues existed on whether defendant fraudulently concealed defects in the design of a waste water measuring system, committed constructive fraud in connection with the system, or was negligent in designing the system. The reviewing court affirmed summary judgment for defendant. Plaintiff did not raise the constitutionality of the statute of repose in its response to defendant's motion for partial summary judgment and waived raising the issue on appeal. The court found that the discovery rule did not apply to the statute of repose. Thus, to avoid being barred by the statute, plaintiff was required to file any claims it had against defendant for the 1977 design no later than September 1988. Because plaintiff failed to institute the suit within 10 years of completion of the 1977 system, the trial judge properly granted summary judgment in favor of defendant.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of defendant architects was affirmed. Because plaintiff city failed to institute suit against defendant within 10 years of completion of the system at issue, the court concluded that the trial judge properly granted summary judgment in favor of defendant.

Godoy v. State


No. 01-94-00073-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1670



July 27, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 184th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 670452.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a ruling of the 184th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was contacted by a friend who had just been asked to leave a party by decedent and the friend asked defendant to help solve the problem. Defendant and his accomplice went back to the scene of the party and witnesses testified that defendant shot decedent in the chest at close range before the accomplice also fired a shot in decedent's direction. Defendant admitted to family members that he had killed someone and was convicted of murder after decedent expired from a single gunshot wound to the chest. Defendant appealed his conviction and the court affirmed. The court held that sufficient evidence existed to convict defendant of murder either as the principal or as a party to the murder. The indictment included murder charges against defendant as principal and as a party and the court found that this failure to specify in which capacity it was alleged that defendant acted was allowed under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 7.01(c)(1994).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court ruling, which convicted defendant or murder, and held that the evidence presented was more than sufficient to support defendant's murder conviction as a principal, or as a party to the murder, both of which were charged in defendant's indictment.

 

1120 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Edmond


NO. 2-94-344-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


903 S.W.2d 856; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1646



July 20, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted November 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 89TH DISTRICT COURT OF WICHITA COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. JUANITA PAVLICK.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution sought review of the order from the 89th District Court of Wichita County (Texas) quashing an indictment against appellee which had alleged that appellee committed the offense of official oppression.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was indicted for the offense of official oppression pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 39.02. The indictment included four separate paragraphs. The lower court granted appellee's motion to quash the indictment, and the prosecution sought review. The prosecution alleged that it was improper to find the indictment defective. The question before the court was whether the face of the indictment set forth in plain and intelligible language sufficient information to enable appellee to prepare his defense. The court found that paragraphs one and three of the indictment failed to adequately notify appellee of the charges he must defend against and they did not sufficiently enable him to plead any resulting judgment to bar further prosecution for the same offense. Paragraph two of the indictment was defective because it failed to allege what purported mistreatment was unlawful or that appellee knew the purported mistreatment was unlawful. The fourth paragraph was defective because it failed to give appellee notice of the manner and means of his alleged criminal acts and failed to define several key terms. Thus, the court affirmed the order dismissing the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order quashing the indictment against appellee after finding that the lower court correctly granted appellee's motion to quash because the indictment failed to adequately notify appellee of the charges he must defend against nor did the indictment sufficiently enable appellee to plead any resulting judgment to bar further prosecution for the same offense.

 

1121 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Salinas v. CMMC


NO. 03-94-00685-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


903 S.W.2d 138; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1641; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,283



July 19, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled August 16, 1995. Released for Publication August 16, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 368TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 93-189-C368, HONORABLE BURT CARNES, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of an order of the District Court of Williamson County, 368th Judicial District, Texas, that dismissed his case against appellee foreign corporation for lack of jurisdiction. Appellant's suit regarded injuries incurred while using an allegedly defective winepress that was shipped by appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was injured while using a winepress that was shipped to the forum state by appellee foreign corporation. Appellant sought damages and the trial court dismissed the case for want of jurisdiction over appellee. On review, the court noted that a nonresident appellee that was contesting jurisdiction bore the burden of proof to negate all bases of personal jurisdiction alleged by appellant. Personal jurisdiction could be asserted over a nonresident corporate defendant that had minimum contacts with the state such that the maintenance of the suit did not offend traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice. The court found that appellee had sufficient minimum contacts with the state to protect appellee from unfair surprise. Appellee placed the press into the stream of commerce and shipped it directly to the forum state. Appellant was a state resident and the state had great interest in protection of its resident's right s against a manufacturer of an allegedly defective product. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court that dismissed appellant employee's action against appellee foreign corporation for injuries incurred while using a winepress. Appellee had sufficient minimum contacts with the state to protect it from unfair surprise and the interests of the forum state in protecting its consumers ensured that traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice were not compromised.

 

1122 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Zuliani v. State


NO. 03-92-00110-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


903 S.W.2d 812; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1540



July 12, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled August 16, 1995. Released for Publication August 16, 1995. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 29, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 102,693, HONORABLE MACE B. THURMAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of conviction for intentional and knowing causing bodily harm to a child younger than 14 under Tex. Penal Code § 22.04(a), in appellee state's favor, in the 147th Judicial District Court for Travis County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for intentionally and knowingly causing bodily harm to a child younger than 14 under Tex. Penal Code § 22.04(a), based on the contention his confession was inadmissible due to lack of voluntariness. The court reversed appellant's conviction concluding that error existed in both the admission of extraneous offense evidence and in the admission of a confession extracted through police psychological and physical coercion. The court explained that appellee state's witnesses established that the confession was the product of a custodial interrogation where appellant was yelled at, shoved against a wall, and lifted off the ground. The court determined a sufficient break did not exist between the undisputed coercion and the confession. The court explained that it was unable to conclude that the admission of the confession was harmless when it was emphasized by appellee in support of witness corroboration by an admitted liar. The court reasoned it could not conclude the confession did not contribute to the conviction under such circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for intentional and knowing causing of bodily harm to a child younger than 14 years old because his confession was involuntarily the product of coercion and its admission at trial was not harmless when emphasized by appellee state and pointed to as corroboration for discredited witness testimony.

 

1123 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Gonzalez v. State Bar


Appeal No. 04-94-00438-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


904 S.W.2d 823; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2049



July 12, 1995, Delivered  
July 12, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion For Rehearing Denied August 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 37th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 93-CI-03894. Honorable J. F. Clawson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the judgment from the 37th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) that granted partial summary judgment in favor of appellee state bar in a disciplinary action under the Tex. Disciplinary R. Prof'l. Conduct 7.01(a)(1) and denied appellant's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney challenged the trial court judgment that granted appellee state bar's motion for summary judgment and assessed a public reprimand and costs against appellant for a violation of Tex. Disciplinary R. Prof'l. Conduct 7.01(a)(1). The action was instituted as the result of appellant's solicitation of clients through a letter that stated that the client would incur no "fees" if the suit were unsuccessful. The court affirmed summary judgment, concluding that there was no genuine issue of material fact in dispute with regard to the language regarding his fee. The court held that the letters contained false, misleading and deceptive statements where appellant failed to distinguish between legal fees and costs and to state the amount of his fee as required by Rule 7.01(a)(1), and were misleading to laymen who were unaware of the technical meanings of such terms as fees and costs. The court found that the disclosure requirements of Rule 7.01(a)(1) were reasonably related to the State's interest in preventing deception of consumers and were not violative of appellant's right to commercial free speech or his due process rights guaranteed by the U.S. Const. amend. V and XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee state bar, holding that appellant violated disciplinary disclosure rules by sending a client solicitation letter that was inherently deceptive where it represented that no fees would be incurred in an unsuccessful case without mentioning legal costs, how they were distinct from fees, or stating the amount of his fee.

 

1124 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Messina v. State


No. 05-91-00847-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


904 S.W.2d 178; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1841



July 7, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Appeals. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MC90R0078. Judge Ken Vaughan.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the County Criminal Court of Appeals, Dallas County, Texas, which affirmed the municipal court's conviction and sentence for operating a sexually oriented business in violation of the Dallas, Tex., City Code § 41A-13(a)(4) (1993), a municipal ordinance of appellee city, on the grounds that this ordinance violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 3A, the Texas Equal Rights Amendment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of the county criminal court of appeals judgment that upheld the municipal court's conviction and sentence for operating a sexually oriented business in violation of municipal ordinance, Dallas, Tex., Code § 41A-13(a)(4) (1993). Appellant claimed that the ordinance violated the Texas Equal Rights Amendment (ERA), Tex. Const. art. I, § 3A, because its definition of "state of nudity" treated females differently from males based solely on gender. The court affirmed the criminal court of appeals judgment, finding that the "state of nudity" definition within the ordinance was not facially unconstitutional. The court found that appellee as proponent of the law had rebut the premise that the law discriminated based solely on gender where it had shown in prior cases that physiological and sexual distinctions existed between male and female breasts and that their respective physical characteristics required the gender based distinction. Therefore, the court held that, as a matter of law, the doctrine of stare decisis applied to this question of law and that it was bound by its prior determination that the definition did not violate the ERA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the county court of appeals judgment upholding appellant's conviction and sentence for operating a sexually oriented business in violation of a municipal ordinance of appellee city, because under the doctrine of stare decisis, the ordinance was constitutional and did not violate the Texas Equal Rights Amendment because there were physical characteristics that required the gender based distinctions.

1127 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. State


NO. 12-93-00099-CR, NO. 12-93-00100-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


906 S.W.2d 534; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1608



June 30, 1995, delivered  
June 30, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 114TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. SMITH COUNTY, TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the114th Judicial District Court of Smith County (Texas), which convicted him of two cases of constructive delivery of cocaine and imposed two life sentences to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to his plea of guilty, appellant was convicted of two cases of constructive delivery of cocaine and was sentenced to life imprisonment in both cases, to run concurrently. Appellant argued that the punishment was disproportionate to the crime, and that the lack of sentencing guidelines deprived him of equal protection and due process. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that appellant waived these arguments because he did not raise them in the trial court. The court noted, however, that the trial court assessed punishment within the range set by Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.106 (1994). Because appellant was given numerous chances to change his ways and all attempts at drug rehabilitation had failed, the court held that the sentence was not arbitrary or capricious. Further, the court stated that the sentencing system ensured against arbitrary or capricious assessment of punishment because it allowed appellant to elect whether the trial court or a jury would determine his sentence. Thus, the court held that the sentencing scheme did not violate the U.S. Const. amend. V and XIV or Tex. Const. art. 1, § 19.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of appellant for two cases of constructive delivery of cocaine and imposition of two life sentences to run concurrently, because the sentence was not arbitrary or capricious and was within the range provided by statute and because the sentencing scheme did not violate the equal protection or due process clauses of the U.S. and Texas constitutions.

 

1128 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Cover v. State


NO. 12-93-00323-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


913 S.W.2d 611; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1611



June 30, 1995, delivered  
June 30, 1995, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 11, 1995. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Denied November 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 1ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. SABINE COUNTY, TEXAS. 273RD DISTRICT COURT.



DISPOSITION: Having found no error by the trial court, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the 1st Judicial District Court, Sabine County, Texas, which convicted appellant of retaliation under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.06(a) (1989), and assessed a punishment of 25 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: While in prison for aggravated robbery, appellant wrote a letter to a witness from the trial, asking the witness to recant the testimony. Appellant was convicted of retaliation under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.06(a) (1989). On review sought by appellant, the court affirmed his conviction. The court held that appellant intended to threaten the witness with the letter because appellant used the witness's first name, implied knowledge about the witness's children, and stated that prison hardened the heart. The court found that the indictment was not void for its referral to a prior offense for enhancement purposes because in order for the prior conviction to be used against appellant in connection with the primary offense, the prior conviction had to be alleged in the indictment. The court also ruled that appellant failed to establish an insanity defense by a preponderance of the evidence where a psychologist testified that appellant knew the difference between right and wrong at the time the offense was committed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that convicted appellant of retaliation and assessed a punishment of 25 years in prison because appellant intended to threaten the witness in the letter, the indictment properly contained an allegation of a prior offense for sentence enhancement purposes, and appellant failed to establish the insanity defense.

Ex parte Anderson


NO. 03-94-00688-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


902 S.W.2d 695; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1425



June 28, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Amended June 27, 1995. As Corrected July 12, 1995. Released for Publication August 2, 1995. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 26TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NOS. 94-545-K26, 94-546-K26 & 94-547-K26, HONORABLE BILLY RAY STUBBLEFIELD, JUDGE PRESIDING.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of May 17, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1060.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged order that denied habeas corpus relief from the 26th Judicial District Court of Williamson County (Texas), in a proceeding that attacked the constitutionality of the statute under which he was charged.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was denied relief in pretrial habeas corpus proceeding that attacked the constitutionality of the statute under which he was charged and challenged that order denying relief. The court affirmed the denial of habeas corpus and held that there was a presumption that the statute was valid and a party challenging the constitutionality of a statute had the burden of proof to establish its invalidity. The court held that the indictment alleged an offense as defined by Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.25(b) and the lower court did not err in denying the motion to quash. The court held that appellant had not demonstrated that in its operation, the statute was unconstitutional and had not brought forward the statement of facts from the habeas corpus hearing as required under Tex. R. App. P. 50(d). The court found that Tex. Penal Code Ann § 43.25 was not impermissibly vague and when measured by its common understanding and practices, the statute fairly apprised appellant of the conduct it proscribed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's orders denying habeas corpus relief because appellant had not demonstrated that in its operation, the statute was unconstitutional and had not brought forward the statement of facts from the habeas corpus hearing to preserve the matter for review.

 

1130 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Arredondo ex rel. Arredondo v. Hilliard


Appeal No. 04-94-00376-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


904 S.W.2d 754; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 2053



June 28, 1995, Delivered  
June 28, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied August 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 166th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 94-CI-04459. Honorable John Specia, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother sought review of summary judgments entered in favor of defendants, doctors and hospital, by the 166th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) because plaintiff's wrongful death actions were barred by the statute of limitations pursuant to the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act (MLIIA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1995).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mother, individually and as administratrix, sued defendants, doctors and hospital, alleging that their negligence caused the wrongful death of her newborn son (decedent). The trial court granted summary judgment on each claim based on the statute of limitations in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act (MLIIA), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4095i, § 10.01 (1995). On appeal, plaintiff argued that § 10.01 did not apply, or that if it did, defendants fraudulently concealed the causes of action. Further, plaintiff argued that the statute of limitations were tolled because of the minority of the decedent. The court found that plaintiff's case was founded on a health care liability claim, therefore, the operative limitation period for redress was the one specified by § 10.01 of MLIIA. However, the court also found that the statute of limitation was tolled from the date of the alleged injuries until the date of the minor's death. Therefore, plaintiff was not time-barred from filing the wrongful death claims with regard to her derivative action. Accordingly, the judgments were reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The summary judgments entered in favor of defendants, doctors and hospital, in plaintiff mother's wrongful death actions, were reversed and remanded for trial because the summary judgment evidence failed to show that defendants were entitled to judgment as a matter of law based upon the affirmative defense of limitations.

 

1131 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Richardson v. State


NO. 07-90-0349-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


902 S.W.2d 689; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1449



June 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Richardson v. Stephens, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 101414 (S.D. Tex., June 29, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 364TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 89-410,346; HONORABLE BRADLEY S. UNDERWOOD, JUDGE.

Original Opinion of May 18, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1268.
Richardson v. State, 865 S.W.2d 944, 1993 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 167 (Tex. Crim. App., Oct. 27, 1993)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for the offense of engaging in organized criminal activity of the 364th Judicial District Court of Lubbock County (Texas), on the issue that the installation of a pen register can be a search under Tex. Const. art. I, § 9.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction on the alleged illegality of evidence obtained by the use of a court authorized pen register and wiretap. The court affirmed the conviction and held that appellant had no standing to challenge installation of the pen register because the pen register did not record the origin of appellant's calls and there was no privacy interest in the telephone records of another. The court held that the finding of probable cause to support the wiretap order was not based on evidence obtained from the pen register installed on the telephone, but telephone records authorized by 18 U.S.C.S. § 2703(c)(1)(B)(i). The court held that because appellant's calls were collect and appellant made disclosures of the information to other inmates, appellant had neither a subjective nor objective expectation of privacy in the existence of his calls and he lacked standing to contest the acquisition or use of the billing records used in support of the affidavit for the wiretap order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court and held that appellant had neither a subjective nor objective expectation of privacy in the existence of his calls, and thus he lacked standing to contest the acquisition or use of the billing records used in support of the affidavit for the wiretap order.

 

1132 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Wren v. Texas Employment Comm'n


No. 14-94-00230-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


915 S.W.2d 506; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1387



June 22, 1995, Rendered  
June 22, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 80th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-17824.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employees challenged a judgment from the 80th District Court, Harris County (Texas) in favor of appellee employment commission in their claim for unemployment compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: Appellee employment commission denied appellant employees unemployment compensation benefits for failing to make a reasonable effort to protect their positions while absent due to illness. On appeal, they challenged dismissal of the suit, denial of their requests to amend their petition, and the constitutionality of Tex. Lab. Code Ann. art. 5221b. The court affirmed the denial of benefits because the court lacked jurisdiction to hear the case, and appellants failed to preserve constitutional challenges for review. Appellants dropped their employers as defendants in their second amended pleadings, which superseded the originals. Since the employers were not added within the statutory time limit, the court lacked jurisdiction to grant leave to amend and had to dismiss the suit. Appellants waived their constitutional challenges by not presenting them to the trial court and they could not raise them for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying appellants unemployment compensation benefits was affirmed because the trial court lacked jurisdiction to grant leave to amend their petition and to hear their case, they failed to preserve constitutional challenges for review, they were not denied access to the courts, and their other claims lacked merit.

 

1133 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Gomez v. Carreras


NUMBER 13-94-170-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


904 S.W.2d 750; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1398



June 22, 1995, delivered  
June 22, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 206th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas. (Tr.Ct.No. C-4988-91-D).



DISPOSITION: The trial court's summary judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged the order of the 206th District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor in appellant's suit for medical malpractice. The trial court did not state the grounds upon which the ruling was made.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient filed suit for medical malpractice against appellee doctor. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor without stating the grounds on which the ruling was made. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the record reflected that appellant discovered his injuries well within two years of his last treatment by appellee, and appellant admitted that he discovered his injuries nine months after his last treatment by appellee. The court stated that appellant had 15 months after discovering his injury to have filed suit and still fallen within the two-year limitations period. The court held that appellant's claims were barred by the statute of limitations. The court also held that there was no evidence in the record that raised a fact issue in avoidance of the affirmative defense of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor in appellant patient's claim for medical malpractice because it was barred by the statute of limitations. Appellant had 15 months after discovering his injury to have filed suit and still fallen within the two-year limitations period. There was no evidence in the record that raised a fact issue in avoidance of the affirmative defense of limitations.

 

1134 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Meyer v. Aronoff


No. 05-94-01562-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3575



June 22, 1995, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 14th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-00454-A.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a judgment from the 14th District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which granted appellee physician's motion for summary judgment in appellant's medical malpractice action on the ground that the action was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient brought a medical malpractice action against appellee physician, alleging that she sustained permanent physical and emotional damage as a result of a misdiagnosis and incorrect treatment. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment on the ground that the statute of limitations barred the suit. The court reversed and remanded the judgment, finding that the suit was not barred by the statute of limitations. Although both parties agreed that the statute of limitations began running on the last day of treatment, they disagreed as to the date treatment ended. The court rejected appellee's assertion that treatment ended on the date of appellant's last office visit with appellee. The court held that appellant's telephone conversations with appellee, in which appellee told appellant to continue taking steroids, constituted a course of treatment and thereby extended the treatment period and brought it within the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded summary judgment in favor of appellee physician in appellant patient's medical malpractice action where the trial court erred in determining that the suit was barred by the statute of limitations. The court held that appellant's telephone conversations with appellee constituted a course of treatment, thereby extending the treatment period and bringing it within the statute of limitations.

 

1135 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ruiz Wholesale Co.


NO. 03-93-00618-CV, NO. 03-94-00269-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


901 S.W.2d 772; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1372



June 21, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 2, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 93-11542, HONORABLE MARGARET A. COOPER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in number 03-94-00269-CV; Appeal Dismissed in number 03-93-00618-CV


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commission challenged an order of the 53rd Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas) that granted an injunction sought by appellee distributors. A cross-appeal disputed the trial court's denial of the injunction. The issues were whether the granted injunction was valid, whether the trial court erred in dissolving that injunction, and whether the trial court should have granted a second request for that injunction.


OVERVIEW: Appellee distributors sought to enjoin appellant commission from enforcing Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 102.52, as amended by 1993 Tex. Gen. Laws 3950, 3975. The trial court granted a temporary injunction, which appellant challenged. On rehearing, the trial court dissolved the injunction, which appellees challenged. Appellees then sought a second temporary injunction, which the trial court denied, which denial appellees challenged. On appeal, the court dismissed appellant's challenge. Because the injunction had been dissolved, the appeal was moot, and the court had no jurisdiction to consider it. The court could not review appellees' challenge to the dissolution of the injunction, because they had not timely perfected the appeal. The court affirmed the denial of the second request for the injunction, because appellees asserted no new grounds and circumstances had not changed since the dissolution of the injunction. Further, the trial court had not clearly abused its discretion in denying the second request for the injunction. Even if it were an initial request, appellees had not demonstrated a probable right to recover at trial on the merits and probable injury in the interim.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant commission's challenge, holding that, once the injunction was dissolved, the court had no jurisdiction over it. The court did not consider the cross-appeal as to dissolution of the injunction because it had not been timely brought. The court affirmed as to denial of the second request, holding that the trial court had not clearly abused its discretion, and no new grounds were asserted nor had circumstances changed.

 

1136 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Wilhelm


Nos. 01-94-01084-CR, 01-94-01085-CR, 01-94-01087-CR, 01-94-01088-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


901 S.W.2d 956; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1319



June 15, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 4, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 185th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 9419750, 9419751, 9419752, 9419753. CARL WALKER, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged decisions of the 185th District Court of Harris County (Texas) that denied the relief requested in their pretrial petitions for writs of habeas corpus. At issue was whether the amendment of certain gambling statutes, subsequent to the alleged offense, so as to carry a lighter penalty rendered unconstitutional, as cruel and unusual punishment, the application to appellants of the former statutes carrying a heavier penalty.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were charged with engaging in organized criminal activity consisting of gambling offenses. As an element of the offense, appellants were also charged with the commission of other, predicate offenses. The legislature amended the statutes proscribing the predicate offenses, effective September 1, 1994, downgrading their punishment category from third degree felony to Class A misdemeanor. Appellants and the state agreed that appellants were charged with committing their offenses before September 1, 1994. Appellant filed petitions for writ of habeas corpus challenging the application of the former statutes carrying a heavier penalty. The trial court denied the petitions. The court affirmed, finding that the rule that habeas corpus relief should not be granted when there was an adequate remedy at law should be adhered to when there was good reason to support it. The court held that the good reason in this case was to avoid wasting judicial resources to decide a matter that would not stop the prosecution and might become moot. The court found that if appellants were not convicted, the question of the constitutionality of the old statutory penalties would become moot.


OUTCOME: The trial court's orders denying the relief requested in appellants' petitions for writs of habeas corpus were affirmed on the basis that, even if appellants' points of error were sustained, that would not have stopped the prosecution of their cases. The court followed the general rule that a court should not grant habeas corpus relief when there was an adequate remedy by appeal.

 

1137 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Prater v. State


NO. 2-94-048-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


903 S.W.2d 57; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1272



June 8, 1995, Decided  
June 8, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended July 14, 1995. State's Motion for Rehearing Overruled August 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 4 OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Joe Drago III.



DISPOSITION: Appellant's single point of error is overruled and the judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Criminal District Court No. 4 of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted him of capital murder and imposed a mandatory life sentence after the state waived the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of capital murder. The court affirmed that judgment on appeal. The court found that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.31(a) (1994) did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VIII or Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 13, 19 by imposing an automatic life sentence if the state waived the death penalty in a capital murder case. The court reasoned that having a jury hear the sentencing phase when the death penalty was sought met the requirement of having the jury determine whether any mitigating circumstances warranted a life sentence. The court also held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.071, § 1 (1995) was not unconstitutional for failure to avoid arbitrary and capricious infliction of punishment because the law, not the jury or the judge, predetermined the punishment if the death penalty was waived. The court further found that a mandatory life sentence did not rise to the level of being cruel and unusual punishment. The court additionally ruled that the right to have a jury assess punishment was not constitutionally based.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, finding that imposing an automatic life sentence if the death penalty was waived in a capital murder case did not violate the United States Constitution or the Texas Constitution. The court determined that arbitrary punishment did not occur because the law predetermined the sentence if the death penalty was waived. The court also held that a mandatory life sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment.

 

1138 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Spurlock v. Texas Dep't of Protective & Regulatory Servs.


NO. 03-94-00268-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


904 S.W.2d 152; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1249



June 7, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled September 13, 1995. Released for Publication September 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 479,475, HONORABLE W. JEANNE MEURER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District (Texas), which terminated her parental rights to two children in an action brought by the state under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 15.024 (Supp. 1995), challenging the sufficiency of the evidence and constitutionality of § 15.024.


OVERVIEW: The state, pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 15.024, sought termination of the parental rights of appellant mother, who suffered from a chronic mental illness and the trial court ordered the termination of her parental rights. Appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to support the judgment and contended that § 15.024 violated equal protection by singling out the mentally ill and was unconstitutionally vague by not defining mental illness. On appeal, the court affirmed the termination of appellant's parental rights. The court balanced the needs of the children and the termination, finding that the evidence was factually sufficient to show that appellant was unable to meet the physical, emotional, and mental needs of the children; that in all reasonable probability appellant would not be able to care for the children until they reached 18; and that termination of appellant's parental rights was in the children's best interest. The court held that there was no equal protection violation because § 15.024 was rationally related to the state's legitimate interest in protecting children; and that § 15.024 was not void for vagueness when read in its plain and ordinary meaning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the termination of appellant mother's parental rights; found the evidence factually sufficient to show that she was unable to meet the physical, emotional, or mental needs of her children; unable to care for them until they reached 18 years old; and termination of parental rights was in their best interest; and held that the termination statute was rationally related to the state's legitimate interest in protecting children.

 

1139 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


NO. 09-93-069 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


900 S.W.2d 475; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1301


October 6, 1994, Submitted  
June 7, 1995, Delivered  
June 7, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 253rd District Court. Liberty County, Texas. Cause No. 16,133. Honorable W.G. Woods, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the 253rd District Court, Liberty County, Texas, which sentenced defendant to 60 years in prison and a fine for delivery of a controlled substance, cocaine, in an amount exceeding 400 grams. The sentence was cumulated on a sentence defendant was serving in Virginia. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss under the Interstate Agreement on Detainers, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 51.14 (1979).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's 1986 conviction for delivery of a controlled substance, cocaine, was reversed for a punishment charge error in 1990. In 1993, the trial court refused to dismiss the cocaine indictment under the Interstate Agreement on Detainers (IAD), Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 51.14 (1979), and defendant was sentenced to 60 years in prison. The court affirmed the judgment and sentence. IAD did not apply because no detainer was issued for the cocaine offense and the offense for which a detainer was issued did not arise out of the same transaction. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 44.29(b) (1995) was not an ex post facto law. Art. 44.29(b) was a procedural statute, and procedural statutes applied to both pending and future actions from their effective date. U.S. Const. amend. XIV did not prohibit defendant's increased sentence based on the intervening Virginia conviction after his successful appeal because it was not the result of actual vindictiveness. Cumulation of his sentence with the Virginia sentence under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 4208 did not violate the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws because only the offense predated the 1987 amendments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for delivery of a controlled substance, cocaine. IAD did not apply because no detainer was issued for the cocaine charge. The procedural sentencing statute applied to both pending and future actions from its effective date. The sentence did not result from vindictiveness; cumulation was proper because the amendment allowing cumulation with foreign sentences predated the sentencing hearing.

 

1140 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hays County Appraisal Dist. v. Mayo Kirby Springs


NO. 03-93-00264-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


903 S.W.2d 394; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1248



June 7, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled August 30, 1995. Released for Publication August 30, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HAYS COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-0620, HONORABLE FRED A. MOORE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appraisal district challenged the judgment of the 22nd Judicial District Court, Hays County (Texas), which referred the dispute concerning the market value of appellee property owner's real property to arbitration pursuant to former section Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.225, 1991 Tex. Gen. Laws 1576. The trial court then rendered judgment according to the market value fixed by the arbitrator.


OVERVIEW: Appellee property owner had property that was subdivided into residential lots sold as a trade or business. A dispute arose between appellant appraisal district and appellee concerning the proper method for assessing the market value of this property. Appellee brought an action for a judicial review of the appraisal order issued by appellant and requested arbitration under former Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.225, 1991 Tex. Gen. Laws 1576. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellee as determined by the arbitrator. On appeal, the court held that by purporting to allow the taxpayer to invoke secret proceedings in the appraisal of property for ad valorem tax purposes, former § 42.225 violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court held that former § 42.225 infringed unduly upon the judicial power in violation of the separation of powers principle, and it was an unconstitutional delegation of judicial power implicitly prohibited by Tex. Const. art. V, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which upheld the arbitration award in favor of appellee property owner in an action concerning the market value of appellee's property, and remanded the cause for further proceedings. The court held that the former provision, which permitted a property owner who appealed an appraisal review board order to have the appeal resolved through binding arbitration, was unconstitutional.

 

1141 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Williamson County Appraisal Dist. v. Nootsie, Ltd.


NO. 03-93-00588-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


905 S.W.2d 289; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1250



June 7, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled September 27, 1995. Released for Publication September 27, 1995. As Corrected November 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 26TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 90-320-C26, HONORABLE BILLY RAY STUBBLEFIELD, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board challenged the judgment of the District Court of Williamson County, 26th Judicial District (Texas), which adjudged Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 23.51(1) to be not unconstitutional and directed appellant to grant appellee landowner's classification, in an application to the appraisal review board to classify property as qualified open-space land under § 23.51(1).


OVERVIEW: Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 2 prohibited the appraisal of land, for ad valorem purposes, on any basis other than market value. An amendment excluded from the prohibition qualified open-space lands devoted to agriculture and timber production and applied a new appraisal method. Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 23.51(1) (1978) defined qualified open-space lands to include land used as an ecological laboratory. Appellee landowner filed a suit against appellant board, which denied its application to classify its land as qualified open-space land. Appellant sought to declare § 23.51(1) unconstitutional since its definition added a third class of land, land used as an ecological laboratory, entitled to the new appraisal method. The trial court adjudged the statute constitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and found the statute to be unconstitutional to the extent it purported to remove from market-value appraisal open-space land used as an ecological laboratory and held that the amendment specifically excluded from the prohibition agricultural and timber lands but did not authorize, by implication, the new appraisal method for land used as an ecological laboratory.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, rendered a take-nothing judgment against appellee applicant, and affirmed appellant board's order denying appellee's application. The court found the statute unconstitutional to the extent it purported to remove from market-value appraisal open-space land used as an ecological laboratory since the amendment expressly excluded from market-value appraisal only agricultural and timber lands.

 

1142 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Dorsey v. State


No. 05-93-00900-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3559



June 5, 1995, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 194th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F92-04273-UM.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 194th District Court, Dallas County, Texas, that convicted her of the unlawful possession of food stamps in an amount greater than $ 200, a violation of 1979 Tex. Gen. Laws 2333. The trial court found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded no contest to unlawful possession of food stamps in an amount greater than $ 200, a violation of 1979 Tex. Gen. Laws 2333. Appellant sought review and contended that 1979 Tex. Gen. Laws 2333 was unconstitutionally vague as applied to her. The court affirmed. The court held that where no constitutionally protected right was implicated, the court had to only scrutinize the statute in question to determine whether or not it was impermissibly vague as applied to the challenging party's specific conduct. The court found that people of common intelligence understood the distinction between authorized possession of food stamps and unauthorized possession so as to avoid the prohibited conduct under 1979 Tex. Gen. Laws 2333. The court also found that appellant was aware, inter alia, that she could not trade or sell or improperly possess food stamps. The court determined that 1979 Tex. Gen. Laws 2333 was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant's conduct. The court also determined that the evidence was sufficient to support her conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that, given the statute in question, people of common intelligence understood the distinction between authorized possession of food stamps and unauthorized possession so as to avoid the prohibited conduct. Based on this and appellant's awareness as shown by the evidence, the court found that the statute in question was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant's conduct.

 

1143 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


GM Acceptance Corp v. Harris County Mun. Util. Dist. #130


No. 14-93-01046-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


899 S.W.2d 821; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1214



June 1, 1995, Rendered  
June 1, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 295th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-19916. Downey, Dan Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant automotive credit corporation sought review of a decision of the 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas) that granted appellee municipal appraisal district's motion to dismiss a personal property ad valorem tax appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant automotive credit corporation seized vehicles from an automobile dealership. As of January 1, 1992, appellant was still in possession of the vehicles. Appellee municipal appraisal district determined that appellant was the owner of the vehicles for tax purposes and appraised the vehicles at $ 2.8 million. Appellant challenged the determination to the review board which upheld the appraisal. Appellant timely sought review to the trial court, contending that it was not the owner of the vehicles. The trial court granted appellee's motion to dismiss the appeal because appellant failed to pay the undisputed portion of the taxes per statute. The court affirmed, holding that a property owner who appealed an appraisal to the courts was required to pay the greater of the undisputed amount of taxes or the tax imposed in the preceding year. Failure to do such warranted dismissal of the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant's tax appraisal appeal. The court held that dismissal of appellant's appeal was warranted because a property owner appeal of an appraisal to the courts was required to pay the greater of the undisputed amount of taxes or the tax for the preceding year.

Webb v. State


No. 10-94-237-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


899 S.W.2d 814; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1226



May 31, 1995, delivered  
May 31, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 54th District Court. McLennan County, Texas. Trial Court # 94-20-C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a ruling of the 54th District Court, McLennan County (Texas), which found defendant guilty of possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after his ex-wife contacted police and indicated that defendant had been bothering her in violation of a protective order. The police proceeded to the ex-wife's home and, while there, defendant drove by, which was a violation of the protective order in itself as it forced defendant to come within 200 feet of his ex-wife's residence. When the police saw this, they followed defendant, arrested him, and during a search incident to that arrest discovered methamphetamine on defendant's person. Defendant was convicted of possession of methamphetamine and he appealed that conviction. The court affirmed, and held that defendant waived his challenge to the admission of the methamphetamine evidence by not objecting in the trial court even where defendant's challenge was based on his claim that the statute regarding violating a protective order, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.07(1994), was unconstitutionally vague and, therefore, the evidence was the product of an unlawful arrest. The court found that the officers had probable cause to arrest where three individuals, including the officers, testified that defendant was within 200 feet of his ex-wife's home.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court ruling, which found defendant guilty of possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, and held that defendant waived his challenge to the admission of the methamphetamine evidence where the admission was not objected to in the trial court. The court found that the police had probable cause to arrest defendant when they saw him violate a protective order.

Long v. State


NO. 03-94-00513-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


903 S.W.2d 52; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1546



May 31, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] States's Motion to Publish Granted July 12, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO.3 OF TRAVIS COUNTY. NO. 416-794, HONORABLE DAVID CRAIN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a ruling of the County Court at Law No. 3 of Travis County (Texas), which convicted defendant of harassment in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(7)(1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of harassment in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(7)(1994) after he verbally abused, choked, physically restrained, and abused his prior live in girlfriend on multiple occasions. The last contact at issue between the two came when defendant sat illegally parked outside of his ex-girlfriend's apartment so that he could watch her apartment door. This "watching" incident came after the police had been called to intervene previously and they were again called on this occasion. The police eventually obtained a warrant for defendant's arrest and arrested defendant. Defendant challenged his conviction on multiple grounds and, on appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 42.07(a)(7) was not unconstitutionally vague or overly broad where it adequately defined the criminal conduct which it sought to prevent and provided very specific guidelines for its enforcement. As to defendant's claim that his sitting and watching the victim from his car was not conduct prohibited by the statute, the court disagreed and held that based on the specific facts, there was no question that this conduct was intended to abuse and torment the victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court ruling, which convicted defendant of harassment, and held that the Texas harassment statute not unconstitutionally vague or overly broad.

Burgess v. Jennings


No. 05-94-01054-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


903 S.W.2d 388; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1802



May 31, 1995, Filed, Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied July 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 134th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-5107-G. Name of Judge: Judge Anne Ashby.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, patient and husband, sought review of the judgment of the 134th District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor in a medical malpractice action. Appellee had prevailed on his argument that the action was time-barred.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, patient and husband, sought review of the grant of summary judgment to appellee doctor in their medical malpractice action. Appellant patient's nose was invaded by cancer while she was receiving treatment for a lesion. Appellants contended that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment to appellee because a genuine issue of material fact still existed as to whether appellee should have discovered the cancer within the limitations period. The court concluded that appellee's failure to discover the cancer within the two years he was treating appellant had not left a genuine issue of material fact as to the date the statute began running. Appellants argued that the limitations period did not begin until the date appellant patient was last treated. The court held that because the statute under which the action was filed violated the open courts provision the grant of summary judgment could not stand. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that granted summary judgment to appellee doctor because the statute under which the action had been filed by appellants, patient and husband, violated the open courts provision. The court determined that whether or not appellee doctor should have discovered the cancer within the limitations period did not create a genuine issue of material fact.

Walls v. First State Bank


NO. 07-94-0184-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


900 S.W.2d 117; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1240



May 30, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's and Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Overruled June 26, 1995. As Corrected July 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 223RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF GRAY COUNTY; NO. 28,508; HONORABLE LEE WATERS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of a grant of summary judgment by the 223rd District Court of Gray County (Texas) in favor of appellees, bank and bank employees, in appellant's action alleging malicious prosecution, libel, and slander.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, bank and bank employees, informed the district attorney that appellant debtor committed a criminal act with respect to a promissory note he had executed with the bank. The referral led to an indictment, but the district attorney dismissed the indictment shortly after it was issued because the allegation was false. Appellant filed suit against appellees. alleging malicious prosecution, libel, and slander. Appellees moved for summary judgment claiming that they were immune from suit for reporting the suspected violation pursuant to the Annunzico-Wylie Anti-Money Laundering Act, 31 U.S.C.S. § 5318(g)(3). The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the court first concluded that § 5318(g)(3), which was enacted after appellant's claims accrued, could be applied retroactively because appellant did not have a vested right in his unadjudicated claims. However, the court concluded that § 5318(g)(3) did not insulate bank officials from liability for knowingly making a false report of possible criminal activity and reversed the grant of summary judgment because there were genuine fact issues as to whether appellees knew that their accusation against appellant was false.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees, bank and bank employees, in appellant debtor's action alleging malicious prosecution, libel, and slander because there were genuine issues of material fact as to whether appellees knowingly made a false report to the district attorney accusing appellant of engaging in criminal conduct with regard to a promissory note. The court remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

1148 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Rocha v. State


No. 05-94-00839-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


903 S.W.2d 789; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1798



May 30, 1995, Filed, Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 204th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F91-21475-Q. Name of Judge: Larry Baraka.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for attempted murder by the 204th District Court, Dallas County, Texas. Appellant had pleaded nolo contendere but his adjudication of guilt was deferred until he violated his probation. He challenged the sufficiency of evidence to proceed with adjudication and contended that his lack of a right to appeal violated his constitutional equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: After appellant pleaded nolo contendere to attempted murder, the trial court deferred adjudication of guilt and placed him on probation. On appellee state's motion to adjudicate on the basis of probation violations, the trial court convicted appellant on the original charge and sentenced him to a 20-year prison term. On appeal, the court rejected appellant's claim that there was insufficient evidence for the adjudication on his guilt to proceed because that decision was within the absolute discretion of the trial court and unappealable under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12 § 5(b) (1994). Appellant claimed he was denied his federal and state constitutional rights to equal protection because a regular probationer had the right to appeal. Affirming appellant's conviction, the court held that the state had a legitimate interest to deny a deferred adjudication probationer the right to appeal because it was rationally related to conserving court resources and benefited appellant by giving him the opportunity to avoid conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for attempted murder after the trial court's adjudication of his guilt. Appellant had pleaded nolo contendere to the charge and adjudication was deferred until he violated probation. The court held the decision to adjudicate was unappealable and did not violate appellant's constitutional equal protection rights because it was rationally related to the state's interest in conserving court resources.
