Rathjen v. Rathjen


No. 05-93-00846-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3759



May 30, 1995, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 296th District Court. Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 296-50409-90.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of the decision of the 296th District Court, Collin County (Texas), which found that a pre-marital agreement signed in Hawaii between appellant and appellee wife was not voluntarily executed and was unconscionable.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband and appellee wife signed a pre-marital agreement in Hawaii where they resided. They moved to Texas and appellee subsequently filed for divorce. The trial court found that the pre-marital agreement was not executed voluntarily and that it was unconscionable. The court reversed finding that there was not duress in procuring appellee's signature because the threat that appellee would not get married without her first signing the pre-marital agreement, and cancelling the wedding was a reasonable alternative for not signing the agreement if she did not agree with it. The court found that there was no undue influence evidence presented other than appellee was domineering. The court found under Hawaii law that the agreement was not so disproportionate that it could not enforce it. The court held that a balance sheet was not inadequate to provide financial disclosure and that appellee had adequate knowledge of appellee's financial situation. Thus, the trial court erred in holding the agreement as unconscionable. The agreement was enforceable under Texas law and did not violate Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 16 and was a valid proportionment of their property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court holding that appellant husband did not procure the pre-marital agreement by duress or threat, and that appellee wife could have called off the wedding. The court held that there was adequate disclosure of appellant's financial situation to appellee and that the agreement was not unconscionable.

 

1150 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Singleton v. State


No. 01-94-00590-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1135



May 25, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 20, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 183rd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 646193.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 183rd District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance and sentenced him to 35-years confinement pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.42(d) (1994), and alleged his sentence was cruel and unusual under U.S. Const. amend. VIII; Tex. Const. art I, § 13; and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.09 (1977).


OVERVIEW: After appellant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance, he was sentenced to 35-years confinement with the possibility of parole, after enhancement for two prior convictions. Appellant sought further review, claiming that the length of his prison term constituted cruel and unusual punishment, in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII; Tex. Const. art I, § 13; and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.09 (1977). He relied in part on the fact that possession of less than one gram of cocaine was classified as a state jail felony, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 481.102(3)(D), 115(b) (1994), although at the time he was convicted it was classified as a second degree felony, 1989 Tex. Gen. Laws 2230, 2936. Appellant conceded that his punishment was within the statutory range of punishment for a felony under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.42(d) (1994). On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the enhancement of punishment under § 12.42(d), did not render the punishment unconstitutionally cruel and unusual. The court also found that the sentence was not disproportionate to the offense committed, and that the revised sentencing guidelines were not dispositive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and 35-year prison term, because the enhancement of punishment for two prior felony convictions under the recidivist statute did not make the punishment cruel and unusual. The court also found that the sentence was not disproportionate to the offense committed.

 

1151 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hillman v. State


No. 01-94-00863-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1137



May 25, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 182nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 656635.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 182nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted her of involuntary manslaughter after appellant entered a plea of no contest.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of involuntary manslaughter after pleading no contest without an agreed punishment recommendation from state. Appellant challenged the conviction, attacking the validity of her plea. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1994), was constitutional and did not prohibit appellant from presenting evidence or the trial court from considering such evidence. The court held that when a guilty plea was entered, a defendant must specifically waive the privilege against compulsory self-incrimination, the right to trial by jury, and the right to confront one's accusers. The court held that because the record clearly showed that appellate waived these rights, the trial court could render its judgment after accepting her plea. The court held that a defendant was not required to expressly waive the right to compulsory due process before entering a plea. The court held that appellant's sentence was proportional to the offense committed based upon the gravity of the offense, the harm caused to the victim and society, appellant's culpability, and the harshness of the penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for involuntary manslaughter because the statute pursuant to which the trial court convicted appellant after she entered her plea was constitutional. Appellant did not have to expressly waive her right to compulsory due process before pleading no contest. Appellant's sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.

Texas Workers' Compensation Comm'n v. City of Bridge City


NO. 03-94-00124-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


900 S.W.2d 411; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1132



May 24, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled July 12, 1995. Released for Publication July 12, 1995. The Docket Number of this Case has been Corrected November 21, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO.92-14599, HONORABLE JOSEPH H. HART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Workers' Compensation Commission, its executive director, and the Subsequent Injury Fund challenged a decision from the District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District (Texas), in favor of appellee city, which declared that the four-tier system for determining claims was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Threatened by administrative penalties if they did not pay workers' compensation benefits during the only period when reimbursement was not expressly secured by the statutory scheme, appellee self-insured city and Texas Municipal League Intergovernmental Risk Pool sued for declaratory judgment that the Workers' Compensation Act was unconstitutional. The trial court agreed and issued a permanent injunction against enforcement of the scheme. The Commission, its executive director, and the Subsequent Injury Fund appealed. The court held that the trial court exceeded its power in deciding that the statutory scheme was not "suitable" and, therefore, unconstitutional. The court held that appellees could not use the sword of due-process to invalidate the laws that governed them. It also ruled the statutory scheme was not unconstitutional. Appellants had argued their due process rights had been violated. The court found the legislature could rationally adjust the competing public and private interests in the manner set out in the statutory scheme and reversed the decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and held the statutory scheme in the Workers' Compensation Act was not unconstitutional because it was rationally designed to adjust competing public and private interests and appellee city and agency did not have standing to invalid the laws that governed them.

Cannon v. State


No. 01-94-00268-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1096



May 18, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 675,892.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas), for possession of cocaine. Defendant's appeal challenged the trial court's failure to suppress evidence, denial of defendant's motion to quash, denial of defendant's motion to strike sentence enhancements, permitting the state to mention defendant's prior convictions, and denial of defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of cocaine possession and sentenced to an enhanced term of imprisonment because of prior convictions. Defendant appealed the trial court's denial of a motion to suppress evidence, denial of a motion to quash the indictment, denial of a motion to strike the enhancements, permitting evidence concerning prior convictions and arrests, and denial of a motion for a new trial. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the challenged evidence because questions concerning the care and custody of the evidence went to its weight rather than admissibility. The court also found that the trial court had not abused its discretion when it denied the motion to strike the enhancements but had, instead, properly applied Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.46. Finally, the court noted that defendant waived any objections to the evidence concerning his prior convictions and arrests and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied the motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed. The court found that defendant waived his objections concerning admission of evidence, there was no abuse of discretion with regard to the sentence enhancements, defendant waived any objection concerning his prior convictions, the prosecution's mention of defendant's prior convictions was permissible summation, and there was no abuse of discretion in the denial of the motion for a new trial.

LaGesse v. PrimaCare, Inc.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND

May 18, 1995, Decided  
May 18, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 160th District Court of Dallas County.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the order of the 160th District Court of Dallas County, Texas that granted defendant physicians and health care facility summary judgment in plaintiff's medical malpractice action because the statute of limitations had run.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought a medical malpractice action against defendant physicians and health care facility. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment because more than two years had elapsed between the negligent health care treatment and when she filed her claim. Defendants claimed that this violated the statute of limitations of the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1995), which adopted an absolute two-year statute of limitations period. However, case law found the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act unconstitutional insofar as it prevented injured persons from bringing suit before they had a reasonable opportunity to discover the wrong. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to defendants because more than a year passed between when plaintiff discovered the negligence and when she brought suit, and, therefore, her delay was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that granted defendant summary judgment in plaintiff's medical malpractice action because the statute of limitations did not adopt a discovery rule and plaintiff had delayed unreasonably in bringing suit.

In the Interest of Sicko


NUMBER 13-94-083-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


900 S.W.2d 863; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1120



May 18, 1995, delivered  
May 18, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 25th District Court of Lavaca County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Having overruled all of appellant's points of error, we AFFIRM the trial court's judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child sought review of the decision of the 25th District Court of Lavaca County, Texas, that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee putative father in appellant's action seeking to establish appellee's paternity.


OVERVIEW: Appellant child filed his paternity action against appellee putative father when he was 57 years old. When summary judgment was granted to appellee, he sought review arguing that there was no reasonable statute of limitations applicable to his situation or that if there was one, it violated his equal protection rights. The court found that no specific provision in Family Code applied to appellant's right to bring paternity action. As such, it looked to the residual limitations period of four years contained in Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.051, and concluded that, even if it tolled that period until appellant learned the possible identity of his father, his action would still have been barred because it was filed six years after he discovered the possible identity of his father. Because appellant did not show any impermissible statutory classification that discriminated against him as an illegitimate child, or that he had been denied any substantial benefit accorded to children generally, the court found no equal protection violation. While the court was sympathetic to appellant's desire to learn the identity of his father, it affirmed the summary judgment for appellee.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment in favor of appellee putative father, finding that appellant child's paternity action was barred by statute of limitations and that barring appellant's paternity action did not violate his rights to equal protection of the law because he was unable to show that any impermissible statutory classification that discriminated against him as an illegitimate child or that he was denied substantial benefit accorded to children.

Franklin v. Kyle


No. 10-94-211-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


899 S.W.2d 405; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1040



May 17, 1995, delivered  
May 17, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 74th District Court. McLennan County, Texas. Trial Court # 94-1681-3.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed for want of jurisdiction


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant probationer sought review of the order of the 74th District Court, McLennan County, Texas, that denied his petition to enjoin appellee Board of Pardons and Paroles from proceeding with his parole revocation hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant probationer sought a temporary injunction to require appellee Board of Pardons and Paroles to hold appellant's parole revocation hearing after a determination of his competency. The court denied the temporary injunction, and appellant sought review. Appellant argued that he was entitled to an injunction because he was facing a constitutional injury. The court analogized appellant's argument to a pretrial order involving the constitutionality of a criminal statute, which was interlocutory and could not be appealed until a final judgment was rendered. The court found no reason to grant appellant a right denied criminal defendants and concluded that his only method of redress was to file a post-incarceration petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Because there was no evidence in the record that appellant's request for a injunction would affect the mandate of the Court of Criminal Appeals, it concluded that the trial court did have jurisdiction to consider the injunction sought by appellant. It held, however, that the court did not have the authority to grant appellant declaratory relief on the constitutionality of appellee's rules which may result in his reincarceration.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant probationer's petition to enjoin appellee Board of Pardons and Paroles from holding a parole revocation hearing for lack of jurisdiction, finding that the trial court did not have authority to declare appellant's rights under appellee's rules or to address the constitutionality of appellee's rules.

October 19, 1994, Submitted

May 11, 1995, filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ dismissed by, 01/25/1996


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 332nd District Court. Hidalgo County, Texas. Cause No. C-454-91-F.
Richards v. Mena, 820 S.W.2d 371, 1991 Tex. LEXIS 125 (Tex., 1991)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the judgment of the 332nd District Court, Hidalgo County (Texas), that awarded attorneys' fees to appellee civil rights organizations in conjunction with appellees' successful challenge of the Texas House of Representatives' and Senate's redistricting plans on the grounds that such plans illegally and unconstitutionally discriminated against Mexican-Americans.


OVERVIEW: After appellee civil rights organizations successfully enjoined appellant state from using the 1991 legislative enactments redistricting the Texas House of Representatives and the Texas Senate, appellees sought reimbursement for their attorneys' fees from appellant. The court affirmed the trial court's determination that attorneys' fees were available to appellees, but reversed some of the awards made by the trial court. The court held that appellant's use of the unconstitutionally discriminatory redistricting plans were prohibited acts under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 106.001(a)(6). Further, the court held that appellant's immunity was waived pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 106.002(b). With respect to the evidentiary foundation for the award of attorneys' fees, the court held two attorneys were competent to testify as fact witnesses regarding their attorneys' fees. The court, however, held that the reasonableness of attorneys' fees had to be supported by competent evidence and that there was no evidentiary foundation that the attorneys' fees were reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that appellant state's 1991 enactments regarding redistricting imposed an unreasonable burden on Mexican-Americans due to their national origin and that the trial court could award attorneys' fees to appellee civil rights organizations. The court, however, reversed some of the attorneys' fees awarded to appellees because there was no evidentiary foundation that such fees were reasonable.

Wilson v. State


NO. 07-94-0341-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


899 S.W.2d 36; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1031



May 11, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled June 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 364TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 94-418863; HONORABLE BRADLEY S. UNDERWOOD, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment and sentence for the crime of delivery of a controlled substance of less than 28 grams, entered by the 364th Judicial District Court of Lubbock County (Texas), based upon the trial court's denial of his motion to be sentenced under the amended version of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.112(b) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Appellant moved the trial court to be sentenced under the amended version of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 482.112(b) (1992), which reclassified the crime of delivery of a controlled substance of less than 28 grams from a first degree felony to a state jail felony. The trial court denied the motion. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. In so ruling, the court rejected appellant's argument that the savings provisions clause of the Code Construction Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 311.031 (1988), mandated that his sentence be determined in accordance with the revised version of § 481.112(b). The court held that § 311.031 was not applicable because the senate bill which revised § 481.112(b) specifically stated that it did not apply to offenses, such as appellant's, which were committed prior to the effective date of the amendments. The court also ruled that the trial court did not deny appellant his U.S. Const. amend. V right to equal protection by applying the old version of § 481.112(b). The court held that appellant was treated no differently than any other criminal defendant who committed the charged offense before the effective date of the amendments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and sentence for the crime of delivery of a controlled substance of less than 28 grams because the trial court did not err in refusing to sentence appellant under the revised version of the statute he was charged with violating.

Smith v. State


NO. 03-94-00158-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


899 S.W.2d 31; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 977



May 10, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled June 21, 1995. Released for Publication June 21, 1995. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 8, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 0940237, HONORABLE LARRY FULLER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District (Texas) that found him guilty of two counts of aggravated robbery pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.03. He appealed on numerous grounds, including the unconstitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 37.07, § 3(a), which permitted evidence regarding unadjudicated offenses to be admitted during punishment phase of his criminal trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of armed robbery. During the punishment phase of his trial, evidence of two prior unadjudicated armed robberies committed during the same week as the charged offenses were admitted pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 3(a). Appellant sought review, arguing that this section was unconstitutional because it was vague, denied him due process, delegated legislative power to the judiciary, and violated the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. Appellant did not raise these challenges in the trial court, and, therefore, the court concluded that he did not preserve them for appeal as required by Tex. R. App. P. 52(a). The court found that even if appellant had preserved them for appeal, he failed to show, or even to assert, that the section was unconstitutional as applied to him in his situation. The court found that proof beyond a reasonable doubt was a primary requirement for the admission of extraneous offense evidence at the punishment stage rather than a part of the state's case, and a jury instruction on the burden of proof was not required. The court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the aggravated robbery convictions, finding that appellant did not preserve his arguments of unconstitutionality because he did not raise them during the trial and that, even if he had preserved them, he failed to show how the criminal code section was unconstitutional as it applied to him in his specific situation.

Keyes v. State


No. 05-94-01172-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 4088



May 10, 1995, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 4. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F93-43700-NK.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Criminal District Court No. 4, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted her of possession of cocaine following her guilty plea pursuant to a plea bargain agreement. The trial court granted defendant permission to appeal its ruling on her motion to suppress the cocaine as the fruit of an illegal arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine. A police officer saw defendant talking to a man in a parking lot known for drug activity and prostitution. Other officers had told the officer that defendant was a prostitute. Based on the officer's conversation with defendant and the man, he arrested defendant for manifestation of prostitution, a violation of Dallas, Tex., City Code § 31-27. He searched defendant's purse and found a "crack pipe" containing cocaine residue. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment, as the trial court erred in not suppressing the cocaine seized as a result of the arrest. None of the factors specified in the ordinance were present in the case. Because the ordinance's listed factors were not exclusive, the court looked to see if any other facts and circumstances known to the officer when he arrested defendant would justify the warrantless arrest. The court held that the totality of all the facts and circumstances established reasonable suspicion to temporarily detain defendant, but did not give the officer probable cause to justify a warrantless arrest.


OUTCOME: The court reverse the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of possession of cocaine because the court found that the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress. The court remanded the cause for further proceedings.

Shoberg v. Shoberg


No. 01-94-00954-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 915



May 4, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 113th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-36819.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife sought review of a summary judgment rendered in favor of appellee ex-husband by the 113th District Court of Harris County (Texas) in a suit to quiet title to real property. Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in granting appellee's motion for summary judgment and refusing to acknowledge valid constitutional challenge.


OVERVIEW: Appellant ex-wife and appellee ex-husband were divorced on December 4, 1978. The divorce decree incorporated an agreement incident to divorce providing that appellee would convey his interest in their residence to appellant in consideration for the execution and delivery of a $ 67,000 promissory note and a deed of trust securing the note. Appellant made few payments and the parties renewed the note. Appellant defaulted and appellee instituted foreclosure proceedings. Appellant sought an injunction, claiming the lien was void as unconstitutional and that the interest was usurious. A temporary injunction was issued. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment on the basis that the constitutional claim was an impermissible collateral attack on the divorce decree. Summary judgment was granted. Appellant claimed the trial court erred in refusing to recognize the constitutional prohibition of a valid lien attaching to her undivided one-half interest. The court held that divorce judgments are not subject to collateral attack and therefore the constitutional challenge was impermissible. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment granting summary judgment to appellee ex-husband in an action by appellant ex-wife seeking an injunction against appellant's foreclosure of her interest in property was affirmed. The court held that the appellee could not seek an injunction because the divorce judgment was not subject to collateral attack.

McDaniel v. State


No. 01-94-00542-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 919



May 4, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion on Remand from the Court of Criminal Appeals November 27, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Tex. App. LEXIS 5357.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9402414.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for possession of less than 28 grams of a controlled substance, cocaine, imposed by the 337th District Court, Harris County (Texas). He contended that the evidence was both legally and factually insufficient to support his conviction, that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 1.15 (1995) unconstitutionally prevented appellant from presenting evidence, and that he did not validly waive his U.S. Const. amend. VI rights.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for possession of less than 28 grams of a controlled substance, cocaine. Appellant contended that the evidence was both legally and factually insufficient to support his conviction, that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 1.15 (1995) unconstitutionally prevented him from presenting evidence, and that he did not validly waive his U.S. Const. amend. VI rights. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and held that, based on the evidence, any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The evidence showed that appellant was arrested in a crack house, he was found in a room with the contraband, which was accessible to appellant and in plain view, and he threw the away as the police entered the room showing appellant's consciousness of guilt. The court also held that the purpose of article 1.15 was to ensure that no person was convicted of a felony on a plea of guilty without the state introducing evidence to show guilt. It did not prevent appellant from offering evidence. Finally, the court found that appellant waived his U.S. Const. amend. VI compulsory process because he did not raise the issue at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance, cocaine. The evidence showed that the trial court could have found all essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that a statute did not prohibit appellant from offering evidence after he pled guilt to the charges and found appellant had waived his sixth amendment compulsory process rights.

Powell v. State


No. 05-94-00743-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 4091



May 4, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 204th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F93-04823-TQ.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the 204th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him, upon a plea, of criminal nonsupport of his children, contending it was error for the trial court to deny his motion to dismiss the indictment for violating his equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV because the charging statute made the offense a misdemeanor for a resident and a felony for a nonresident.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with criminal nonsupport of his children, a violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.05 (1994), and filed a motion to dismiss the indictment, claiming the statute violated his equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV because it made the offense a misdemeanor for a resident and a felony for a nonresident. The trial court denied the motion and defendant appealed his subsequent conviction. The court reversed and dismissed the indictment, finding that defendant had the right to travel from state to state and to reside in the state of his choice. The court determined that because the statute penalized defendant's fundamental right of residence choice it was invalid unless the state could show it was truly necessary to promote a compelling government interest. The court concluded that the state was unable to establish that it was necessary to classify nonresident offenders as felons in order to ease their extradition from foreign jurisdictions. The court found the state could not prove that there was a problem in extraditing misdemeanants, thus failing to show the classification was necessary for the extradition of criminal nonsupport offenders.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction of defendant for criminal nonsupport and dismissed the indictment against him, finding that it violated his equal protection rights under the Fourteenth Amendment by making the offense a misdemeanor for residents and a felony for nonresidents. The court determined that the state failed to establish a compelling government interest in restricting defendant's right to reside in the state of his choice.

Lall v. Central Appraisal Dist.


No. 05-94-01326-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3062



April 21, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Writ Granted November 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 354th Judicial District Court. Rockwall County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 1-93-316.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the dismissal by the 354th Judicial District Court of Rockwall County (Texas), in favor of appellee, Central Appraisal District of Rockwall County, in an action for judicial review of appellee's valuation of their property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owners had filed a protest with the Appraisal Review Board contending that appellee's valuation of their property was excessive. This protest was denied and appellants argued that Tex. Tax Code Ann § 42.08 (1992), was unconstitutional and the trial court had erred in upholding its constitutionality. Section 42.08 required appellants to pay by certain date either the amount of taxes assessed on the property or the greater of (1) the amount of taxes not in dispute, or (2) the amount of taxes imposed in the preceding year. Appellants had paid no taxes and the forfeiture provision of the statute authorized forfeiture of a taxpayer's appellate rights if a taxpayer did not prepay taxes. The court found that the forfeiture provision of the statute furthered no additional state interest other than was already accomplished by the prepayment provision. Therefore, the court sustained appellant's points of error because the forfeiture provision created an unreasonable financial barrier on their access to the courts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal order because it found that the forfeiture clause of the tax statute violated the open courts provision of the Texas Constitution by unreasonably restricting a taxpayer's access to the courts.

Hill v. State


NO. 2-94-089-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


897 S.W.2d 533; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 814



April 20, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 10 OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Pete Gilfeather.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the County Criminal Court No. 10 of Tarrant County (Texas), for knowingly causing the unwarranted commitment of his stepfather to a mental health facility.


OVERVIEW: Appellant completed an application for the emergency apprehension and detention of his stepfather, claiming that the stepfather had previously received mental health treatment, threatened to kill his estranged wife and himself, was isolated from family and evidenced increasingly agitated behavior. That same day, the stepfather was taken by sheriff's deputies to a mental health facility for psychiatric evaluation. After a preliminary examination, the stepfather was released and allowed to return home. A jury convicted appellant of knowingly causing the unwarranted commitment of his stepfather to a mental health facility. Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 571.020 (1992). Appellant sought review and contended that there was no evidence as to the commitment element of the offense. The court agreed that the stepfather's brief detention did not rise to the level of a "commitment" and reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to enter an acquittal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for knowingly causing the unwarranted commitment of his stepfather to a mental health facility, because the brief detention of appellant's stepfather for purposes of evaluation did not constitute a "commitment." The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to enter an acquittal.

Waggoner v. State


NO. 03-94-00279-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


897 S.W.2d 510; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 778



April 12, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 0941886, HONORABLE JOE DIBRELL, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 147th Judicial District, Travis County (Texas), which convicted and sentenced him for compelling prostitution in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.05 (1994), upon a jury finding of guilty and assessment of punishment.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of compelling prostitution in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.05 (1994) and assessed punishment, and he was convicted and sentenced by the trial court. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the evidence was sufficient to support appellant's guilt because he clearly provided the opportunity of the minor to engage in prostitution and delivered her for prostitution, and by those means caused her to act. The court noted that appellant's actions satisfied the statutory language in § 43.05(a)(2), which provided that a person had violated the law if he caused "by any means" a person younger that 17 years to commit prostitution. Further, the court determined that the state did not have to prove that the minor committed prostitution in order to find appellant guilty.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for compelling prostitution was affirmed because the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's finding of guilt. The court found that under the relevant statute, appellant's actions caused "by any means" the minor to commit prostitution.

Hegan v. State


No. 01-94-00797-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 765



April 6, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law Number Six. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9402647.



DISPOSITION: Judgment


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant challenged a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law Number Six, Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of driving while intoxicated (DWI), enhanced by a previous DWI conviction, and sentenced appellant to confinement in the county jail for one year, probated, and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for driving while intoxicated (DWI). He was taken to police headquarters, and an officer unsuccessfully attempted four times to administer an intoxilyzer test. The first two times, a tube on the machine was disconnected, and the last two times there was radio interference. The officer decided "that was enough" and no attempt was made on another machine. Appellant was convicted of DWI, enhanced by a previous DWI conviction, and was sentenced to confinement in the county jail for one year, probated, and a fine. On appeal, appellant contended that the trial court erred in failing to dismiss because the police failed to conduct a successful intoxilyzer test after appellant agreed to submit to the test. The court affirmed. The court held that neither Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-5, § 1 nor any provision of the state or federal constitutions gave a person arrested for DWI an absolute right to request and to have administered at state expense any kind of test that might reflect whether he or she were intoxicated. The court found that the statute did not require the test as a mandatory prerequisite for a DWI prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because a person arrested for driving while intoxicated did not have an absolute right to request and to have administered at state expense any kind of test for intoxication.

W.V. Grant Evangelistic Ass'n v. Dallas Cent. Appraisal Dist.


No. 05-94-01156-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


900 S.W.2d 789; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 1462



March 31, 1995, Filed, Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 68th District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-10474-C. Name of Judge: Gary Hall.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer appealed a judgment of the 68th District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which dismissed its ad valorem tax case in favor of appellee appraisal district and upheld the constitutionality of the prepayment requirement for appeal of property tax assessment under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08 (1992).


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer sought judicial review of appellee appraisal district's denial of its application for exemption as a religious organization. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08 (1992), and dismissed appellant's suit for failure to comply with the prepayment requirements of § 42.08. On appeal, the court held that the forfeiture provision of § 42.08 facially violated the opens courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court held that the forfeiture of the right of judicial review for failure to meet prepayment requirements for property tax appeal was an unreasonable financial barrier to access to the courts, where less restrictive means, such as accelerated administrative proceedings and expedited court procedures, equally furthered government's interests in assuring that the activities of local government that rely on ad valorem taxes to operate were not unduly impeded and insuring that taxpayers did not use the right of judicial review as a subterfuge for delaying or avoiding the payment of at least some tax. The court reversed the trial court's dismissal order and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing appellant taxpayer's suit for failure to comply with prepayment requirement for property tax appeal because the forfeiture clause was an unconstitutional restriction on access to the courts.

Bonner v. State

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 14, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of promoting an obscene device in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23 (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a clerk in an adult video store. Police officers entered the store and saw appellant standing behind a glass counter which contained sexually explicit material. Palermo v. Palermo


No. B14-94-00482-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 580



March 16, 1995, rendered  
March 16, 1995, filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 310th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-13228.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, boyfriend and family member, sought review of an order from the 310th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which issued a protective order against appellants in favor of appellee girlfriend.


OVERVIEW: Appellee girlfriend filed an application for a protective order against appellants, boyfriend and family member, which alleged family violence on the part of appellees. The trial court set a hearing on the protective order the day following notice to the parties, pursuant to the Texas Family Code. Tex. Fam. Code. Ann. § 71.09(a) (1995). The trial court granted appellee's protective order. Upon appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that appellants failed to preserve error on their argument that the notice provision of Tex. Fam. Code. Ann. § 71.09(a) (1995) violated the open court's doctrine because they failed to assert that claim at the trial court. The court held that the short notice provision in the statute did not violate appellants' due process rights because it was not unreasonable or arbitrary when balanced against the purposes behind the statute to prevent family violence and preserve property. The court held that the provision requiring the trial court to set a hearing within 14 days after the filing of an application for protective order was not jurisdictional it was merely a protection for the applicant. Tex. Fam. Code. Ann. 71.09(a) (1995).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that granted a protective order in favor of appellee girlfriend. The court held a notice provision of a statute for family protective orders was constitutional because it was not unreasonable or arbitrary when balanced against purposes of preventing family violence and preserving property. The court held the requirement that a hearing be held within 14 days of a protective order application was not jurisdictional.

Busse v. Pacific Cattle Feeding Fund #1


No. 06-94-00052-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


896 S.W.2d 807; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 529


December 8, 1994, Submitted  
March 14, 1995, Decided  
March 14, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 14th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court No. 91-09492-A.

This Opinion Substituted on Overrule of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of February 2, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 176.



DISPOSITION: For the reasons stated, the judgment is in all things affirmed. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing was OVERRULED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of an adverse judgment from the 14th Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, rendered in plaintiff's suit to recover damages resulting from an investment in a failed cattle marketing arrangement on the grounds that defendants' violated the Texas Securities Act, the Texas Deceptive Trade Practices Act, Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 17.41 et seq. (1987), and committed common law fraud.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendants alleging violations of the Texas Securities Act and Deceptive Trade Practices Act (DTPA), Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 17.41 et seq. (1987), common law fraud, and breach of contract. The trial court rendered summary judgment for plaintiff on the Securities Act claims, and the jury found in plaintiff's favor on the DTPA and fraud claims. The trial court also directed verdicts for defendants on plaintiff's breach of contract claims. On review, the court found that the trial court did not err in denying defendants' motion to dismiss based on forum selection clauses because the case did not involve an interpretation or construction of the contracts. Further, the court found that the evidence was both legally and factually sufficient to support the jury finding that defendants committed fraud and engaged in deceptive acts. Finally, the court held that the trial court correctly reduced plaintiff's damages to the limit provided by the DTPA because the legislature intended the treble damages to be a cap on the total damages recoverable in a DTPA action, regardless of the number of defendants. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The adverse judgment rendered in plaintiff's suit to recover damages resulting from an investment in a failed cattle marketing arrangement was affirmed because defendants' points of error were overruled, and the evidence was both legally and factually sufficient to support the findings that defendants committed fraud and engaged in deceptive acts.

Trahan v. Trahan


NO. 03-93-00607-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


894 S.W.2d 113; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 447



March 8, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 5, 1995. Released for Publication April 5, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 344,539, HONORABLE F. SCOTT MCCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife sought review of a judgment entered by the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District (Texas), declaring invalid and unenforceable a final judgment partitioning appellee veteran's military retirement pay.


OVERVIEW: Appellant ex-wife filed suit, claiming entitlement to a portion of appellee veteran's military retirement pay. The trial court declared that a portion thereof was community property that should have been divided in the divorce. The case reached the Texas Supreme Court, which reversed based on a decision of the United States Supreme Court, and rendered judgment for appellee. Congress then enacted the Uniformed Services Former Spouses' Protection Act (USFSPA), 10 U.S.C.S. § 1408, allowing states to apply family property law as it existed prior to the U.S. Supreme Court decision. Appellant returned to court and received a judgment awarding her a portion of appellant's right to retirement pay. The decision was affirmed on appeal. Based on a later amendment to the USFSPA, appellee filed suit to vacate the judgment. The trial court found in favor of appellee. The court reversed, concluding that appellant's right to a portion of appellee's retirement pay vested upon affirmation of the prior judgment, that res judicata barred reopening the prior judgment, and that the subsequent amendment of the USFSPA could not be applied retroactively to extinguish appellant's vested rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, vacating a prior judgment that awarded appellant ex-wife a portion of appellee veteran's military retirement benefits, because appellant's right to part of the benefits was vested, res judicata precluded relitigation of appellant's rights, and a subsequent amendment to the Uniformed Services Former Spouses' Protection Act could not be applied retroactively to extinguish appellant's rights.

Harris County v. Going


No. 01-93-00406-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


896 S.W.2d 305; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 365



March 2, 1995, rendered and delivered  
March 2, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 295th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-335891. DANIEL M. DOWNEY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and rendered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipal employer challenged the judgment of the 295th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which found appellant had violated appellee patrolman's right to free speech under the Texas Constitution, and violated the whistleblower statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-16a, and the Civil Rights Act of 1871, 42 U.S.C.S. 1983, when it demoted and then fired appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee patrolman published a list of violations of his employer's departmental rules and regulations and was thereafter demoted and terminated. Appellee filed a suit against appellants, his employer, his supervisor, and a county commissioner, under the whistleblower statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-16a, and the Civil Rights Act of 1871, 42 U.S.C.S. 1983, for wrongful termination and violation of his constitutional right to free speech. After judgment was rendered for appellee, appellant municipal employers sought further review, alleging governmental immunity and good cause. On appeal, the court reversed and rendered judgment in favor of appellant municipal employer. The court held that appellee's demotion and termination were not in violation of his right to free speech since appellant employer was immune from the illegal acts of its officials; that there was no waiver of governmental immunity for the claim under § 1983, and appellant employer was liable under § 1983 only for acts sanctioned or ordered by it. The court also held that appellee's claim under art. 6252-16a was not timely made.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and rendered judgment for appellant municipal employer. The court held that appellee patrolman's demotion and termination did not violate appellee's right to free speech, appellee's whistleblower claim was untimely, and that liability did not attach under the Civil Rights Act of 1871 (Act), because the Act only applied to officially sanctioned acts.

Holt v. Epley


NO. 07-94-0078-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


894 S.W.2d 511; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 433



March 2, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 7, 1995. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled April 3, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 108TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF POTTER COUNTY; NO. 79,419-E; HONORABLE ABE LOPEZ, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of an order of the 108th Judicial District Court of Potter County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee radiologist in a medical malpractice case for negligence and infliction of mental distress, on grounds that the statute of limitations was tolled by the open courts provision of the Texas constitution, Tex. Const. art. I §13.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient had mammographies performed and interpreted by appellee radiologist who detected no malignancy. Two years later, appellant detected a lump in her left breast, had another mammogram, a biopsy, and a radical mastectomy of her left breast. Further testing indicated a high risk for cancer in her right breast. Appellant filed a medical malpractice lawsuit four years after the initial mammography. A motion for summary judgment asserting the two-year limitation on medical malpractice was granted in favor of appellee. Appellant sought review on grounds that the evidence established that she filed within the limitations period, and that appellee failed to establish that the application of the two-year limitations period did not violate the "open courts" provision. The court affirmed the trial court, finding that the evidence sufficiently established that the dates of any alleged negligence were readily ascertainable, that appellant's claims did not arise from a continuing course of treatment sufficient to toll the running of limitations, and that the fact that appellant "wondered" about the accuracy of other women's tests was insufficient to demonstrate mental anguish.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because evidence sufficiently established that the dates of appellee radiologist's alleged negligence were readily ascertainable, that the claims did not arise from a continuing course of treatment sufficient to toll the running of limitations, and that the fact that appellant patient "wondered" about the accuracy of other women's tests was insufficient to demonstrate mental anguish.

City of Irving v. Dallas/Fort Worth Int'l Airport Bd.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cities sought review from the 96th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which upheld the constitutionality of a state law giving municipal airport authorities the power to make land-use decisions in a declaratory judgment action in favor of appellee airport board, airlines, corporation, and state attorney general.


OVERVIEW: Appellant cities sought review from a declaratory judgment action upholding the constitutionality of state law in favor of appellee airport board, airlines, corporation, and state attorney general giving municipal authorities the power to make land-use decisions for property within geographic boundaries of the airports. The court held the Texas Municipal Airports Act (Act) (amended 1993) was not local or special even though its enforcement or operation was confined to a restricted area, because people throughout the state were affected thereby. XI, § 5, general laws by the legislature could override ordinances passed by home-rule municipalities. The court held that the limitation on the powers of home rule city were unmistakably clear and compelling and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which upheld the constitutionality of state law in favor of appellees airport board, airlines, corporation, and state attorney general against appellant cities, which gave the municipal authorities the power to make land-use decisions. The court held that the legislature could override such power if the limitations were unmistakably clear.

The court also noted that the court of criminal appeals had expressly declined to set a different standard for reviewing obscenity laws under Tex. Const. art. I, § 8, even though it had the power to do so. The court declined appellant's invitation to conduct a separate analysis under the Texas Constitution, holding that it could not apply a separate test in criminal cases that was in conflict with the pronouncements of the court of criminal appeals.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for obscenity was affirmed, because the obscenity statutes have historically been held constitutional under the First Amendment, and the court could not conduct a separate test under the Texas Constitution that conflicted with the holdings of the court of criminal appeals.

HL Farm Corp. v. Henderson County Appraisal Dist.


NO. 12-91-00033-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


894 S.W.2d 830; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 468



February 14, 1995, delivered  
February 14, 1995, filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 173RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF HENDERSON COUNTY, TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foreign corporation challenged an order by the 173rd District Court in Henderson County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee tax authorities and state, claiming that Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 25.56(3) violated Tex. Const. art. I., § 3.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a foreign corporation. It appealed a decision by appellee tax authorities which denied it an advantageous tax appraisal because of its foreign status. Appellant challenged the Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 25.56(3), claiming that it violated Tex. Const. art. I., § 3, and sought summary judgment. Appellee was then joined by the State of Texas who joined to defend the validity of the statute, and filed for summary judgment. The trial court found in favor of appellees. The court reversed and held that there was no rational basis for appellees to deny appellant's open space designation, so the classification under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 25.56(3) was not rationally related to the promotion and preservation of the open-space land and violated Tex. Const. art. I § 3. The court would not address the other constitutional challenges made by appellant because the statute was invalidated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee taxing authority and state because it found that the tax code section relied on by appellee taxing authority was unconstitutional because it was not rationally related to its stated purpose of preservation of open-space lands.

 

1182 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


No. C14-94-00717-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 172



February 2, 1995, rendered  
February 2, 1995, filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 683185.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas), revoking his probation and sentencing appellant to prison following his plea of guilty to the offense of attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to attempted murder, and the trial court sentenced him to probation. The trial court found that appellant violated the terms of his probation, and it revoked the probation and sentenced appellant to prison. Appellant sought review of the judgment, arguing that the trial court erred in admonishing him in writing, rather than orally, of the consequences of his plea and that the trial court erred in failing to require the probation office to submit a supervision plan in the presentence investigation report. The court ruled that appellant was admonished in writing of the range of punishment for attempted murder and informed that any recommendation as to punishment was not binding on the trial court. Further, the court held that any error with regard to the admonishments given pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13, was waived by appellant's failure to object. The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant, concluding that appellant waived error with regard to the allegedly flawed presentence report because he failed to object to the absence of the proposed plan.


OUTCOME: Judgment adjudicating appellant guilty was affirmed where appellant waived any error concerning the admonishments he received from the trial court and concerning the presentence investigation report because he failed to object.

 

1183 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Villa v. State


No. 05-93-01751-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 3892



January 31, 1995, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 3. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F93-40815-VJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order entered in the Criminal District Court, No. 3, Dallas County (Texas), which denied his motion to suppress evidence. Defendant contended that his reliance on assurances made by police officers regarding a traffic offense rendered a second warrant for his arrest unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed a trial court order, which denied his motion to suppress. Defendant contended that his reliance on assurances made by local officers, regarding a traffic offense, rendered a second warrant for his arrest unconstitutional. Defendant got a traffic ticket for driving without a license. In response to a letter, defendant sent a money order to pay the ticket. The local police later arrested defendant because he had an outstanding warrant. The warrant issued on the ground that defendant had not paid the ticket. A local officer told him that posting bail was the same as paying the fine for the ticket and he would have no more problems with the offense. Defendant was arrested again, based on a second warrant issued on the original traffic ticket, and his car was impounded. A search of the car revealed cocaine and heroin in the ashtray. On appeal, the court held that defendant's argument did not justify suppression because he did not attack the underlying affidavit for the warrant, the magistrate's role in its issuance, or the warrant's facial validity and the arresting officer's reliance on it. Accordingly, the court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant did not attack the underlying affidavit for the warrant, the magistrate, the magistrate's role in the issuance of the warrant, the arresting officer's reliance on the warrant. Suppression was not justified.

Nghia Thi Dinh v. Harris County Hosp. Dist.


No. 01-94-00416-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


896 S.W.2d 248; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 99



January 26, 1995, rendered and delivered  
January 26, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 215th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-30174A. EUGENE CHAMBERS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, wife and as next friend of her husband, challenged the grant of a summary judgment by the 215th District Court, Harris County (Texas), to appellee county hospital under the notice provision of Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. 101.101(a) in a medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, wife and as husband's next friend, filed a medical malpractice claim alleging that a delay in treatment caused her husband to suffer a stroke. Appellee county hospital was granted summary judgment on the ground that appellant did not give the notice required under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.101(a) to waive appellee's governmental immunity. Appellant argued that § 101.101(a) did not apply because her husband was incompetent and that it violated the open courts provisions of Tex. Const. arts. §§ I, XIII. The court held that incompetency did not excuse the required notice and that the open courts provisions did not apply to statutory claims. The court then reversed and remanded because § 101.101(a) did not apply if appellee had actual notice of an injury, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.101(c), and there were factual issues regarding actual notice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to appellee, county hospital, and remanded the medical malpractice action of appellant, wife and next friend of husband, because there was an issue of fact as to whether appellee had actual notice of the alleged injury under the applicable statute.

Harrington v. Norex Am.


No. 01-93-01116-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 79



January 19, 1995, rendered and delivered  
January 19, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 80th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-11035A.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of October 6, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2419.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed as reformed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guarantor challenged the decision of the 80th District Court, Harris County (Texas), that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee corporation and severed the claims in an action by appellee to recover payment from appellant as guarantor on three notes.


OVERVIEW: Appellee corporation and another company executed two notes in favor of appellee. Appellant guaranteed the notes. Appellant then guaranteed a third note executed in favor of a bank that was later assigned to appellee. After the company defaulted, appellee sued appellant to recover payment from him as guarantor. Appellant filed counterclaims asserting usury, wrongful foreclosure, libel, slander, breach of good faith and fair dealing, fraud, and fraudulent inducement. Appellee's motion for summary judgment on the two notes originally executed in its favor was granted, and the trial court rendered a take-nothing summary judgment on appellant's counterclaims for usury, wrongful corporate takeover, and wrongful foreclosure. The trial court severed the summary judgment from appellee's claims relating to the bank note and from the remainder of the counterclaims. On review, the court concluded that appellant's objection to severance was untimely and that summary judgment was proper as to all counterclaims except the wrongful corporate takeover claim. There was no such claim in appellant's pleadings, so the judgment was vacated and the order reformed. As reformed, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that granted summary judgment in favor of appellee corporation was reformed to vacate the judgment for the claim of wrongful corporate takeover because appellant guarantor's pleadings did not contain that claim. As reformed, the trial court's judgment was affirmed because appellant's objection to the severance was untimely and the grant of summary judgment was proper.

Texas Workers' Compensation Ins. Facility v. State Bd. of Ins.


NO. 3-94-122-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


894 S.W.2d 49; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 70



January 18, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 93-06293, HONORABLE PETER M. LOWRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, state workers' compensation insurance facility, sought review of a decision of the 353rd District Court of Travis County (Texas) that upheld a state board of insurance order against appellant to indemnify appellee insurers who participated in an assigned risk pool.


OVERVIEW: The Texas legislature created a workers' compensation assigned risk pool promising to issue policies to employers who could not obtain workers' compensation insurance. In exchange the pool promised to pay appellee insurers each a carrier fee and to indemnify for certain items as formalized by servicing company agreements. Appellant, state workers' compensation insurance facility, ceased indemnifying appellees for expenses incurred in the defense of risk pool litigation. The state board of insurance ordered appellant to continue to indemnify appellees and the lower court affirmed. The court affirmed holding that at the time the servicing company agreements were signed, the law did not prohibit indemnification of the servicing carriers, thus the right to indemnification was vested. A statute which took away or impaired vested rights acquired under existing laws could not be upheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the indemnification order against appellant. The court held that a statute which took away or impaired vested rights acquired under existing laws could not be upheld. When the agreements were signed, the law did not prohibit indemnification of the servicing carriers.

Gebhardt v. Gallardo


Cause No. 04-94-00690-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


891 S.W.2d 327; 1995 Tex. App. LEXIS 140



January 9, 1995, Delivered  
January 9, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 150th District Court of Bexar County. Trial Court No. 94-CI-05455.



DISPOSITION: WRIT OF MANDAMUS GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator judicial candidate claimed abuse of discretion, seeking a writ of mandamus from an order of the 150th District Court of Bexar County (Texas), where respondent judge severed and abated a negligence claim from a civil conspiracy claim, pending criminal charges against defendants. Relator sought damages from political party officials or members who allegedly negligently promoted and certified an invalid nominating petition.


OVERVIEW: Relator judicial candidate claimed abuse of discretion, seeking a writ of mandamus from an order in which respondent judge severed and abated a negligence claim from a civil conspiracy claim, pending criminal charges against defendants. Relator sought actual and exemplary damages from political party officials or members who allegedly negligently promoted and certified an invalid nominating petition. The court held that the assertion of the privilege against self-incrimination, by itself, could not be a legal basis for severance and abatement of the negligence claim while a criminal investigation proceeded. The negligence claim was vitiated since relator was prohibited from preserving defendants' testimony through oral deposition while the abatement order was in effect. The court found that severance without valid and sustaining reasons was not in the interest of judicial economy. Because the claims were based on the same factual allegations, the parties were identical, the proof required was drawn from the same events, and the abatement was clearly indefinite, the court was led to the conclusion that relator had no adequate remedy at law, and mandamus was conditionally granted.


OUTCOME: The court granted mandamus conditionally. The court could not find any legal basis for severance and abatement in the transcript or the statement of facts for the trial court's finding, and held that the order by respondent judge to sever and abate constituted a clear abuse of discretion for which relator judicial candidate had no adequate remedy on appeal. Unless the trial court rescinded its order to sever and abate, the writ would be issued.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the verdict from the 161st Judicial District Court of Ector County (Texas), which found appellant guilty of theft of oilfield equipment under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.93(e)(5)(A)(ii).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury of theft of oilfield equipment that was held in state custody. Appellant sought review of his conviction. The court affirmed the conviction under Tex. OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of theft of oilfield equipment because the jury charge and indictment were complete, consistent, and supported by sufficient evidence such that a reasonable person could find guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.

Francis v. State

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 110TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DICKENS COUNTY; NO. 2083; HONORABLE JOHN R. HOLLUMS, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction by the 110th Judicial District of Dickens County, (Texas) for delivery of a controlled substance by an offer to sell.


OVERVIEW: Officers entered a conversation with appellant, pursuant to a buy-bust operation, in which appellant told officers that he did not have anything to see but that he would take them to a place where he could get something for them. Appellant and the officers walked to the officers' van, and appellant opened the side door, and exposed the surveillance team. The court determined that the term "offer" in "an offer to sell" maintained its plain meaning, and that appellant's references to get "it" and get "some" were enough for a rational trier of fact to have found beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant offered to sell cocaine. The court found that Tex. Health and Safety Code Ann. § 481.112(a) was not unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, having determined that "offer to sell" was given its plain ordinary meaning, that appellant, through his words, represented that he had cocaine to sell, and that the statute under which appellant was convicted was not unconstitutionally vague.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO

December 8, 1994, Decided
