PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 140TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 87-520,343; HONORABLE WILLIAM R. SHAVER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city and fire department challenged the judgment of the 140th Judicial District Court of Lubbock County (Texas), which ordered payment of overtime compensation to appellee firemen for overtime hours appellees spent in continuous contact with appellant by pager or telephone. The challenged judgment came after remand from the Texas Supreme Court, which reversed the court's previous order affirming a summary judgment against appellees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city and fire department challenged the trial court's judgment, rendered on a jury's verdict, ordering overtime compensation paid to appellee firemen as back pay for overtime hours appellees spent in continuous contact with appellants by pager or telephone and subject to call for immediate return to duty. The court affirmed, holding that evidence supported the finding that appellees were required to remain in continuous contact with appellants and were subject to immediate call to duty. The court held that the trial court did not err in refusing appellants' requested instruction, because the instruction was one which could be handled by advocacy and argument, rendering the instruction unnecessary for the jury to reach its verdict. The court held that the trial court did not err in excluding the budgets for the Fire Marshal's office, because the budgets were cumulative evidence. The court held that appellants' were not entitled to judgment as a matter of law. The court found without explanation that it was precluded from entertaining appellants' attacks on the constitutionality of the law addressing overtime, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1269p, § 6.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the evidence supported the finding that appellee firemen were in continuous contact with appellant city and fire department and were subject to immediate call to duty. The court held that the trial court did not err in excluding appellants' budgets and refusing appellants' instruction concerning an officer's authority to act for appellants; and that appellants were not entitled to summary judgment.

Skillern v. State

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 0911666, HONORABLE BOB JONES, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 167th Judicial District Court, Travis County (Texas), which convicted him of the second-degree felony offense of theft of property having an aggregate value of $ 20,000 or more in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a), (e)(5)(B).


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction of second-degree felony theft in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a), (e)(5)(B). The court held that the indictment was proper because it alleged the county where the offense actually occurred. The court held that the addition of certain articles to the Texas Insurance Code did not violate ex post facto principles. The court held that the jury instruction defining culpable mental states was proper because theft, as charged, was not strictly a result-oriented offense. There was no fundamental error in the trial court's failure to give an instruction as to accomplice witness testimony because the accomplice's testimony was corroborated under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. The court held that even if the reasonable hypothesis rule applied, appellant asserted no reasonable hypotheses. The court held that a prior federal probated sentence, which counted as a final conviction under federal law, was properly used for enhancement purposes, even though a probated sentence under Texas law was not a final conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting appellant of second-degree felony theft because there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction, the jury charge was proper, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence of appellant's tax debt, and the prior federal conviction used for enhancement of punishment purposes was a final conviction and was not void as a matter of law.

Reuters Am., Inc. v. Sharp


NO. 3-93-124-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


889 S.W.2d 646; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2971; 23 Media L. Rep. 1129



December 7, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled January 25, 1995. Released for Publication January 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-5430, HONORABLE W. JEANNE MEURER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order from the 201st Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas), which found Tex. Tax Code §§ 151.0101(10), 151.038(a), and 151.310(a), (f) (1992) taxes on information services and exemptions for newspapers to be constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant electronic news service was denied relief in its tax protest suit, in which appellant alleged that sales tax assessments on information services while exempting newspapers was an unconstitutional restriction on free speech under Tex. Const. art. I, § 8 and U.S. Const. amend. I, and a violation of equal protection under Tex. Const. art. I, § 3 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Appellant sought review of the adverse judgment. The court affirmed judgment in favor of the state, holding that the tax was not based upon content but upon format, that the tax did not single out the press but was a general sales tax, and that the tax did not single out a small group of the press. Further, taxing information services while exempting newspapers did not violate federal or state equal protection clauses since the exemption was rationally related to promoting literacy and administrative economy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment denying relief to appellant electronic news service in a tax protest suit, and upheld taxation of information services and exemptions for newspapers as constitutional because it was a general tax that was not based on the content of speech, nor did it single out a small group of the press.

Adams v. Aetna Life Ins. Co.


No. B14-93-00596-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2901



December 1, 1994, Rendered  
December 1, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 280th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90-46726-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant on behalf of minor children challenged a decision from the 280th District Court. Harris County, Texas, which granted summary judgment to appellee insurers, holding they had been discharged from liability because appellant had not filed a claim as required under Tex. Ins. Code Ann. Art. 3.48 (1981).


OVERVIEW: Appellant on behalf of minor children filed a claim against appellee insurance companies to recover benefits for the loss of their insured mother. Summary judgment was granted to appellees because benefits had already been paid to the named beneficiary, father of the minor children. Father was subsequently found guilty of murdering the mother. On appeal, appellant argued that Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 3.48 (1981), discharging appellees of liability, was unconstitutional because minors were unable to file notice of an adverse claim as required under the statute. Since the children had a cause of action against their father, the statute did not deprive them of their common law action. The open courts provision of the state constitution did not guarantee a recoverable judgment, it merely protected those rights which existed at common law. Appellant argued that appellees had constructive notice of the adverse claim. The court held that the decision by the sheriff, in "clearing" father of the crime, made appellees' payment to father proper. Since appellant had filed no adverse claim, prior to the time appellees paid the claim, the decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which granted summary judgment to appellee insurers because the statute requiring minors to file notice of an adverse claim was constitutional and insurers did not have constructive notice of adverse claim when sheriff indicated that named beneficiary was cleared of murdering the insured.

Henning v. Henning


No. B14-93-01049-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


889 S.W.2d 611; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2859



November 23, 1994, Rendered  
November 23, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 328th District Court. Fort Bend County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 77035. Stansbury, T.O. Hon., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former wife sought review of a final decree of divorce rendered by the 328th District Court, Fort Bend County (Texas), which named appellant and appellee former husband joint managing conservators of a minor child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former wife argued an entitlement to a new trial following a master's decree of divorce ruling, because she was unable to obtain a complete statement of the facts from the trial and, thus, was unable to prosecute her appeal. The court disagreed, noting first that portions of the tape recording of the proceedings were inaudible. The court observed that appellant effectively waived her right to court reporter transcribed proceedings when she failed to request the reporter's presence, as required by Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 11.14(d) (1986). And even if the waiver was not express, the absence of a record would not warrant reversal where the record's absence was the result of appellant's lack of due diligence. The court noted that appellant failed to object to a trial by a master and did not request that a reporter be provided, as allowed by Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 54.018 (1988). Further, appellant failed to seek a de novo review of the master's findings, failed to refute a finding that she had no objection to relying on a poor quality tape, and failed to have a partial fact statement prepared of audible portions or to correct any tape inaccuracies.


OUTCOME: A final decree of divorce was affirmed that named appellant former wife and appellee former husband as joint managing conservators of a minor child, because appellant was not entitled to a new trial following a decree supported only by a partially audible set of facts from a tape recording of the trial, because the absence of a record was the result of her lack of due diligence in seeking a court reporter.

Phillips v. State


No. 09-93-265 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


887 S.W.2d 267; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2873


November 3, 1994, Submitted  
November 23, 1994, Delivered  
November 23, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 28, 1994. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 1, 1995.
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 03/01/1995
Appeal dismissed by Phillips v. State, 2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 770 (Tex. App. Beaumont, Feb. 2, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 252nd District Court. Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 50530. Honorable Leonard Giblin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment, and an order denying him a new trial, from the 252nd District Court, Jefferson County, Texas, that revoked his probation on deferred adjudication, convicted him of sexual assault of a minor, and sentenced him to 99 years in prison. Appellant contended that the judgment and sentence violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII, XIV, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19.


OVERVIEW: Appellant received a deferred adjudication and 10 years probation on a sexual assault of a minor charge. He later pleaded true to allegations that he violated probation. These violations included leaving the jurisdiction for two years, failing to report to his probation officer, failing to wear a probation bracelet, and testing positive for marijuana. He was adjudicated guilty and sentenced to 99 years in prison. The court affirmed the judgment and sentence. The court noted that appellant was well apprised of the consequences of his failure to adhere to the terms of his probation. The court also explained that the trial court, after advising appellant that he could be sentenced to 99 years, gave him the opportunity to withdraw his guilty plea and pleas of true. Thus it did not appear from the record that the trial court was so biased against sex offenders that his sentencing decision amounted to violations of appellant's constitutional rights. The court noted also that the sentence was within the range permitted by statute, and that appellant's offenses were several and bizarre.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. Although the trial court made his distaste for sex offenders clear, the procedures he adhered to in offering appellant the chance to withdraw his pleas were inconsistent with appellant's claim that the trial court was unconstitutionally biased.

Richardson v. State


No. 01-94-00472-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2881



November 23, 1994, Rendered and Delivered  
November 23, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 8, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 174th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 643908.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Harris County (Texas) which convicted him of murder based upon a guilty plea, pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 1.15 (1994), and sentenced him to 60 years' confinement.


OVERVIEW: Indicted for capital murder, appellant pleaded guilty to the lesser-included offense of murder. The trial court convicted appellant under the provisions of Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 1.15 (1994) and sentenced him 60 years' imprisonment. On appeal, appellant contended that art. 1.15 was unconstitutional in that it provided for a bench trial where the trial court could not consider any evidence offered by appellant, and it was therefore a denial of appellant's right to compulsory due process. The court held that nothing in art. 1.15 prohibited appellant from putting on his own evidence or prohibited the trial court from considering that evidence. The court noted that appellant did put on witnesses at the punishment hearing and was not prevented from cross-examining the state's witness. The court also rejected appellant's contention that the trial court committed fundamental error in entering a judgment of guilt because the record was silent as to his waiver of the right to compulsory process. Neither federal nor Texas law required that appellant expressly waive the right to compulsory due process, the court held. Accordingly, the court affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and punishment for murder, because the trial court did not commit fundamental error in entering judgment after accepting appellant's guilty plea.

 

1197 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Vinmar, Inc. v. Harris County Appraisal Dist.


No. 08-93-00294-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


890 S.W.2d 493; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2888



November 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 18, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 157th Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas. (TC# 90-03085). Trial Court Judge: Hon. Michael Schneider.



DISPOSITION: Having overruled all of Appellant's points of error, we affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a take nothing judgment from the 157th Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas, in his action for a property tax refund. Appellant contended that the assessment of property taxes, pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.01(c), on material destined for export violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, and the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Holding that a state tax on goods awaiting foreign export approval in appellant taxpayer's warehouse did not violate U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, or U.S. Const. amend. XIV, the court affirmed the judgment. The court applied a six factor test to determine that the tax did not violate the "dormant" Commerce Clause. The court found a "substantial nexus" between the presence of the property in the warehouse and the state. The tax did not discriminate against interstate commerce. Appellant failed to prove the tax was not fairly apportioned. It was virtually a given that the tax was fairly related to the services provided by the state. Appellant had not demonstrated more than a possibility of a risk of international multiple taxation. Finally, appellant failed to demonstrate how the tax prevented or frustrated the federal government from speaking with "one voice" with respect to regulating commercial relations with foreign governments. The tax also did not violate equal protection. Appellant's challenge was principally fact-based, and he cited no authority finding an equal protection violation based on an erroneous fact determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the take-nothing judgment in this refund action. The court held that the tax violated none of the six factors applicable to the test for determining whether the tax violated the "dormant" Commerce Clause, and found no violation of equal protection.

Nash v. City of Lubbock


No. 07-94-0045-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


888 S.W.2d 557; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2851



November 21, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 237TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 88-523,344; HONORABLE JOHN R. McFALL, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the decision of the 237th District Court of Lubbock County (Texas), which denied appellants' summary judgment motion and granted the summary judgment motion of appellees, a city and its housing standards commission, in appellants' action to recover damages for the demolition of appellants' buildings pursuant to a housing commission order.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, a city and its housing standards commission, caused the demolition of buildings owned by appellant property owners pursuant to an administrative order. After demolition, appellants sued appellees seeking damages, and a trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees. The court affirmed summary judgment against appellants. The court rejected the claim that the city ordinance authorizing the demolition order, which set forth a ten-day period for judicial appeal, violated the enabling act. Rather than apply the enabling act in effect when appellants filed suit, which required a thirty-day appeal period, the court reviewed the ordinance under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1175, § 36 (1979), the enabling act in effect when the demolition order issued that did not specify an appeal period. The court held that a ten-day appeal period did not violate the open court rights in Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. Finally, the court refused to entertain arguments that the demolition order did not comply with the city ordinance and suffered other defects because these arguments constituted impermissible collateral attacks on an order that was not directly appealed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant property owners' summary judgment motion and the grant of the summary judgment motion of appellees, a city and its housing standards commission. A city ordinance authorizing the demolition if the administrative order was not appealed within ten days did not violate the applicable enabling either act or the constitutional right to open courts.

 

1199 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. Employers Casualty Co.


No. 07-94-0060-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


888 S.W.2d 219; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2841



November 17, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 47TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF RANDALL COUNTY; NO. 36,198-A; HONORABLE DAVID L. GLEASON, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, individually and as next friend of her son, a minor, sought review of a take-nothing judgment of the 47th Judicial District of Randall County (Texas) rendered in her action seeking death benefits under the Texas Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Labor Code Ann. § 401.001 et seq. (Pamph. 1994), after her husband's fatal heart attack.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, individually and as next fried of her son, a minor, sought review of a trial court judgment denying her claim for death benefits under the Texas Workers' Compensation Act (the Act), Tex. Labor Code Ann. § 401.001 et seq. (Pamph. 1994), as not compensable. Appellant sought death benefits after her husband's fatal heart attack at work. Appellant contended that § 408.008 of the Act was unconstitutional because it violated her rights to open courts, due process of law, and equal protection. The court refused to pass on the constitutionality of the statute, because it found that appellant sought to avail herself of the benefits of that statute by seeking recovery under it. Appellant also contended that the jury's failure to find that her husband's heart attack was compensable was against the great weight and preponderance of the evidence. The court overruled the contention, holding that the jury's finding was not so against the great weight of the evidence as to be clearly wrong and unjust.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's take-nothing judgment against appellant, individually and as next friend of her son, a minor, in her action seeking death benefits under the state workers' compensation law after her husband's fatal heart attack, holding, inter alia, that the jury's finding was not so against the great weight and preponderance of the evidence as to be clearly wrong and unjust.

 

1200 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


National Ass'n of Indep. Insurers v. Texas Dep't of Ins.


No. 94-181-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


888 S.W.2d 198; 1994 Tex. App. LEXIS 2789



November 16, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled December 21, 1994. Released for Publication December 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 93-11514, HONORABLE JERRY DELLANA, JUDGE PRESIDING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurers challenged the judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District (Texas), which upheld two rules adopted by appellee Texas State Board of Insurance (Board) and defended by appellee Board, the Texas Department of Insurance, and the Office of Public Insurance Counsel.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurers challenged a judgment upholding two rules, 28 Tex. Admin. Code § 21.1000 (Rule 1000) and 28 Tex. Admin. Code § 21.1003 (Rule 1003), which appellee Texas State Board of Insurance (Board) adopted and appellee Board, the Texas Department of Insurance and the Office of Public Insurance Counsel defended. Rule 1000 prohibited insurers from blacklisting customers merely because another insurer previously rejected them, while Rule 1003 prohibited insurers from refusing to sell insurance or denying a preferred rate because the consumer owned only one automobile. The court affirmed on a host of challenges, holding that the Board acted within its statutory authority because the rules were in harmony with the general statutory objective to prevent unfair practices and that the Board was not required to promulgate special criteria for determining whether a given practice was unfair. Further, the rules were not arbitrary and capricious where the Board had legitimate reasons supporting their adoption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed on a host of challenges because appellee Texas State Board of Insurance acted within its statutory authority, and the rules were not arbitrary and capricious where the Texas State Board of Insurance had legitimate reasons for adopting them.
